Prohibition of Selling Booty Before Division in Dar al-Harb
Ruling that selling booty before division in dar al-harb is impermissible.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on selling booty before division, identify the evidence, and explain the exception for the imam.

Core Idea
Booty cannot be sold before division because ownership is not yet transferred.

Booty captured in battle is collective property of the Muslim army until formally divided. Individual fighters do not own any portion until that division occurs. This lesson establishes the prohibition of selling booty before division, supported by the Prophet's hadith, and clarifies the limited authority of the imam to sell if necessary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is selling booty (ghanimah) before formal division in dar al-harb. The ruling is haram (impermissible).
2
Determine the reason for prohibition
Ownership of booty is not transferred to any individual fighter until the imam divides it. Without ownership, a person cannot sell what he does not own.
The text states: 'Since the fighter has not become owner, selling is not permissible.'
3
Note the exception for the imam
If there is a genuine necessity (darurah), the imam may sell booty before division. This is because the imam has authority over collective property.
The text says: 'If necessary, the imam may sell.'
4
Locate the dalil (proof)
The hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri records that the Prophet prohibited buying booty before it is divided. This implies prohibition of selling as well, since both involve transferring ownership.
Hadith in Sunan al-Tirmidhi, chapter on dislike of selling.
5
Apply the implication of the dalil
The prohibition of buying is understood to also forbid selling, because the underlying reason (ownership not yet established) applies equally.
The hadith uses 'buying' but the ruling covers selling by analogy (mafhum al-muwafaqah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۳۰۲۶ (۴۷) ولا يجوز بيع الغنائم قبل القسمة في دار الحرب. (Urdu follows) دار الحرب میں تقسیم سے پہلے غنیمت کو بیچنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ دار الحرب میں مال غنیمت جمع ہو گیا ہو اور ابھی تقسیم نہ کی ہو اس سے پہلے عامی آدمی کے لئے جائز نہیں ہے کہ مال غنیمت کو بیچے۔ البتہ استعمال کی چیز بقد، ضرورت استعمال کر سکتا ہے۔ اسے پہلے مجاہد مالک نہیں ہوا ہے اس لئے اس کے لئے بیچنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ ضرورت پڑے تو امام بیچ سکتا ہے(۲) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابی سعید الخدري قال نهى رسول الله الا الله عن شراء المغانم حتى تقسم (ب) ( ترمذی شریف، باب کراہیتہ بیع) (حاشیہ: (الف) حضور نے مقام جعرانہ سے عمرہ کیا جہاں حسین کی نقیمت تقسیم کی (ب) تقسیم ہونے سے پہلے حضور نے مال غنیمت خریدنے سے روکا۔
3026 (47) And it is not permissible to sell booty before division in dar al-harb. (Urdu): Selling booty before division in dar al-harb is not permissible. If booty has been collected in dar al-harb and not yet divided, it is not permissible for an ordinary person to sell it. However, a needed item can be used by necessity. Since the fighter has not become owner, selling is not permissible. If necessary, the imam may sell. (2) There is a hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: The Messenger of Allah forbade buying booty until it is divided. (Tirmidhi, Chapter on dislike of selling) (Footnote: (a) The Prophet performed Umrah from Ji'ranah where he divided the spoils of Hunayn. (b) The Prophet forbade buying booty before division.)
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This lesson states the ruling that booty (ghanimah) may not be sold in dar al-harb before it is officially divided among the fighters. The reason is that ownership of the booty is not yet established for any individual; it is collectively owned by the Muslim army. Therefore, an individual fighter cannot sell any portion because he does not own it. However, the imam may sell if there is a pressing need, as the imam has authority over the booty. The proof is a hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri that the Prophet prohibited buying booty before division, which implies prohibition of selling as well.

Key Terms
غنيمة (ghanimah): Booty taken from the enemy after a battle.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Who is permitted to sell booty before division in dar al-harb?
A) Any fighter
B) The imam, if necessary
C) No one
D) The original owner of a retrieved item

Key Takeaway
Booty cannot be sold before division in dar al-harb; only the imam may sell if necessary.

Distributing Spoils as Trust When No Transport
Ruling on temporary transfer of spoils for transport to Dar al-Islam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for handling spoils when transport is unavailable and identify the hadith evidence used to support it.

Core Idea
Spoils must be divided in Dar al-Islam; only as trust may mujahideen carry them when no transport exists.

In the chaos of war, transporting spoils back to Islamic territory can be a logistical challenge. The Hanafi school provides a practical solution: if the imam lacks sufficient transport animals, he may give the spoils to the mujahideen as a trust (wadi'ah) so they can carry them on their own animals. This temporary transfer does not confer ownership until the final division in Dar al-Islam. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its proof from the Prophet's practice at Hunayn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The imam does not have enough transport animals (himūlah) to carry all the spoils from Dar al-Harb to Dar al-Islam.
This is a logistical problem, not a change in the fundamental rule.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The imam distributes the spoils among the mujahideen as a trust (qismat idā‘), not as ownership, so they can transport them.
Temporary measure; ownership is not transferred.
3
Understand the procedure after transport
Once the spoils reach Dar al-Islam, the imam collects all the property and divides it properly, making each mujahid the owner of his share.
This is the required final division in Dar al-Islam.
4
Analyze the hadith evidence
The Prophet ﷺ divided the spoils of Hunayn at Ji'ranah, which is in the vicinity of Makkah (Dar al-Islam). The mujahideen must have brought the spoils there, indicating that they acted as carriers.
The hadith is from Bukhari, showing that final division occurs after the spoils are brought to safe territory.
5
Compare with Shafi'i view
Imam Shafi'i holds that spoils become owned immediately after battle, so division can occur in Dar al-Harb. The Hanafi position emphasizes the need for Ihraz (securing) in Dar al-Islam before final division.
This is a legitimate scholarly difference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا لم يكن للامام حمولة يحمل عليها الغنائم قسمها بين الغانمين قسمة ايداع ليحملوها الى دار الاسلام ثم يرجعها منهم فيقسمها۔ امام کے پاس اتنے جانور نہیں ہیں کہ ان پر سارا مال غنیمت لاد کر دار الاسلام لا سکے۔ ایسی صورت میں مال غنیمت امانت کے طور پر تھوڑا تھوڑا کر کے مجاہدین کو دیدے تا کہ وہ اپنے جانوروں پر لاد کر دار الاسلام تک لائے ۔ جب دار الاسلام لے آئے تو امام سب مال کو جمع کرے اور ہر مجاہد کو اس کے حصے کے مطابق تقسیم کر کے دے اور مالک بنادے۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک غنیمت دار الاسلام میں تقسیم کرنا ہے۔ اور دار الاسلام تک لانے کے لئے جانور میسر نہیں ہے تو یہی صورت ہو سکتی ہے کہ مجاہدین کو تھوڑا تھوڑا کر کے لانے کے لئے کہے (۲) حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور نے حسنین کی نعیمت جعرانہ میں تقسیم کی تو جعرانہ تک مجاہدین ہی، ال غنیمت لائے ہوں گے ۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ مجاہدین کو مال غنیمت لانے کے لئے دے۔ حدیث یہ ہے۔ ان انسا اخبـره قـال اعتمر النبي الله من الجعرانة حيث قسم غنائم حنين (الف) ( بخاری شریف ، باب من قسم الغنيمة في غزوه و سفره ، ص ۱۴۳۱، نمبر ۳۰۶۶) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جنگ حنین کی غنیمت جعرانہ میں تقسیم کی۔
If the imam does not have transport to carry the spoils, he distributes them among the gainers (mujahideen) as a trust (wadi'ah) so that they may carry them to the abode of Islam, then he takes them back from them and divides them. Comment: The imam does not have enough animals to load all the spoils and bring to Dar al-Islam. In such a case, he gives the spoils little by little to the mujahideen as a trust so that they load them on their animals and bring to Dar al-Islam. When they bring them to Dar al-Islam, the imam collects all the property and divides it among each mujahid according to his share and makes him owner. According to Imam Abu Hanifah, the spoils are to be divided in Dar al-Islam. And if animals are not available to bring them to Dar al-Islam, then this is the only possible course: that he tells the mujahideen to bring them little by little. (2) In a hadith, the Prophet divided the spoils of Hunayn at Ji'ranah, and the mujahideen must have brought the spoils to Ji'ranah. This indicates that the mujahideen are given the spoils to bring. The hadith is: Anas informed him, he said: The Prophet performed Umrah from Ji'ranah where he divided the spoils of Hunayn. (Bukhari, Bab man qasama al-ghanimah fi ghazwih wa safarih, p. 1431, no. 3066). This hadith states that the spoils of the battle of Hunayn were divided at Ji'ranah.
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage deals with a practical situation in the distribution of war spoils (ghanimah). The ruling is from the Hanafi school. If the imam (commander) does not have enough animals to transport the spoils to Dar al-Islam, he gives the spoils to the mujahideen as a trust (wadi'ah) — not as ownership — so they can carry them on their own animals. Once the spoils reach Dar al-Islam, the imam collects everything and divides it properly among the fighters. The author supports this with the precedent of the Prophet ﷺ dividing the spoils of Hunayn at Ji'ranah, implying that the mujahideen themselves brought the spoils there. This shows that the Hanafi position requires the spoils to be brought to Dar al-Islam before division, and the imam may use the mujahideen for transport when needed.

Key Terms
حمولة (himūlah): Transport animals such as camels or horses used to carry spoils.
قسمة ايداع (qismat idā‘): Distribution as a trust (wadi'ah), not as ownership, for the purpose of transport.
غنائم (ghanā’im): Spoils of war taken from the enemy by force.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when the imam lacks transport, he gives the spoils to the mujahideen as:
A) A gift to reward their efforts.
B) A trust (wadi'ah) to carry to Dar al-Islam.
C) A loan to be returned after the campaign.
D) An advance payment of their share.

Key Takeaway
Spoils must be divided in Dar al-Islam; if no transport, the imam may give them as trust to mujahideen to carry, but final division and ownership transfer occur only after they reach Dar al-Islam.

Prohibition of Selling Spoils Before Division
Ruling on the impermissibility of selling spoils before division.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling spoils before division and explain the dalil from the hadith.

Core Idea
Spoils are not owned until divided; selling without ownership is prohibited.

This lesson addresses a key fiqh of jihad: the prohibition of selling spoils before the official division by the imam. The underlying principle is that ownership (milk) of spoils does not transfer to the mujahideen until the division (qismah) is completed. The Hanafi school relies on a clear hadith to establish this ruling, while also allowing limited use out of necessity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is selling (bay‘) spoils (ghanaim) in Dar al-Harb before division. The ruling is haram (impermissible).
The prohibition is specific to the mujahid who has not yet received his share.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: the Prophet forbade buying spoils until they are divided.
The hadith is narrated in Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud, and others.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit prohibition (nahy) indicates that the transaction is invalid. The phrase 'until they are divided' shows that ownership is conditional on division.
In Hanafi usul, a prohibition (nahy) generally indicates tahrim (impermissibility) unless there is a counter-indication.
4
Note exceptions
The imam may sell spoils before division if necessary, and a mujahid may use an item of necessity without selling.
Use is permissible because it does not transfer ownership; it is a form of temporary benefit.
5
Understand the principle
The underlying legal cause (illah) is the lack of ownership. Until division, the spoils are owned collectively by the state (or the community) and are not individually owned by any mujahid.
This principle prevents transactions (buy/sell) that require ownership.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يجوز بيع الغنائم قبل القسمة في دار الحرب۔ دار الحرب میں مال غنیمت جمع ہو گیا ہو اور ابھی تقسیم نہ کی ہو اس سے پہلے عامی آدمی کے لئے جائز نہیں ہے کہ مال غنیمت کو بیچے۔ البتہ استعمال کی چیز بقد، ضرورت استعمال کر سکتا ہے۔ اسے پہلے مجاہد مالک نہیں ہوا ہے اس لئے اس کے لئے بیچنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ ضرورت پڑے تو امام بیچ سکتا ہے(۲) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابی سعید الخدري قال نهى رسول الله الا الله عن شراء المغانم حتى تقسم (ب) ( ترمذی شریف، باب کراہیتہ بیع المغانم حتی تقسم ص ۲۸۵ نمبر ۱۵۶۳ ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی وطاء السبايا ص ۳۰۰ نمبر ۲۱۵۸، کتاب النکاح رسن للمتقی ، باب بیج السمی و غیره فی دار الحرب، ج تاسع ص ۲۱۱ نمبر ۱۸۳۰۳) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ تقسیم سے پہلے غنیمت کا بیچنا مجاہد کے لئے جائز نہیں ہے۔
And it is not permissible to sell the spoils before division in the abode of war. In Dar al-Harb, if the spoils have been collected but not yet divided, it is not permissible for an ordinary person to sell them. However, he may use an item of necessity as needed. The mujahid has not yet become owner, so selling is impermissible for him. If necessary, the imam may sell. (2) A hadith: From Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, he said: The Messenger of Allah forbade buying spoils until they are divided. (Tirmidhi, Bab Karahiyat Bay' al-Maghanim hatta tuqsam, p. 285, no. 1563; Abu Dawud, Bab fi Wata' al-Sabaya, p. 300, no. 2158; etc.) This hadith indicates that selling spoils before division is not permissible for a mujahid.
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage presents a clear Hanafi ruling: spoils of war cannot be sold by individuals in Dar al-Harb before the official division (qismah) by the imam. The reasoning is that the mujahideen do not yet own the spoils; ownership only transfers after division in Dar al-Islam. However, the imam may sell if necessary, e.g., to cover urgent needs. The author supports this with a hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri where the Prophet forbade buying spoils before division. This prohibition applies to both buying and selling, as the transaction is invalid due to lack of ownership.

Key Terms
بيع (bay‘): Sale transaction; here, selling spoils before official division.
قسمة (qismah): Official division of spoils by the imam, transferring ownership to mujahideen.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, who may sell spoils before division if necessary?
A) Any mujahid
B) The imam
C) No one
D) The market

Key Takeaway
Spoils cannot be sold by individuals before official division because ownership is not established; only the imam may sell if necessary.

Timing of Ihrāz and Entitlement to Spoils
Rulings on entitlement to spoils when a mujāhid dies before or after spoils reach Dār al-Islām

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for a mujahid's entitlement to spoils and explain the practical difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on the timing of ihrāz.

Core Idea
A mujahid's share in spoils only vests after the spoils reach Dār al-Islām; death before that forfeits the share.

This passage from al-Sharḥ al-Samarqandī clarifies when a mujāhid's right to spoils takes effect. The key is the concept of iḥrāz (securing). In the Ḥanafī school, ownership is established only when the spoils physically arrive in Dār al-Islām. The Shāfi‘ī school, however, places iḥrāz at the end of the battle, leading to different inheritance outcomes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
The text describes three temporal points: (a) death during battle, (b) death after battle but before spoils reach Dār al-Islām, (c) death after spoils reach Dār al-Islām.
The first and second scenarios are considered together in the Ḥanafī position.
2
Apply the Ḥanafī principle of milk (ownership)
For Imām Abū Ḥanīfah, ownership of spoils is established only after iḥrāz in Dār al-Islām. Therefore, death before that point means no right to a share.
This is the core of the Ḥanafī argument.
3
Contrast the Shāfi‘ī position
Imām al-Shāfi‘ī holds that iḥrāz occurs immediately after the battle ends, so ownership vests then. Death after battle does not extinguish the right.
The disagreement is over the moment of iḥrāz.
4
Derive the thamarah al-khilāf
The practical consequence is inheritance: under Ḥanafī law, heirs of a mujāhid who dies after battle but before Dār al-Islām get nothing; under Shāfi‘ī law, they inherit his share.
This difference affects real cases of war spoils distribution.
5
Confirm the muftā bihī
The Ḥanafī position is the relied-upon view in this text, and the passage concludes by stating that if death occurs after spoils reach Dār al-Islām, the share goes to heirs.
The muftā bihī is the Ḥanafī ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن مات من الغانمين في دار الحرب فلا حق له في القسمة۔ اگر جنگ کے درمیان کوئی شہید ہو گیا تو ان کو بالاتفاق حصہ نہیں ملے گا۔ اور اگر جنگ ختم ہونے کے بعد لیکن غنیمت کو دارالاسلام لانے سے پہلے کوئی انتقال کر گیا تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اس کو بھی غنیمت میں حصہ نہیں ملے گا۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کا مسلک یہ ہے کہ دارالاسلام میں احراز کے بعد مجاہد نقیمت کا مالک ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے اس سے پہلے جو انتقال کر جائے اس کو مال غنیمت میں حصہ نہیں ملے گا۔ جس طرح جنگ کے دوران کوئی شہید ہو جائے اس کو حصہ نہیں ملتا ہے۔ اصول یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ دارالاسلام میں مال جمع ہونے کے بعد مجاہد کا حق ہوتا ہے۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ جنگ ختم ہونے کے بعد جو مجاہد انتقال ہوئے ہیں ان کو بھی غنیمت میں حصہ ملے گا چاہے وہ دارالحرب میں ہی کیوں نہ ہو۔ اور دار الاسلام میں مال لانے سے پہلے کیوں نہ ہو۔ ان کا قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ جنگ ختم ہو جانے کے بعد مجاہدین غنیمت کے مالک ہو جاتے ہیں۔ ان کے یہاں جنگ ختم ہوتے ہی احراز ہو جاتا ہـے۔ ومن مات من الغانمين بعد اخراجها الى دار الاسلام فنصيبه لورثته۔ دار الاسلام میں مال غنیمت جمع کیا اس کے بعد کسی مجاہد کا انتقال ہوا تو اس کو غنیمت میں حصہ ملے گا۔ اور یہ حصہ اس کے ورثہ کو دے دیا جائے گا۔
And whoever dies among the gainers (mujahideen) in the abode of war has no share in the division. If someone is martyred during the battle, by consensus he receives no share. And if someone dies after the battle ends but before the spoils are brought to Dar al-Islam, according to Imam Abu Hanifah he also receives no share in the spoils. The school of Imam Abu Hanifah is that the mujahid becomes owner of the spoils only after ihraz (securing) in Dar al-Islam. Therefore, whoever dies before that does not get a share, just as one martyred during battle does not get a share. The principle is that the mujahid's right accrues only after the property is collected in Dar al-Islam. Imam Shafi'i says that those mujahideen who die after the battle ends also get a share in the spoils, even if they are in Dar al-Harb and before the spoils are brought to Dar al-Islam. Their rule is that the mujahideen become owners of the spoils as soon as the battle ends; in their view, ihraz occurs immediately upon the end of battle. And whoever dies among the gainers after the spoils have been taken out to Dar al-Islam, his share goes to his heirs. When the spoils have been collected in Dar al-Islam, then if a mujahid dies, he receives a share in the spoils, and that share is given to his heirs.
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage covers two rulings and a dispute. The first ruling: if a mujahid dies in Dar al-Harb, whether during battle or after battle but before spoils reach Dar al-Islam, he has no share. This is the Hanafi position, based on the principle that ownership of spoils is established only after ihraz (securing) in Dar al-Islam. The second ruling: if a mujahid dies after the spoils have been brought to Dar al-Islam, his share goes to his heirs. The author then contrasts the Shafi'i view: they consider that ownership vests immediately after the battle, so even if a mujahid dies in Dar al-Harb after battle, his heirs inherit his share. The practical thamarah (result) of this difference is in inheritance: under Hanafi law, if a mujahid dies in Dar al-Harb after battle but before Dar al-Islam, his family gets nothing; under Shafi'i, they do.

Key Terms
احراز (iḥrāz): Securing of spoils by bringing them to a safe place (Dār al-Islām), which triggers ownership.
نصيب (naṣīb): Share of a mujāhid in the spoils.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Permissibility of Encouraging with Rewards During Battle
Ruling on imam giving extra rewards (nafl) to motivate fighters during battle

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the imam offering extra rewards (nafl) during battle and explain its permissibility.

Core Idea
The imam may offer extra rewards to motivate fighters during battle; it is permissible (mubah).

In the context of jihad, leaders often need to boost the morale of fighters. Islamic law provides the imam with the discretion to grant additional incentives, known as nafl, beyond the regular share of spoils. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on this practice, which is straightforwardly permissible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The act is the imam granting an extra reward (nafl) to fighters during active battle, such as promising the belongings of a slain enemy to the killer.
This is separate from the regular distribution of ghanimah.
2
State the ruling
The Hanafi ruling is that it is mubah (permissible), indicated by the phrase 'la ba'sa' (no harm).
3
Understand the context
The permissibility applies specifically during the battle, not before or after. The imam uses it as a motivational tactic.
4
Distinguish from regular spoils
Nafl is an additional grant from the imam's discretion, whereas ghanimah shares are fixed by Shariah. Both are legitimate.
5
Note the purpose
The purpose is to encourage bravery and enthusiasm in combat, which is a recognized public interest (maslahah).

Ruling on Promising Salb and Nafal to a Detachment
States the ruling on salb and nafal promised by the imam before battle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on promising salb and nafal, and identify the hadith proofs that permit them.

Core Idea
The imam may promise a killer his salb and grant a detachment extra spoils — both are permissible based on prophetic practice.

This lesson examines the permissibility of the imam (leader) promising additional rewards to fighters before battle to motivate them. The passage covers two specific incentives: promising the salb (the slain enemy's belongings) to the killer, and promising a quarter of the spoils (after khums) to a detachment. We will explore the proofs from the Quran and Sunnah that establish these rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Rulings
The passage presents two separate permissions: (1) The imam may promise a killer his salb; (2) The imam may promise a detachment a portion (e.g., quarter) from the spoils after khums.
These are additional incentives beyond the standard share in ghanima.
2
Locate the Primary Proof for Each
For salb: the hadith of Abu Qatada (transmitted by Bukhari, Muslim, etc.) states that whoever kills an enemy with evidence gets his salb. For nafal: the hadith of Habib ibn Maslama shows the Prophet gave a quarter after khums.
Quran 8:65 is also cited as general encouragement to fight.
3
Understand the Wajh al-Dalalah (Indication)
The hadiths use declarative statements ('فله سلبه') and actions ('كان ينفل') which indicate permissibility. The imperative in the Quran (حرض) supports encouragement but not obligation.
The Hanafi position is that these are mubah (permissible) for the imam.
4
Note the Hanafi Position and Cross-Madhhab Difference
Hanafis allow nafal from the spoils after khums, while some other schools restrict it to the khums portion. This distinction affects how extra rewards are calculated.
The Hanafi view is based on the practice of the Prophet and his companions.
5
Apply the Ruling to a Scenario
Given a detachment returning with spoils, calculate the nafal share: first take khums, then the promised fraction (e.g., quarter) of the remainder, then distribute the rest as regular ghanima.
The example in the text uses 20 camels: khums=4, remaining=16, quarter=4 nafal, 12 distributed.

So his salb is for him. Or he says to the detachment: I have assigned to you the quarter after the khums. The equipment will be for him. There is encouragement in the verse: O Prophet, urge the believers to fight. (Surah al-Anfal 8:65). And in the hadith: On the occasion of Badr, the Prophet urged by saying whoever kills someone, his equipment is for him. The hadith: from Abu Qatada, he said the Messenger of Allah said: whoever kills an enemy and has evidence for it, then his salb is for him. This hadith shows that promising additional reward is permissible. And (51) Or he says to the detachment: I have assigned to you a quarter after the khums. The commentary: The imam says to the detachment going to battle: from the spoils you bring, after taking the khums, a quarter of the remainder will be given to you as nafal, then distributed as ghanima. Example: 20 camels, khums takes 4, remaining 16, quarter of that is 4 nafal, remaining 12 distributed. Proof: hadith of Habib ibn Salama that the Prophet used to give a quarter after khums and a third after khums when returning. So the imam can announce nafal based on circumstance.
Source pages p. 283

Commentary
This passage presents two related rulings on nafal (additional spoils) granted by the imam before battle to motivate the fighters. The first ruling concerns the salb (personal belongings of a slain enemy). If the imam declares that the killer gets the salb, then it becomes his exclusive property. The proof is the hadith of Abu Qatada (may Allah be pleased with him) that the Prophet ﷺ said: 'Whoever kills an enemy and has evidence (a witness), then his salb is for him.' This is supported by the Quranic command to urge the believers to fight (Quran 8:65). The second ruling allows the imam to promise a detachment (sariyya) a specific share of the spoils, such as one quarter after the khums is taken. The example given illustrates the calculation: from 20 camels, 4 are taken as khums; from the remaining 16, one quarter (4) is given as nafal to the detachment; the remaining 12 camels are distributed to the entire army as regular ghanima. The proof is from the hadith of Habib ibn Maslama that the Prophet ﷺ would give a quarter after khums on the outward journey and a third after khums on the return. This shows that the imam has discretion to announce nafal according to circumstances.

Key Terms
سلب (salab): The weapons, armor, and personal belongings of a slain enemy taken by the killer.
نفل (nafal): Additional spoils granted by the imam to encourage fighters beyond their regular share in ghanima.
خمس (khums): One-fifth of the booty (ghanima) set aside for Allah and His Messenger, and distributed to specified categories.
سرية (sariyya): A small detachment sent from the main army for a specific military mission.

6 min
No Nafal After Acquisition of Ghanima Except from Khums
States the prohibition of granting nafal after ihraz except from khums

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on nafal after ihraz and explain the evidence from the Prophet's practice.

Core Idea
Once ghanima is secured, nafal is only from khums — the imam cannot reward from the common pool.

Nafal (extra reward) is a tool to incentivize fighters, but it has temporal limits. Before the spoils are collected, the imam may promise nafal from the ghanima itself. However, once the spoils are secured and rights attach, granting nafal from the entire ghanima would violate the rights of all participants. This lesson explains the Hanafi position that after ihraz, nafal can only come from the khums (one-fifth) portion, and the proof from the Prophet's sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What act is being ruled upon? Granting nafal after the spoils have been acquired (ihraz). What is the ruling? It is not permissible (ja'iz nahin) except from the khums.
The ruling is a prohibition on using the entire ghanima for nafal after ihraz.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The author footnotes a hadith: 'He used to give a quarter after the khums and one third after the khums when returning.' This shows the Prophet's practice of granting nafal only from the khums portion.
The hadith is from Sunan Abi Dawud and al-Tirmidhi; it is ahad (single-chain) in transmission.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (legal inference)
The hadith indicates that the Prophet gave nafal from what remained after khums, implying that nafal was not taken from the entire ghanima but from a specific portion. Since the Prophet did not give nafal from the common pool after acquisition, it establishes the prohibition.
The Hanafi usul principle: the Prophet's action (fi'l) in this context indicates a ruling of prohibition or permissibility depending on context.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (scholarly disagreement)
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) permit nafal from the entire ghanima even after acquisition, based on general verses about nafal or other ahadith. The Hanafis restrict to khums based on this specific practice.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; both views have evidence.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Under the Hanafi view, after ihraz, an imam cannot promise or give extra reward from the main spoils; any nafal must come from the khums. Under the other view, he can give from the entire ghanima, potentially reducing shares for others.
The difference affects how commanders distribute captured assets.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۳۰۳۱] (۵۲) ولا يُنفل بعد احراز الغنيمة الا من الخمس. جنگ ختم ہوگئی۔ لوگوں نے مال غنیمت بھی جمع کر لیا۔ اب اس میں سے کسی کو انعام دینا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور اگر دینا ہی ہے تو پورے مال غنیمت میں سے پانچواں حصہ خمس نکالا ہے اس میں سے انعام دے۔ حاشیہ : (الف) اے نبی مومنین کو قتال کی ترغیب دیجئے (ب) آپ نے فرمایا کسی نے کفار کو قتل کیا اور اس پر گواہ ہو تو اس کا سامان قتل کرنے والے کے لئے ہے (ج) آپ خمس نکالنے کے بعد چوتھائی نفل دیتے تھے اور جب واپس لوٹنے کا موقع ہوتا تو خمس کے بعد تہائی نفل دیتے۔
And no nafal is given after the acquisition of the ghanima except from the khums. The war is over. The people have collected the spoils. Now it is not permissible to give anyone a reward from it. And if one must give, then from the one-fifth (khums) that has been taken out of the entire ghanima, give reward from it. Footnotes: (a) O Prophet, urge the believers to fight. (b) He said: Whoever killed a disbeliever and has a witness, then his equipment is for the killer. (c) He used to give a quarter after the khums and one third after the khums when returning.
Source pages p. 283

Commentary
This ruling establishes a key temporal distinction in the law of nafal. Before the spoils are acquired and secured (ihraz), the imam may promise nafal from the ghanima itself. However, after the spoils have been collected and are in the possession of the Muslim army, no additional nafal can be granted from the entire ghanima. Instead, if the imam wishes to give extra reward, it must come exclusively from the khums (one-fifth) portion. The reason is that once the ghanima is acquired, the rights of all participants become attached to it, and it would be unjust to single out some for extra reward from the common pool. The footnote (c) refers to the practice of the Prophet ﷺ who would grant nafal from the khums portion before returning from expeditions.

Key Terms
نفل (nafal): Extra reward or bonus given to fighters beyond their regular share of spoils.
غنيمة (ghanima): Spoils of war taken from the enemy through combat.
خمس (khums): One-fifth share of ghanima that belongs to the state and is used for public welfare, including nafal.
احراز (ihraz): The act of taking possession and securing the spoils of war in the Muslim army's control.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Salb Not Assigned to Killer Becomes Part of Ghanima
States the ruling when the imam does not assign the salb to the killer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on salb when the imam does not declare it for the killer and explain the proof from the hadith of Hunayn.

Core Idea
Without the imam's explicit announcement, the salb belongs to the general ghanima, not exclusively to the killer.

This lesson addresses a common misconception: that the warrior automatically gets the belongings of the enemy he kills. The Hanafi school, based on the practice of the Prophet ﷺ at the Battle of Hunayn, requires an official declaration and evidence (witness) for the salb to become the killer's exclusive property. If no such declaration is made, the salb is treated as part of the general ghanima and distributed equally among all fighters. We will examine the ruling and its proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
Recognize that the act in question is the imam's decision regarding the salb (the weapons, armor, and personal belongings of a slain enemy). The default ruling is that if the imam does not declare the salb for the killer, it goes into the general ghanima and is shared equally among all fighters, including the killer.
The default is the opposite of what many assume.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith of Abu Qatada from the Battle of Hunayn, where the Prophet ﷺ said: 'Whoever kills an enemy and has evidence, his salb is for him.' The Prophet repeated this three times before anyone came forward. This shows that the salb is not automatically given; it requires an explicit declaration and evidence.
The hadith is ahad but accepted in fiqh.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The condition 'man qatala qatilan lahu alayhi bayyinah' implies that without a witness (bayyinah) and presumably without the imam's prior announcement, the salb is not exclusive. The Hanafi usul principle that a conditional phrase restricts the ruling to the condition confirms that the default is inclusion in ghanima.
The condition indicates that the salb is not automatically the killer's.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) hold that the salb is automatically the killer's property based on a different understanding of the same hadith or other narrations. The Hanafi school disagrees and bases its position on the need for an explicit declaration.
The difference stems from how the conditional clause is interpreted.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is supported by the incident of Hunayn where the Prophet made the announcement three times and required a witness. Additionally, the practice of the Companions (e.g., Anas ibn Malik refusing a captive before distribution) reinforces that extra reward must come from the khums, not the general ghanima. Thus, the mufta bihi is that salb is part of ghanima unless the imam declares otherwise.
The footnotes provide supporting evidence from the Companions' practice.

[۳۰۳۲] (۵۳) واذا لم يجعل السلب للقاتل فهو من جملة الغنيمة والقاتل وغيره فيه. اگر امام نے مزید انعام دینے کا اعلان کیا تب تو مقتول کا سازو سامان قاتل کے لئے ہوگا ۔ اور اگر یہ اعلان نہیں کیا تو مقتول کا ساز و سامان قاتل کے لئے نہیں ہوگا۔ اس کو مال غنیمت میں شامل کر دیا جائے گا۔ اور اس سامان میں قاتل اور غیر قاتل سب کا حصہ برابر ہوگا۔ جنگ حنین کے واقعہ سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ با ضابطہ امام انعام کا اعلان کرے اور قاتل قتل کرنے پر گواہ پیش کرے تب اس کو سلب اور انعام دیا جائے گا ورنہ نہیں۔ حدیث کا ٹکڑا یہ ہے۔ عن ابی قتادة قال خرجنا مع رسول الله الله الله عام حنين ... وجلس النبي الله فقال من قتل قتيلا له عليه بينة فله سلبه فقمت فقلت من يشهد لي؟ ثم جلست ثم قال من قتل قتيلا له عليه بينة فله حاشیه : (الف) عمر بن عبسہ فرماتے ہیں کہ ہم کو حضور نے مال غنیمت کے اونٹ کی طرف نماز پڑھائی۔ جب سلام پھیرا تو اونٹ کے پہلو سے بال پکڑا پھر فرمایا تمہاری غنیمت میں سے میرے لئے اتنا بھی حلال نہیں ہے سوائے خمس کے۔ اور خمس بھی تمہارے اوپر واپس کیا جاتا ہے (ب) انس بن مالک عبید اللہ بن بکرۃ کے ساتھ کسی غزوہ میں تھے ۔ انہوں نے قیدی پایا۔ عبید اللہ نے حضرت انس کو کچھ قیدی تقسیم سے پہلے دینا چاہا تو حضرت انس نے فرمایا نہیں۔ لیکن تقسیم کرو پھر خمس میں سے دو۔ تو عبید اللہ نے کہا نہیں۔ لیکن تمام مال سے تو حضرت انس نے اس کو قبول کرنے سے انکار کیا۔ اور عبید اللہ خمس میں سے کچھ دینا نہیں چاہتے تھے۔
And if the salb is not made for the killer, then it is part of the ghanima, and the killer and others share equally in it. If the imam has made the announcement of additional reward, then the equipment of the slain is for the killer. And if he did not make this announcement, then the equipment is not for the killer. It will be included in the ghanima, and in that equipment, the killer and non-killer all have equal share. The incident of Hunayn shows that when the imam makes a formal announcement and the killer provides a witness, then the salb and reward are given; otherwise not. A portion of the hadith: from Abu Qatada, he said: We went out with the Messenger of Allah in the year of Hunayn... The Prophet sat and said: Whoever kills an enemy and has evidence, his salb is for him. So I stood and said: Who will witness for me? Then I sat down. Then he said: Whoever kills an enemy and has evidence, his salb is for him. Footnotes: (a) Amr ibn Abasa said: The Prophet led us in prayer facing a camel from the ghanima, then after salam took a hair from the camel's side and said: Nothing of your ghanima is lawful for me except the khums, and the khums is returned to you. (b) Anas ibn Malik was with Ubaidullah ibn Abi Bakra on an expedition; they took captives. Ubaidullah wanted to give Anas some captives before distribution, but Anas refused and said: Distribute first, then give me from the khums. Ubaidullah refused to give from the khums, so Anas refused to accept anything.
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This lesson clarifies the default ruling on salb (the personal belongings of a slain enemy). The salb only becomes the exclusive property of the killer if the imam has explicitly declared before the battle that the slayer will get the salb. If no such declaration is made, the salb is treated as part of the general ghanima (spoils) and is distributed equally among all fighters, including the killer himself. The commentary draws on the incident of Hunayn where the Prophet ﷺ made the declaration three times before anyone claimed the salb, emphasizing the need for an explicit imam announcement and evidence (witness). The footnotes provide additional support: (a) shows that the Prophet did not take anything from ghanima except khums, and (b) shows the practice of the Companions that any extra reward should come from khums, not the general ghanima.

Key Terms
سلب (salab): The weapons, armor, and personal belongings of a slain enemy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens to the salb (belongings of a slain enemy) if the imam did not declare before the battle that it belongs to the killer?
A) The killer still gets it exclusively
B) It is given to the killer's family
C) It becomes part of the general ghanima and is shared equally among all fighters
D) It is destroyed

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the salb of a slain enemy becomes part of the general ghanima unless the imam has explicitly declared it for the killer before the battle.

Prohibition of Using Spoils After Leaving Dar al-Harb
Ruling with proof from hadith and athar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on leftover spoils upon leaving dar al-harb and identify the hadith and athar proofs establishing collective property of the mujahideen.

Core Idea
Upon leaving dar al-harb, spoils become collective property of all mujahideen; individual use before division is haram.

In this passage from Al-Sharh al-Thamiri, we encounter a specific ruling from the Book of Siyar: after Muslims exit enemy territory, any spoils in their possession—whether food or fodder—must be returned to the general pool. This rule underscores the principle that ghanimah is not private property until officially divided. The commentary reinforces the ruling with the prophetic practice at Khaybar and the Companions' understanding, providing a clear legal proof for the prohibition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is using spoils (food or fodder) after leaving dar al-harb. The ruling is prohibition (haram).
2
Locate the primary proof
The hadith of Mu'adh at Khaybar: the Prophet divided only a portion of the spoils and kept the rest in the general spoils. This shows that after the battle, all spoils must be pooled.
Hadith from Abu Dawud, no. 2707.
3
Understand the legal link (wajh al-dalalah)
The Prophet's action indicates that after leaving the battlefield, individual possession before division is not allowed; the spoils are collective property.
4
Note the supporting athar
Ibn Abbas allowed eating from spoils only until reaching dar al-Islam, implying that upon arrival, remaining food must be returned.
Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 33337.
5
Apply the rationale
The prohibition ensures complete division among all mujahideen, preserving their rights to the collective property.
If each person kept leftover food, full distribution would be impossible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشرح الثميرى الجزء الرابع
۲۷۹
كتاب السير
۳۰۳۴ (۵۵) واذا خرج المسلمون من دار الحرب لم يجز ان يعلقوا من الغنيمة و لا يأكلوا منها شيئا ومن فضل معه علف او طعام ردّه الى الغنيمة.
ثانی ، ص ۱۲۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ گھوڑا، زمین، لگام، پٹکا اور ہتھیار وغیرہ سب سلب میں داخل ہیں۔ البتہ نقدی ،سونا، چاندی مقتول کے پاس ہو تو وہ سلب میں داخل نہیں ہیں۔ اس کی دلیل حضرت عمرؓ کے اثر کا یہ ٹکڑا ہے۔ فکتب الى عمر ان دع الناس يأكلون ويعلفون فمن باع شيئا بذهب او فضة فقد وجب فيه خمس الله وسهام المسلمين (الف) (مصنف ابن ابی هیة ۱۲۷، في الطعام والعلف يوخذ منه الشى فى ارض العدو، ج سادس، ص ۵۰۸ ، نمبر ۳۳۳۱۹) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ سونے چاندی میں سب مجاہدین کا حق ہے۔ ۱۳۰۳۴ (۵۵) اگر مسلمان دار الحرب سے نکلے تو نہیں جائز ہے کہ چارہ کھلائیں مال غنیمت سے اور نہ اس میں خود کھا ئیں۔ اور جو اس کے ساتھ چارہ یا کھانا بچ جائے اس کو غنیمت میں واپس کر دے۔
جب تک دار الحرب میں رہا مال غنیمت کا کھانا وغیرہ استعمال کر سکتا تھا۔ لیکن جب دار الحرب سے باہر چلے گئے تو اب اس میں سے استعمال نہیں کر سکتے ۔ اب جو باقی بچا ہے اس کو بھی مال غنیمت میں شامل کرے اور امام کے تقسیم کرنے کے بعد اپنے اپنے حصے میں کھائے اور چارہ کھلائے۔
دار الحرب سے نکلنے کے بعد یہ مال سب مجاہدین کا ہو گیا اس لئے مجاہدین میں تقسیم کر کے اپنا اپنا حصہ استعمال کرے (۲) دارالحرب سے باہر جانے کے بعد غنیمت کو مجاہدین میں تقسیم کرنا ضروری ہے اس لئے اگر ہر ایک کے پاس کھانے پینے کی چیز رہ جائے گی تو مکمل طور پر تقسیم نہیں ہو سکے گی۔ اس لئے ان چیزوں کو غنیمت میں شامل کرنا ضروری ہے (۳) فقال معاذ غزونا مع رسول الله الله خيبر فاصبنا فيها غنما فقسم فينا رسول الله الا الله طائفة وجعل بقيتها فى المغنم (ب) (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب فی بیع الطعام اذ افضل عن الناس في ارض العدو، ص ۱۳، نمبر ۲۷۰۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ضرورت کے مطابق ہی استعمال کرے اور باقی مال غنیمت میں شامل کرے (۴) اثر میں ہے۔ ان عبد الله بن عباس لم ير بأسا ان يأكل الرجل طعاما في ارض الشرك حتى يدخل اهله (ج) (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ، ۲۹ امن قال يا كلون من الطعام ولا تحملون ومن رخص فیه ، ج سادس ،ص ۵۰۹، نمبر ۳۳۳۳۷) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ اہل یعنی دار الاسلام تک کھا سکتا ہے اس کے بعد واپس جمع کر دے۔
حاشیہ : (پچھلے صفحہ سے آگے ) حضرت خالد کے پاس آئے ۔ سب سونے اور جو ہر سے مرصع تھے تو خالد نے اس میں کچھ لیا اور باقی نفل دے دی۔ میں نے پوچھا اے خالد ! یہ کیا ہے؟ کیا تمہیں معلوم نہیں کہ حضور نے قاتل کو سب سامان دیا۔ خالد نے فرمایا ہاں! لیکن یہ بہت زیادہ تھا اس لئے کچھ لے لیا (الف) حضرت عمر نے مجھ کو لکھا کہ لوگوں کو کھانے دو اور چارہ مال غنیمت میں کھلانے دو۔ ہاں! کچھ سونا یا چاندی کے بدلے بیچے تو اس میں سے شمس واجب ہے اور مسلمانوں کا حصہ ہے۔ (ب) حضرت معادؓ فرماتے ہیں کہ ہم نے حضور کے ساتھ خیبر کا غزوہ کیا ۔ ہم نے اس میں نقیمت حاصل کی تو حضور نے ایک ٹکڑا ہم میں تقسیم کیا اور باقی غنیمت میں حصہ دے دیا (ج) حضرت عبداللہ بن عباس اس بات میں کوئی حرج نہیں سمجھتے تھے کہ آدمی گھر آنے تک دارالحرب کی زمین میں غنیمت میں سے کھائے۔
Al-Sharh al-Thamiri, Volume 4, page 279, Book of Siyar. 3034 (55): When the Muslims leave the abode of war, it is not permissible for them to feed from the spoils nor eat from it, and whoever has leftover fodder or food should return it to the spoils. Second, p. 127: From this hadith it is known that the horse, land, reins, turban, and weapons etc. are all included in salb. However, cash, gold, silver found with the slain are not included in salb. Its proof is this portion of the effect of 'Umar: 'He wrote to 'Umar: Let the people eat and feed, and whoever sells something for gold or silver, then the khums of Allah and the shares of the Muslims become obligatory upon it.' (a) (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah 127, in food and fodder taken from enemy land, vol. 6, p. 508, no. 33319). From this effect it is known that gold and silver are the right of all mujahideen. 13034 (55) If a Muslim leaves the abode of war, it is not permissible to feed fodder from the spoils nor to eat from it. And whatever fodder or food remains with him, he should return it to the spoils. As long as he remained in the abode of war, he could use the food etc. of the spoils. But when they left the abode of war, now he cannot use from it. Now whatever remains, he should include it in the spoils, and after the imam divides, he may eat and feed from his own share. After leaving the abode of war, this property has become the property of all mujahideen, so he should use his own share after division among the mujahideen. (2) After leaving the abode of war, it is necessary to divide the spoils among the mujahideen, because if each person has leftover food and drink, complete division cannot occur. Therefore it is necessary to include these items in the spoils. (3) Mu'adh said: We fought with the Messenger of Allah at Khaybar and acquired spoils, and the Messenger of Allah divided a portion among us and left the rest in the spoils (b) (Abu Dawud, chapter on selling food if it remains from the people in enemy land, p. 13, no. 2707). From this hadith it is known that he should use only according to need and include the rest in the spoils. (4) In an effect: 'Abdullah ibn 'Abbas saw no harm in a man eating food in the land of shirk until he enters his family (c) (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, section on those who said eat from the food and do not carry it, vol. 6, p. 509, no. 33337). From this effect it is known that he can eat until he reaches dar al-Islam (his family), then return and collect. Footnote: (continued from previous page) They came to Khalid. All were adorned with gold and jewels. Khalid took some of it and gave the rest as nafil. I asked, O Khalid! What is this? Do you not know that the Prophet gave all the equipment to the killer? Khalid said, Yes! But this was too much, so he took some. (a) 'Umar wrote to me: Let the people eat and feed fodder from the spoils. Yes! If someone sells for gold or silver, then khums is obligatory and it is the share of the Muslims. (b) Mu'adh said: We fought with the Prophet at Khaybar and acquired spoils. The Prophet divided a portion among us and gave the rest as a share in the spoils. (c) 'Abdullah ibn 'Abbas did not consider it objectionable that a man should eat from the spoils in the land of dar al-harb until he reaches home.
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Book of Siyar: When Muslims leave dar al-harb (enemy territory), they are prohibited from using any portion of the spoils for feeding or eating. Any leftover fodder or food must be returned to the spoils pool. The commentary explains that while in dar al-harb, limited use was permitted due to necessity, but upon leaving, the spoils become collective property of all mujahideen; thus individual use before division is not allowed. The proof is drawn from the hadith of Sayyiduna Mu'adh in the Battle of Khaybar, where the Prophet divided only a portion and kept the rest in the spoils, and from the athar of Ibn Abbas permitting consumption only until reaching dar al-Islam. The footnote discusses related issues of salb and transactions involving gold and silver.

Key Terms
علف (ʿalaf): Fodder for animals; in this context, feed for horses from the spoils.
دار الحرب (dār al-ḥarb): Territory under non-Muslim control where hostilities are permitted.
غنيمة (ghanīmah): Spoils taken by force from the enemy during battle.
سلب (salb): The personal effects of a slain enemy, typically given to the killer as an incentive.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on using leftover food from spoils after Muslims leave dar al-harb?
A) It is permissible to eat it as long as it is consumed before reaching home.
B) It is prohibited; the food must be returned to the spoils pool.
C) It is permissible only with the permission of the imam.
D) It is recommended to give it to the poor.

Key Takeaway
Spoils become collective property of all mujahideen upon leaving dar al-harb; individual use before division is haram, and all leftovers must be returned.

The Obligation of Khums and Its Distribution
Ruling with proof on khums obligation and distribution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the obligation of khums, identify its five categories of recipients, and explain the proof from the Quran and the Prophet's practice.

Core Idea
The imam must set aside one-fifth of spoils for five categories before distributing the rest to combatants.

This lesson explains the fundamental rule of spoils division: khums is a divine right that must be extracted first. The Quran and the Prophet's practice define the recipients clearly. Understanding this helps us grasp the Islamic financial system of public wealth.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The imam is required to divide the spoils. This is an obligation (wajib) on him.
The text says 'يقسم الامام الغنيمة' – the imam divides, implying duty.
2
Separate the khums
First, take out one-fifth (khums). This is the non-negotiable portion belonging to Allah, the Prophet, and specified groups.
The verse (8:41) explicitly commands this.
3
Identify the five categories
The khums is divided into five portions: for Allah/Kaaba, the Prophet, near relatives, orphans, the poor, and the wayfarer. The athar shows the Prophet striking his hand into the khums and setting some for the Kaaba.
The footnotes clarify that the Prophet allocated part to the Kaaba as 'Allah's share'.
4
Distribute the remaining four-fifths
After khums, the remaining four-fifths go to the combatants (ghānimīn) who participated in the battle.
This is implied by the verse and explicitly stated in the athar.
5
Confirm the proof
The Quran (8:41) and the practice of the Prophet (reported by Abu al-‘Aliyah) are the evidences. The athar confirms the division into five for khums.
The dalil is qat‘i in thubut but zanni in dalala regarding details.

الشرح الثميرى الجزء الرابع)
۲۸۰
كتاب السير
[۳۰۳۵ (۵۶) ويقسم الامام الغنيمة فيُخرج خمسها ويقسم الاربعة اخماس بين الغانمين [۳۰۳٦] (۵۷) للفارس سهمان وللراجل سهم عند ابي حنيفة رحمه الله وقالا علف : چارہ۔
[۳۰۳۵] (۵۶) امام مال غنیمت تقسیم کرے۔ پس اس میں سے پانچواں حصہ نکالے باقی چار حصے مجاہدین میں تقسیم کرے۔ مال غنیمت میں جو بھی آئے اس میں سے پانچواں حصہ شمس نکالے جو حضور کے زمانے میں پانچ طبقوں میں تقسیم ہوتا تھا۔ (۱) حضور (۲) ان کے رشتہ در (۳) یتیم (۴) مسکین (۵) اور مسافر کے درمیان اور باقی چار حصے مجاہدین کے درمیان تقسیم ہوتے تھے۔ مثلا چیپس در هم مال غنیمت میں آیا تو ایک پانچواں حصہ پانچ درہم ہوئے۔ ان پانچ درہم میں سے ایک درہم حضور کے لئے ، ایک درہم ان کے رشتہ دار کے لئے ، ایک درہم یتیم کے لئے، ایک درہم مسکین کے لئے اور ایک درہم مسافر کے لئے ہوگا، باقی چار حصے یعنی ہیں درہم تمام مجاہدین میں تقسیم ہوں گے۔
اس آیت میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ واعلموا انما غنمتم من شيء فان لله خمسه وللرسول ولذى القربى واليتمى والمساكين وابن السبيل ان كنتم آمنتم بالله (الف) ( آیت ۴۱ ، سورۃ الانفال (۸) اس آیت میں پانچویں حصے کو پانچوں طبقوں میں تقسیم کرنے کا تذکرہ ہے (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ عن ابی العالية قال كان رسول الله يوتى بالغنيمة فيقسمها على خمسة فيكون اربعة لمن شهدها ويأخذ الخمس فيضرب بيده فيه فما اخذ من شيء جعله للكعبة وهو سهم ا الله الذي ثم يقسم مابقى على خمسة فيكون سهم لرسول الله وسهم لذوى القربى وسهم لليتامى وسهم للمساكين وسهم لابن السبيل (ب) (مصنف ابن ابی شیبه ۱۲۴ فی الغنیمت کیف یقسم ، ج سادس، ص ۵۰۴ نمبر ۳۳۲۸۷ /مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الغنيمة والفی مختلفان ، ج خامس، ص ۱۳۱۰، نمبر ۹۷۱۵) اس اثر سے پتا چلا کہ چار حصے مجاہدین کے لئے ہیں اور پانچواں حصہ یعنی شمس میں پانچ طبقے شریک ہیں۔ [۳۰۳۶] (۵۷) گھوڑے سوار کے لئے دو حصے اور پیدل والے کے لئے ایک حصہ۔ اور صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ گھوڑے سوار کے لئے تین حصے ہوں گے۔
مال غنیمت میں سے پانچواں حصہ شمس نکالنے کے بعد مجاہدین میں جو مال تقسیم ہوگا اس کی صورت یہ ہوگی کہ جو گھوڑ سوار ہے اس کو دو حصے ملیں گے ایک حصہ گھوڑے کا اور ایک حصہ سوار کا ۔ اور جو پیدل جہاد کر رہا ہے اس کو صرف ایک حصہ ملے گا آدمی کا ۔ یہ امام ابو حنیفہ کی رائے
حاشیہ : (الف) یقین کرو کہ جو کچھ تم نے نقیمت حاصل کی تو اس کا پانچواں حصہ اللہ، رسول، رسول کے رشتہ دار یتیم مسکین اور مسافر کے لئے ہے اگرتم اللہ پر ایمان رکھتے ہو ( ب ) حضور کے پاس غنیمت لائی جاتی تو اس کو پانچ حصوں پر تقسیم فرماتے۔ چار حصے ان کے لئے جو جنگ میں شریک ہوتے اور پانچویں حصے پر ہاتھ مارتے اور اس میں سے کچھ کعبہ کے لئے لیتے کہ وہ اللہ کا حصہ ہے جس کا تذکرہ آیت میں ہے پھر باقی کو پانچ حصوں پر تقسیم کرتے تو ایک حصہ حضور کے لئے ، دوسرا حصہ حضور کے رشتہ داروں کے لئے اور تیسرا حصہ قیموں کے لئے اور چوتھا حصہ مسکینوں کے لئے اور پانچواں حصہ مسافر کے لئے۔
Al-Sharh al-Thamiri, Volume 4, page 280, Book of Siyar. 3035 (56): The imam divides the spoils: he takes out its khums and divides the four-fifths among the combatants. 3036 (57): For the horseman are two shares, and for the footman one share according to Abu Hanifa, and they (Sahibayn) say (horseman gets three shares). Fodder: fodder. 3035 (56): The imam divides the spoils. So he takes out one-fifth from it, and divides the remaining four shares among the mujahideen. Whatever comes into the spoils, he takes out one-fifth as khums, which in the Prophet's time was divided among five categories: (1) the Prophet, (2) his relatives, (3) orphans, (4) the poor, (5) and the wayfarer. The remaining four shares were divided among the mujahideen. For example, if twenty-five dirhams came into the spoils, one-fifth is five dirhams. Of these five dirhams, one dirham for the Prophet, one dirham for his relatives, one dirham for orphans, one dirham for the poor, and one dirham for the wayfarer. The remaining four shares i.e., twenty dirhams, will be divided among all mujahideen. The proof for this is in this verse: 'And know that whatever you take as spoils, one-fifth is for Allah, the Messenger, the near relative, orphans, the needy, and the wayfarer, if you believe in Allah' (a) (Verse 41, Surah al-Anfal (8)). This verse mentions dividing one-fifth among five categories. (2) In an effect: From Abu al-‘Aliyah, he said: The Prophet would be brought the spoils and he would divide them into five parts: four parts for those who witnessed the battle, and he would take the khums. Then he would strike his hand into it, and whatever he took from something, he would put it for the Ka‘bah, and that is the share of Allah. Then he would divide the remainder into five parts: one share for the Messenger of Allah, one share for the near relatives, one share for orphans, one share for the poor, and one share for the wayfarer. (b) (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah 124, on how spoils are divided, vol. 6, p. 504, no. 33287 / Musannaf ‘Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on spoils and fay’ differ, vol. 5, p. 1310, no. 9715). From this effect it is known that four shares are for the mujahideen and the fifth share i.e., khums, five categories participate. 3036 (57): For the horseman are two shares, and for the footman one share. And the Sahibayn say that the horseman will have three shares. After taking out one-fifth khums from the spoils, the form of the division among mujahideen will be: the horseman gets two shares – one share for the horse and one share for the rider – and the footman fighting on foot gets only one share for the man. This is the view of Imam Abu Hanifah. Footnote: (a) 'Believe that whatever you have acquired as spoils, its one-fifth is for Allah, the Messenger, the Messenger's relatives, orphans, poor, and wayfarer, if you believe in Allah.' (b) The Prophet would be brought spoils, then he would divide them into five parts. Four parts for those who participated in the battle, and he would take the fifth part, strike his hand into it, and take some of it for the Ka‘bah – that is the share of Allah mentioned in the verse. Then he would divide the remainder into five parts: one share for the Prophet, one share for the Prophet's relatives, one share for orphans, one share for the poor, and one share for the wayfarer.
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage contains two consecutive rulings from the Book of Siyar. First, the imam's duty in dividing spoils: he must separate one-fifth as khums (which is distributed to five categories: Allah's share, the Prophet, relatives, orphans, poor, wayfarer) and distribute the remaining four-fifths among the combatants. This is proven by the Quranic verse (8:41) and the practice of the Prophet as reported by Abu al-‘Aliyah. Second, the dispute regarding the shares of horsemen and foot soldiers: Imam Abu Hanifah holds that a horseman receives two shares (one for himself and one for his horse), while a foot soldier receives one share. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that the horseman receives three shares. The commentary explains Abu Hanifah's rationale but does not provide a tarjih. The footnote clarifies the verse and the practice of the Prophet in dividing khums.

Key Terms
خمس (khums): One-fifth of the spoils set aside for Allah, the Prophet, relatives, orphans, poor, and wayfarer.
غانمين (ghānimīn): Combatants who participated in the battle and are entitled to a share of the spoils.
سهم (sahm): Share; a portion of the spoils allocated to a combatant or recipient.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many categories of recipients are mentioned for the khums in the Quranic verse cited?
A) Four
B) Five
C) Six
D) Seven

Key Takeaway
The imam must set aside one-fifth of spoils as khums and distribute it to five designated groups; the remaining four-fifths go to the combatants.

Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules
intermediate
10 min
The Dispute on Horseman's Shares: Two vs Three
Intra-Hanafi dispute on horseman's shares

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the number of shares for a horseman, identify the mufta bihi position, and apply it to calculate shares.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa gives the horseman two shares (one for man, one for horse); the Sahibayn give three; the relied-upon view is two.

After khums is extracted, the remaining spoils are divided among combatants. But how many shares does a horseman receive? There is a well-known difference within the Hanafi school itself. This lesson unpacks that dispute and shows its practical impact.

Guided Path
1
State the base rule
After khums, the imam divides the four-fifths among the combatants (ghānimīn).
This is not disputed.
2
Identify the disputed element
The number of shares for a horseman (fāris) compared to a footman (rājil).
Footman gets one share by consensus.
3
Present Abu Hanifa's view
Horseman gets two shares: one for himself and one for his horse.
The text says 'للراجل سهم وللفارس سهمان' indicating the horse gets a separate share.
4
Present Sahibayn's view
Horseman gets three shares (presumably one for man and two for horse, or man gets one and horse gets two).
The exact reason is not given in the text, but later sources discuss whether the horse is considered for cavalry advantage.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Calculate total shares for a mixed force. If 10 horsemen and 20 footmen: Abu Hanifa -> 10×2 + 20×1 = 40 shares; Sahibayn -> 10×3 + 20×1 = 50 shares. The difference affects each combatant's portion.
This shows the practical consequence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Commentary
This passage contains two consecutive rulings from the Book of Siyar. First, the imam's duty in dividing spoils: he must separate one-fifth as khums (which is distributed to five categories: Allah's share, the Prophet, relatives, orphans, poor, wayfarer) and distribute the remaining four-fifths among the combatants. This is proven by the Quranic verse (8:41) and the practice of the Prophet as reported by Abu al-‘Aliyah. Second, the dispute regarding the shares of horsemen and foot soldiers: Imam Abu Hanifah holds that a horseman receives two shares (one for himself and one for his horse), while a foot soldier receives one share. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that the horseman receives three shares. The commentary explains Abu Hanifah's rationale but does not provide a tarjih. The footnote clarifies the verse and the practice of the Prophet in dividing khums.

Key Terms
فارس (fāris): Horseman; a combatant riding a horse in battle.
راجل (rājil): Footman; a combatant fighting on foot.
سهم (sahm): Share; a portion of the spoils allocated to a combatant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position in the Hanafi school, how many shares does a horseman receive?
A) One share
B) Two shares
C) Three shares
D) Four shares

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the operative ruling is that a horseman receives two shares (one for himself and one for his horse), and a footman receives one share.

Shares for a Horseman in Ghanimah: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Presents legal dispute over horseman shares with hadith proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state both Hanafi positions on horseman shares, explain the proofs from hadith, and identify the mufta bihi view.

Core Idea
The horseman receives three shares: one for himself and two for his horse.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute over the number of shares a horseman receives in the division of spoils (ghanimah). While Imam Abu Hanifa held that the horseman gets two shares (one for himself, one for his horse), his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), ruled that the horseman gets three shares (one for himself, two for his horse). The matn we study adopts the Sahibayn view, which has become the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school. By understanding the two proofs and the method of tarjih, you will see how later scholars resolved the apparent conflict between hadiths.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the two positions
The issue is the number of shares for a horseman in ghanimah. State Abu Hanifa's position (two shares) and the Sahibayn's position (three shares). Note that the horse itself gets shares, not the rider alone.
The horse is considered a separate entity for distribution.
2
Analyze the Khaybar hadith (Abu Hanifa's dalil)
The hadith states the Prophet gave the horseman two shares and the footman one. Consider how this proves two shares: does the horseman here include both rider and horse as one unit, or does it give two shares to the horseman himself?
The commentary presents this as proof for two shares.
3
Analyze the Ibn Umar hadith (Sahibayn's dalil)
The hadith explicitly says the Prophet gave a man one share and his horse two shares, total three. This distinguishes the rider's share from the horse's share.
This is the primary proof for three shares.
4
Compare thubut and dalala
Both hadith are ahad (zanni al-thubut) and zanni al-dalala. So neither is decisive by itself. The tarjih must consider other factors such as number of narrators, consistency with general principles, and practice of the Companions.
Tarjih is needed because both are ahad.
5
Apply tarjih and determine mufta bihi
The matn adopted the three-share view, and later Hanafi works follow this. The reasoning: the Ibn Umar hadith is more explicit in distinguishing shares, and it is supported by general practice and qiyas (since the horse provides more utility in battle, it deserves more shares). Also, the Sahibayn's view is more cautious (would distribute more shares, benefiting the mujahid more).
The mufta bihi is three shares.

Source Text

Al-Sharh al-Thamiri, Part 4, page 281, Book of Siyar. For the horseman: three shares. 3037 (58) And no share is given except for one horse. Yes. There is proof of this in the hadith. The Prophet divided Khaybar into thirty-six shares: half for the Muslims' affairs and half (eighteen hundred shares) for the mujahideen. The mujahideen were fifteen hundred, among whom three hundred were horsemen, so they doubled to six hundred, making twelve hundred foot and six hundred horse, totaling eighteen hundred. And the horseman was given two shares. The hadith is: He said: 'Khaybar was divided among the people of al-Hudaybiyyah, the Messenger of Allah divided it into eighteen shares. The army was one thousand five hundred, among whom three hundred were horsemen. He gave the horseman two shares and the footman one share.' (alif) (Abu Dawood, Bab ma ja'a fi hukm ard Khaybar, p. 68 no. 3015; Dar Qutni, Kitab al-Siyar, Vol. 4, p. 61 no. 4138). From this hadith, it is understood that the horseman gets only two shares and the footman gets one. The Sahibayn say that the horseman has three shares. There is proof of this in a hadith: From Ibn Umar that the Messenger of Allah gave a man and his horse three shares: one share for him and two shares for his horse. (ba) (Abu Dawood, Bab fi siman al-khayl, p. 19 no. 2733; Tirmidhi, Bab fi sahm al-khayl, p. 283 no. 1554; Dar Qutni, Kitab al-Siyar, Vol. 4, p. 58 no. 4122). From this hadith, it is understood that the horse gets two shares and its rider one share, totaling three shares. Faris: derived from faras (horse), meaning horseman; sahm: share.
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This passage presents the first ruling of the section on ghanimah shares from the matn. The matn states that the horseman receives three shares, and the commentary immediately discusses a dispute. Although the matn gives the three-share ruling, the commentary first presents the proof for the two-share position (attributed to Abu Hanifa via the Khaybar hadith) and then the proof for the three-share position (Sahibayn via Ibn Umar's hadith). The commentary does not explicitly weigh which is stronger, but the matn itself adopts the Sahibayn view. This is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa argues from the practice at Khaybar where the horseman got two shares, while the Sahibayn argue from the general hadith giving the horse two shares and the rider one. In practice, the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position is the Sahibayn view as reflected in the matn.

Key Terms
فارس (faris): Horseman, rider of a horse in battle
سهم (sahm): Share, portion of the spoils of war

Key Takeaway
The horseman receives three shares in ghanimah: one for himself and two for his horse, based on the Ibn Umar hadith.

The Rule of Horse Shares in Ghanimah: One Horse per Person
Ruling on horse shares in ghanimah with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on how many horses receive shares in ghanimah, identify the evidence for the majority view, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute with Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Only one horse per person receives a share in ghanimah, even if multiple horses are brought; Abu Yusuf holds two.

This lesson examines the rule of horse shares in ghanimah. The Hanafi school holds that only one horse per fighter receives a share, regardless of how many horses he brings into battle. We will explore the textual and rational evidence, the precedent from the Battle of Khaybar, and the dissenting view of Imam Abu Yusuf, who argues for two horses based on a mursal hadith. Understanding this dispute clarifies how distributive justice in ghanimah is balanced with practical considerations.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling and its scope
Identify the clear statement from the matn: 'No share is given except for one horse.' This applies to any person who brings multiple horses to jihad.
The ruling covers horses only; riding camels and mules receive no share.
2
Identify the evidence for the majority
Examine the hadith of Zubayr: the Prophet gave Zubayr two shares for his horse (one horse only) despite Zubayr having two horses. Also consider the rational arguments: a person can only ride one horse at a time, and giving shares for multiple horses would unjustly reduce shares for other fighters.
The hadith shows only one horse received shares; the other horse was excluded.
3
Present Abu Yusuf's dissent and his evidence
Abu Yusuf holds that if someone participates with multiple horses, they receive shares for two horses. His proof is a mursal hadith from Makhul: 'No share from horses except for two horses, even if he has a thousand horses.'
The mursal hadith is of weaker transmission (thubut zanni) compared to the established practice.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
The practical difference: under the majority view, a fighter with multiple horses gets shares for one horse; under Abu Yusuf's view, for two horses. The matn and the majority Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) support the one-horse view, and this is the mufta bihi.
The commentary does not explicitly resolve the dispute, but the matn's wording and the lack of rebuttal indicate the relied-upon position.

Equality of Shares: Local and Arab Horses in Ghanimah
Establishes that local (non-Arab) horses and purebred Arab horses receive equal shares in ghanimah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the equality of shares between local and Arab horses in ghanimah and explain the evidence from the athar of Hasan al-Basri.

Core Idea
All war horses, regardless of pedigree, receive equal shares in ghanimah.

In the distribution of war spoils (ghanimah), horses that are used in combat are entitled to a share. A common misconception is that purebred Arab horses (itaq) deserve a larger share than local horses (baradhin) due to their superior lineage. However, the Hanafi school, relying on an athar from Hasan al-Basri, rules that both types are equivalent in share entitlement. This lesson will examine the ruling, its proof, and the underlying rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
State the explicit ruling from the matn: local horses and Arab horses are equal in shares.
The ruling is expressed by the word 'sawa' (equal).
2
Define the Terms
Understand the definitions: baradhin are smaller, non-Arab horses that serve in war; itaq are tall, purebred Arab horses.
Both are classified as 'faras' (horse) and used in battle.
3
Locate the Evidence
Examine the athar from Hasan al-Basri: 'Al-baradhinu bi-manzilati al-faras' (the local horse is equivalent to the Arab horse).
This is a qawl sahabi (statement of a Companion) found in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah and Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq.
4
Analyze the Proof
Understand why this proof is used: Hasan al-Basri explicitly equates the two, indicating equal entitlement. The key is that both are horses and both are useful in war.
The proof is zanni in transmission and meaning, but sufficient for a ruling in ghanimah.
5
Note the Scope
The ruling applies only to horses used in warfare. Non-combat horses receive no share.
The criterion is utility in battle, not pedigree.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۳۰۳۸](۵۹) والبراذين والعتاق سواء
ر ایسے گھوڑے جو جنگ کے کام آئے لیکن قد میں تھوڑے چھوٹے ہوں اس کو براذین یعنی دیسی گھوڑے کہتے ہیں۔ اور لمبے قد کے گھوڑے کو عتاق یعنی عربی گھوڑے کہتے ہیں۔ چونکہ دونوں ہی گھوڑے ہیں اور دونوں ہی جنگ میں کام آتے ہیں اس لئے دونوں کے حصے برابر ہیں۔ کسی کے کم نہیں۔
اثر میں ہے۔ عن الحسن قال البرذون بمنزلة الفرس (ب) (مصنف ابن ابى شيبة ۱۰۳ فی البراذین مالها وكيف يقسم لها، ج سادس، ص ۴۹۴، نمبر ۳۳۱۷۶ / مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب السهام خیل ، ج خامس، ص ۱۸۵، نمبر ۹۳۱۸) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ دیسی گھوڑا اور عربی گھوڑا دونوں کے حصے برابر ہیں۔
[3038] (59) And local horses and Arab horses are equal. [Explanation:] Such horses that are useful for war but smaller in stature are called baradhin (local horses), and tall horses are called itaq (Arab horses). Since both are horses and both are useful in war, their shares are equal; neither is less. There is an athar: From al-Hasan: 'The local horse is equivalent to the [Arab] horse (faras).' (ba) (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, ... Vol. 6, p. 494 no. 33176; Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Bab al-siham khayl, Vol. 5, p. 185 no. 9318). From this athar, it is understood that the local horse and the Arab horse have equal shares.
Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This passage presents the third ruling from the matn: local horses (baradhin) and purebred Arab horses (itaq) are equal in terms of ghanimah shares. The commentary defines both types: baradhin are smaller but still suitable for combat, while itaq are the taller Arab horses. Since both are called 'horse' (faras) and serve the same purpose, they have identical shares. The commentary cites an athar (tradition) from Hasan al-Basri that a local horse is in the same category as an Arab horse for this purpose. This ruling applies only to horses that are actually used in warfare; non-combat horses are excluded.

Key Terms
براذين (baradhin): Local, non-Arab horses that are smaller but still used in battle
عتاق (itaq): Purebred Arab horses, tall and of noble lineage

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) They are equivalent
C) The Arab horse receives double
D) Local horses receive no share

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, all horses used in war receive equal shares in ghanimah, regardless of breed or pedigree.

Riding Camels and Mules Do Not Receive Shares in Ghanimah
Clarifies that only horses receive shares in ghanimah; other mounts are excluded.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the entitlement of riding camels and mules in ghanimah and explain the Quranic proof that restricts shares to horses.

Core Idea
Only horses receive shares in ghanimah; other mounts are compensated separately.

In the distribution of war spoils (ghanimah), not every animal used in battle entitles its owner to a share. The Hanafi school rules that only horses qualify, while riding camels and mules are excluded. This distinction is based on explicit Quranic mention and early practice. Let's examine the evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the animals and the ruling
Determine which animals are excluded from ghanimah shares according to the text: riding camel (rahilah) and mule (baghl). The ruling is that they do not receive shares.
The text explicitly states they are not given shares, unlike horses.
2
Locate the primary proof (dalil)
The author cites Quran 8:60, which commands preparing 'power and horses tethered' (wa min ribat al-khayl). The specific mention of horses indicates that other mounts are not entitled to shares.
The verse is qat'i in transmission but zanni in dalala (interpretation) regarding shares.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (evidentiary link)
The phrase 'ribat al-khayl' restricts the war animals that qualify for shares to horses. This is a dalalat al-nass (implicit meaning) that other animals (camels, mules) are excluded from this category.
The Hanafi usul principle: al-amm yufidu al-wujub, but here the specificity of 'khayl' is key.
4
Examine the supporting athar
An athar from Makhul confirms that the early Muslims did not give shares for mules or donkeys. This corroborates the Quranic inference.
The athar supports the 'amal (practice) of the Companions.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference and tarjih
Some other schools may extend shares to other useful animals, but the Hanafi school restricts to horses based on the explicit text. The mufta bihi is to not give shares for camels and mules.
The Hanafi position is stronger due to the clear proof from the Quran and practice.

[3039] (60) And no share is given for the riding camel nor the mule. [Explanation:] For load-carrying animals and mules, there are no shares. Camels etc. that carry loads can be given something in exchange for service, but not a formal share in ghanimah like the horse. In the verse, the command is to prepare horses to frighten the enemy. Since in earlier times battles were won by horses, a share is allocated for them; for other animals, no share in ghanimah is allocated. This verse encourages that: 'And prepare against them whatever you can of power and of horses tethered, that you may frighten thereby the enemy of Allah and your enemy.' (jim) (Surah al-Anfal 8:60). This verse encourages breeding horses to frighten the enemy, so they have a share in ghanimah. (dal) Makhul: They did not give shares for a mule, nor for a ..., nor for a donkey.

Commentary
This final passage of the set presents the fourth ruling: riding camels (rahilah) and mules (baghl) do not receive shares in ghanimah. The commentary explains that such animals may be compensated for their service, but they are not entitled to a formal share like horses. The proof is derived from Quran 8:60, which specifically mentions horses for warfare, implying that other mounts do not qualify. An athar from Makhul confirms that no shares were given for mules, donkeys, etc. The footnotes repeat earlier points about horses and the verse. This ruling distinguishes between horses (which are essential for combat and thus get shares) and other pack animals (which are auxiliary and do not).

Key Terms
راحلة (rahilah): Riding camel used for transport in warfare
بغل (baghl): Mule
