Khums Shares After the Prophet's Death
Analysing the abrogation of khums shares

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi reasoning for the abrogation of the Prophet's and relatives' shares in khums and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
After the Prophet's death, his khums share and relatives' unconditional share are abrogated; only poor relatives receive, as part of general categories.

The distribution of khums (one-fifth of war booty) involves shares for Allah, the Prophet, his relatives, orphans, needy, and travelers. A key question arose after the Prophet's death: do his share and his relatives' share continue? The Hanafi school holds that these shares are abrogated, while Imam al-Shafi'i maintains the relatives' share remains. This passage presents the Hanafi argument and responds to the Shafi'i proof.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on khums shares
Identify what the Hanafi school says about the shares of Allah, the Prophet, and relatives after his death. Note that only poor relatives receive, and they are included in the three categories.
The share of Allah is only a verbal blessing, not an actual share.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that the relatives' share remains because the Quranic verse (8:41) is still in effect.
Shafi'is hold that the relatives' share is perpetual and unconditional.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Shafi'i proof: the verse remains, so the ruling continues. This is based on the general principle that a Quranic ruling applies until abrogated.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school responds that the verse was specific to the Prophet's lifetime; after his death, the ruling is abrogated because the reason (support of the Prophet) no longer exists. They cite the hadith that the Prophet's wealth is charity and the practice of the caliphs.
The safi (right to choose an item) is also abrogated analogously.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis do not allocate a separate share for relatives; they give to poor relatives only as part of the general categories. Shafi'is allocate a fixed share to relatives unconditionally.
This affects how war booty is distributed in both schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويدخل فقراء ذوى القربى فيهم ويُقدَّمون ولا يدفع الى اغنيائهم شيء. ... واما ماذكر الله تعالى في الخمس فانما هو لافتتاح الكلام تبركا باسمه ... وسهم النبى عليه السلام سقط بموته كما سقط الصفی ... وسهم ذوي القربى كانوا يستحقونه في زمن النبي عليه السلام بالنصرة وبعده بالفقر. ... واما قول الامام شافعی انهم يستحقونه بعد النبي عليه السلام لبقاء الاية فالجواب ان الاية محمولة على زمن النبي عليه السلام واما بعده فقد سقط حكمها لسقوط النبي عن هذه الدنيا والله اعلم.
And the poor among the relatives enter into them and are given precedence, and nothing is given to their wealthy ones. ... As for what Allah mentioned in the khums, it is only for opening the speech seeking blessing with His name. ... The share of the Prophet, peace be upon him, is dropped by his death just as the safi is dropped. ... The share of the relatives: they used to deserve it in the time of the Prophet, peace be upon him, due to support, and after him due to poverty. ... As for the statement of Imam Shafi'i that they deserve it after the Prophet, peace be upon him, because the verse remains, the answer is that the verse is interpreted as applicable in the time of the Prophet, peace be upon him; after him its ruling has dropped due to the departure of the Prophet from this world. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage discusses the distribution of the khums (one-fifth) of war booty, focusing on the shares of Allah, the Prophet (peace be upon him), and his relatives (dhu al-qurba). The Hanafi position is that the share of Allah is only a way to begin speech with blessing, not an actual share. The Prophet's share is abrogated after his death, similar to the safi (the right to choose any item before division). The relatives' share was given during the Prophet's lifetime due to their support for him, but after his death it is only given to those among them who are poor, and they are included in the general categories of orphans, needy, and travelers, given precedence due to their relation. The text then addresses the Shafi'i view that the relatives' share continues after the Prophet's death because the verse (Quran 8:41) still exists. The Hanafi response is that the verse was applicable during the Prophet's time; after his death, its ruling on the relatives' share abates. Evidence includes the hadith that the Prophet's inheritance is charity, and the practice of Caliphs Ali, Abu Bakr, and Umar.

Key Terms
خمس (khums): One-fifth of war booty set aside for Allah, the Prophet, relatives, orphans, needy, and travelers.
صفي (safi): The Prophet's right to choose any item from the booty before division; also abrogated after his death.
ذوي القربى (dhu al-qurba): The relatives of the Prophet (peace be upon him), specifically Banu Hashim and Banu Muttalib.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is given to the caliph.
B) It is dropped and no longer given to anyone.
C) It is given to the poor among his relatives.
D) It is added to the share of the relatives.

Key Takeaway
After the Prophet's death, his khums share and the unconditional share of his relatives are abrogated; only poor relatives receive, as part of the general categories.

Abrogation of the Share of Relatives After the Prophet's Death
Ruling on cessation of share for relatives and consensus to divert it

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the share of relatives in khums after the Prophet's death and explain the evidence from the hadith and the Companions' consensus.

Core Idea
The share of relatives in khums was specific to the Prophet’s lifetime; after his death, it was abrogated by consensus.

In this lesson, we examine the fate of the share of relatives (sahm dhi al-qurba) from the khums after the Prophet's death. The Hanafi school holds that this share ceased because its reason—support from relatives—ended with the Prophet. We will analyze the hadith of Jubayr ibn Mut'im and the subsequent consensus of the Companions who diverted these funds to military preparation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the allocation of a portion of khums to the Prophet's relatives (Banu Hashim and Banu al-Muttalib). The Hanafi ruling is that after the Prophet's death, this share is abrogated (no longer given).
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence is the hadith from Jubayr ibn Mut'im in Abu Dawud, which shows the Prophet allocated the share during his life. The commentary explains that the reason (illah) was the support from relatives.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's statement 'we are one thing' and the interlacing of fingers indicate unity and support. After his death, this support no longer exists, so the share drops.
The reasoning is based on the cessation of the cause (zawal al-illah).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school holds that the share continues. The Hanafi position relies on the Companions' consensus after the Prophet's death.
The consensus (ijma) of the Companions is recorded by al-Hakim and others.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The consensus overrides any apparent continuation. This becomes the mufta bihi (operative ruling) in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اخبرنی جبیر بن مطعم قال لما كان يوم خيبر وضع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم سهم ذي القربي في بني هاشم و بني المطلب و ترك بني نوفل و بني عبد شمس، فانطلقت انا و عثمان بن عفان حتى أتينا النبي فقلنا يا رسول الله ! هؤلاء بنو هاشم لا ننكر فضلهم للمواضع الذي وضعك الله به منهم، فما بال اخواننا بني المطلب اعطيتهم و تركتنا و قرابتنا واحدة؟ فقال رسول الله انا و بنو المطلب لا نفترق في جاهلية و لا اسلام و انما نحن و هم شيء واحد و شبك بين اصابعه صلى الله عليه وسلم ( ابوداؤد شريف ، باب في مواضع قسم الخمس و سهم ذي القربي ، ج 2، ص 60، رقم 298) اس حديث میں آپ نے اشارہ فرمایا کہ زمانہ جاہلیت اور زمانہ اسلام دونوں میں بنو مطلب نے ہماری مدد کی ہے جس کی وجہ سے اس کے لئے خمس میں ایک حصہ ہے۔ اور آپ کی وفات کے بعد مدد کی ضرورت نہیں ہے اس لئے ان کا حصہ ساقط ہو جائے گا (2) اور مستدرك الحاكم كا بھی اثر گزرا جس میں تھا کہ اب آپ کے رشتہ داروں کے حصے ساقط ہونے پر صحابہ کا اتفاق ہو گیا۔ عبارت یہ تھی فاجتمع رأيهم على ان يجعلوا هذين السهمين في الخيل و العدة في سبيل الله فكانا على ذلك في خلافة ابي بكر و عمر (مستدرك الحاكم، كتاب قسم الفيء، ج ثاني، ص 140، رقم 2585 / مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب ذكر الخمس و سهم ذي القربي، ج خامس، ص 238، رقم 9482)
Jubayr ibn Mut'im said: On the day of Khaybar, the Messenger of Allah placed the share of relatives among Banu Hashim and Banu al-Muttalib, and left Banu Nawfal and Banu 'Abd Shams. So I and 'Uthman ibn 'Affan went to the Prophet and said: O Messenger of Allah, we do not deny the virtue of Banu Hashim for the position Allah placed you among them, but what about our brothers Banu al-Muttalib? You gave them and left us, though our relationship is the same? The Messenger of Allah said: I and Banu al-Muttalib do not separate in ignorance or Islam; we are one thing, and he interlaced his fingers. (Abu Dawud, Bab fi Muwadi' Qism al-Khumus wa Sahm Dhi al-Qurba, vol. 2, p. 60, no. 298) In this hadith, he indicated that both in Jahiliyyah and Islam, Banu al-Muttalib supported us, so they have a share in the khums. After his death, support is not needed, so their share is dropped. (2) Also, an athar in al-Mustadrak al-Hakim passed that the Companions agreed to drop the shares of relatives: they agreed to place these two shares in horses and equipment in the path of Allah, and they remained upon that in the caliphate of Abu Bakr and 'Umar. (al-Mustadrak al-Hakim, Kitab Qism al-Fay', vol. 2, p. 140, no. 2585; Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, Bab Dhikr al-Khumus wa Sahm Dhi al-Qurba, vol. 5, p. 238, no. 9482)
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This passage discusses the abrogation of the share of relatives (sahm dhi al-qurba) from the spoils after the Prophet's death. It begins by presenting the hadith of Jubayr ibn Mut'im, which shows that during the Prophet's lifetime, the share was allocated to Banu Hashim and Banu al-Muttalib due to their continuous support. The Prophet's statement 'we are one thing' and the interlacing of fingers emphasize their closeness. After the Prophet's death, the reason for this allocation—support from relatives—ceased, so the share was dropped. The commentary then cites the consensus of the Companions, recorded by al-Hakim and 'Abd al-Razzaq, that the two shares (the share of relatives and the share of the Prophet) were diverted to horses and equipment for jihad. This consensus was maintained during the caliphates of Abu Bakr and 'Umar. Thus, the ruling is that after the Prophet, no special share is given to relatives; instead, it is spent on military preparedness.

Key Terms
سهم ذي القربي (sahm dhi al-qurba): The share of the spoils allocated to the relatives of the Prophet, specifically Banu Hashim and Banu al-Muttalib, as per the hadith.
إجماع (ijma'): Consensus of the Companions to divert the share of relatives to horses and equipment for jihad.
خمس (khums): One-fifth of the spoils that is set aside for specific categories mentioned in Quran 8:41.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because the Quranic verse was abrogated
D) Because the Prophet forbade it in his final sermon

Key Takeaway
The share of relatives in khums was abrogated after the Prophet's death due to the cessation of its cause and confirmed by the Companions' consensus.

Unauthorized Raiding and the Ruling on Khums
Ruling on khums for unauthorized raiders

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school does not apply khums to spoils taken by unauthorized raiders, and identify the legal consequence of such acts.

Core Idea
Unauthorized raiding is theft, not jihad: no khums on stolen goods.

This lesson examines a nuanced ruling in Hanafi siyar: when individuals raid without the Imam's permission, the status of what they take changes from ghanimah to stolen property. Understanding this distinction is crucial for properly applying khums and recognizing the Amir's authority in military affairs. We will explore the ruling, its basis in the hadith against treachery, and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
Determine what action is being ruled upon (entering Dar al-Harb without permission by one or two individuals) and what the legal classification of both the act and the property obtained is: the act is sinful, and the property is not considered ghanimah (spoils of war) but rather stolen property.
The hukm level for the act is haram; the property is not subject to khums.
2
Locate the Dalil
Identify the evidence cited: the hadith of Ibn 'Umar that the treacherous person will have a banner raised on the Day of Judgment. This hadith is used to show that breaking covenants is a grave sin.
The dalil is from Abu Dawud and Bukhari, and it is a hadith ahad (zanni al-thubut).
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
Explain how the hadith proves the ruling: unauthorized raiding without the Imam's permission amounts to treachery (ghadr) because it potentially breaks existing covenants and disobeys the Imam, who represents the Muslim polity. The hadith condemns treachery, so the act is sinful; additionally, the property taken is likened to theft, not legitimate spoils.
The prohibition on ghadr establishes the sinfulness; the lack of authorization makes the property akin to stolen goods.
4
Note the Ikhtilaf
Acknowledge that other schools may differ: some schools might consider all property taken from hostile enemy territory as ghanimah subject to khums, even without permission. The Hanafi position prioritizes the requirement of Imam's authorization and the principle that unauthorized acts are not legitimate jihad.
Cross-madhhab: the Hanafi view is mukhtalaf fih; the thamarah al-khilaf is the applicability of khums.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi Tarjih
The Hanafi reliance on this ruling is based on the hadith's condemnation of treachery and the principle that the Imam's permission is central to legitimate military action. Therefore, the mufta bihi is that no khums is taken and the property is considered stolen, which must be returned or disposed of appropriately.
The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is well-established in Hanafi siyar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا دخل الواحد والاثنان الى دار الحرب مغيرين بغير اذن الامام فاخذوا شيئا لم يخمس. اگر ایک یا دو آدمی دار الحرب میں لوٹ مار کرتے ہوئے داخل ہو جا ئیں بغیر امام کی اجازت کے اور وہ کچھ لے لیں تو خمس نہیں لیا جائیگا۔ بغیر امام کی اجازت کے ایک دو آدمی لوٹ مار کرتے ہوئے داخل ہو جائیں اور حربیوں کا کچھ مال لوٹ لائیں تو اس میں سے امام خمس نہیں لے گا۔ یہ مال غنیمت کا نہیں ہے بلکہ اس طرح کرنا چوری کا مال شمار کیا جائے گا۔ اور چوری کے مال میں خمس نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ چوری بہر حال مبغوض ہے چاہے حربیوں کے مال کی چوری کیوں نہ ہو (۲) حدیث میں اس کا اشارہ ہے۔ عن ابن عمر ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: الغادر ينصب له لواء يوم القيامة فيقال هذه غدرة فلان بن فلان ( ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی الوفاء بالعهد ، ص ۲۳، نمبر ۲۷۵۶ / بخاری شریف، باب اثم الغادر للبر والفاجر ، ص ۴۵۲، نمبر ۳۱۸۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ عہد کو پورا کرنا چاہئے ۔ اور ایک دو آدمیوں نے گویا کہ چوری کر کے عہد کو توڑا اس لئے اس میں خمس نہیں لیا جائے گا۔
And if one or two individuals enter Dar al-Harb as raiders without the permission of the Imam and take something, it is not subject to khums. [Urdu: If one or two people enter Dar al-Harb plundering without the Imam's permission and bring back some property, the Imam will not take khums from it. This wealth is not spoils of war, but rather it is considered stolen property. And there is no khums on stolen property, because theft is detestable even if it is theft from the property of the warring disbelievers. (2) The hadith indicates this: Ibn 'Umar reported that the Messenger of Allah said: The treacherous person will have a banner set up for him on the Day of Resurrection, and it will be said, 'This is the treachery of so-and-so.' (Abu Dawud, Bab fi al-Wafa' bi al-'Ahd, p. 23, no. 2756; Bukhari, Bab Ithm al-Ghadir li al-Barr wa al-Fajir, p. 452, no. 3186) This hadith shows that covenants must be fulfilled. And the one or two individuals have broken the covenant by committing theft, so khums is not taken from it.]
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling that when a very small number of individuals (one or two) raid Dar al-Harb without the Imam's authorization, the spoils they obtain are not considered legitimate ghanimah (spoils of war) but rather theft. Consequently, the khums (one-fifth tax) is not applied. The reasoning is that such unauthorized raids amount to breaking the covenant of security (aman) that may exist between the Muslims and the enemy, or they are simply acts of theft. The proof is the hadith about the treacherous person having a banner on Judgment Day, indicating the sin of breaking covenants. Since these individuals acted without permission and in a deceitful manner, their action is sinful and the property is not subject to the khums that is specific to lawful spoils.

Key Terms
مغيرين (mugheerīn): Raiders, those who make a sudden attack for plunder.
خمس (khums): The one-fifth tax on lawful spoils of war.
غدر (ghadr): Treachery, breach of covenant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is khums not taken from property taken by one or two individuals who enter Dar al-Harb without the Imam's permission?
A) Because the amount is too small
B) Because their act is considered theft, not legitimate ghanimah
C) Because the Imam's permission is not required for small groups
D) Because khums is only due on property obtained through jihad, not raiding

Key Takeaway
Unauthorized raiding by a small group is not legitimate jihad; the spoils are stolen and not subject to khums.

Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules
intermediate
8 min
Group with Strength Entering Dar al-Harb Without Permission: Khums Obligated
Ruling that khums is taken from spoils taken by a strong group without permission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on spoils obtained by a strong group without the Imam's permission and identify the supporting evidence from hadith and athar.

Core Idea
Khums is taken from spoils of a strong group even without permission, because implicit consent suffices.

In the previous lesson, we learned that a small raiding party entering Dar al-Harb without permission does not yield khums. This passage introduces an important exception: when the group has strength (man'ah), their action is considered jihad, not mere raiding. Consequently, khums is obligatory on the spoils they acquire, even without explicit authorization. The reasoning relies on the group's capacity to engage in genuine combat and the Imam's implicit desire for enemy defeat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The passage rules on a group with strength (man'ah) entering Dar al-Harb without permission and taking spoils. The hukm: khums (1/5) is wajib on those spoils.
The term 'man'ah' is key — it distinguishes a formidable detachment from a weak raiding party.
2
Understand the key distinction
The group's strength elevates their action to jihad, not raiding. Thus the spoils are considered ghanimah (legitimate spoils of war) subject to khums.
The passage explicitly states: 'yahum jihādun' ba'l-lā ghāratun (this is jihad, not raiding).
3
Locate the proofs
Two proofs are cited: (1) The hadith of Salama ibn al-Akwa', who fought without the Prophet's order and was given shares. (2) The athar of Hasan al-Basri, stating that such a group is 'like the army' (uswat al-jaysh), meaning khums is taken.
Hadith from Abu Dawud and Muslim; athar from Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba.
4
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's granting of shares from spoils obtained without his permission indicates that these spoils are ghanimah and subject to khums. The athar directly states that the group is equivalent to the main army.
The implicit permission argument is reinforced: the Imam's general desire for enemy defeat constitutes consent.
5
Note the ikhtilaf
Some scholars (e.g., Shafi'is) require explicit permission for spoils to be considered ghanimah. The Hanafi response is that the group's strength and the existence of implicit permission suffice.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf): Hanafi school takes khums; other schools might not.

Source Text

And if a group that has strength (protection) enters and takes something, it is subject to khums. [Urdu: And if a strong group enters and they take something, khums will be taken even if the Imam did not give them permission. By 'strong group' is meant a detachment of mujahideen, not a raiding group. So if a detachment of mujahideen goes to Dar al-Harb without the Imam's permission and brings back spoils from jihad, there is khums in it. This is not raiding but jihad. The only difference is that it is without the Imam's permission. Because this detachment obtained spoils from those who are warring and with whom war is ongoing. (2) Although there is no explicit permission from the Imam, internally there is permission, because in such situations the Imam certainly desires that the warring disbelievers be defeated and suffer loss of life and property. This detachment did that, so there is implicit permission, therefore khums will be taken. (3) The hadith of Salama ibn al-Akwa' is long, where he fought against the people of Mecca without the Prophet's permission, freed the Prophet's camel, and obtained the property of the Meccans as spoils. Then the Prophet gave him both the horseman's and the foot soldier's share. This shows that if a group understands the Imam's intention and brings spoils without his permission, khums will be taken, because it is spoils, not stolen property. The part of the hadith: Iyas ibn Salama narrated from his father: 'Abd al-Rahman ibn 'Uyaynah raided the camels of the Messenger of Allah... and then the Prophet was in five hundred (i.e., he gave me the share of the horseman and the foot soldier) (Abu Dawud, Bab al-Sariyya Tardu 'ala Ahl al-'Askar, p. 22, no. 2752; Muslim, Bab Ghazwat Dhi Qard, vol. 2, p. 113, no. 1807). This hadith shows that he fought jihad without the Prophet's permission, and the Prophet must have taken khums from it and gave shares. Also, the athar of Hasan: 'If they set out with the Imam's permission, khums is taken and the rest is for them; if they set out without the Imam's permission, they are like the army' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, 12, Fi al-Sariyya Takhruj bi-ghayr Idhn al-Imam Tanghanam, vol. 6, p. 499, no. 33231). This athar indicates that they are equal to the army, meaning khums is taken.]
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage distinguishes between a small raiding party and a substantial military detachment. When a group with strength (lhum man'ah) enters Dar al-Harb without the Imam's permission, their action is considered jihad, not mere raiding. Therefore, the spoils they obtain are legitimate ghanimah and subject to khums. The reasoning is that the Imam implicitly desires the defeat of the enemy, and such a group effectively carries out that desire. The hadith of Salama ibn al-Akwa' supports this: despite acting without explicit orders, the Prophet granted him shares, implying approval. Additionally, the athar of Hasan al-Basri states that such a group is treated like the main army, meaning khums is taken. Thus, the key factor is the group's strength and ability to engage in genuine combat, distinguishing them from the unauthorized raiders of the previous lesson.

Key Terms
منعة (man'ah): Strength, protection, or power that prevents the group from being considered mere raiders.
اسوة الجيش (uswat al-jaysh): Equal to the army; meaning the group is treated like the main army in terms of distribution.
سهم الفارس والراجل (sahm al-fāris wa al-rājil): The share of the cavalryman and the foot soldier, indicating proper distribution of spoils.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Khums is taken from spoils obtained by a strong group entering Dar al-Harb without permission because their strength makes it jihad and implicit permission exists.

Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules
intermediate

Ruling on Muslim Trader Treacherously Taking Property in Dar al-Harb
Ruling with proof for a Muslim who commits treachery in enemy territory

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a Muslim who enters Dar al-Harb as a trader and treacherously takes property, explain why the ownership is milk mahzur, and apply the ruling to analogous cases.

Core Idea
A Muslim who enters enemy territory under aman and then treacherously takes property becomes the owner, but the property is prohibited—it must be given in charity.

This passage examines a delicate scenario: a Muslim enters Dar al-Harb as a trader (thereby implying a covenant of safety) and then betrays that trust by taking enemy property. The Hanafi school rules that he becomes the owner of that property, but because it was acquired through treachery, the ownership is 'milk mahzur'—valid but tainted. Consequently, he is ordered to give it in charity. We will explore the scriptural evidence and the rationale behind this unique ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario and Initial Ruling
The passage begins by stating that if a Muslim enters Dar al-Harb as a trader, it is not permissible to touch enemy property or life. If he commits treachery (ghadr) and takes property, he becomes the owner, but it is milk mahzur. Identify the key terms: ghadr and milk mahzur.
2
Examine the Prohibition of Ghadr
The author cites the hadith of Sulayman ibn Burayda in which the Prophet forbids ghadr in warfare. This hadith establishes the general prohibition of treachery, even against enemies. Note that this prohibition applies to all Muslims, including traders.
The hadith is from Muslim and Abu Dawud.
3
Analyze the Hadith of al-Mughira
The passage then presents the incident of al-Mughira, who killed his companions in Jahiliyya and took their property, then accepted Islam. The Prophet accepted his Islam but rejected the property, calling it 'mal ghadr' and not taking any of it. The author argues that since the Prophet did not order the property to be returned to the heirs, the Muslim (al-Mughira) is considered the owner, but the property is impure.
4
Understand the Underlying Principle
The commentary explains that entering as a trader implies a covenant of aman, so treachery breaks that covenant. However, the Muslim becomes owner because property taken from harbis is analogous to ghanima. But because it was taken by treachery, ownership is not pure; it is milk mahzur.
5
Apply the Ruling
The practical outcome: the Muslim must give the property in charity (sadaqah). He may not keep it for personal use. This ruling balances the prohibition of ghadr with the practical difficulty of returning property to enemy territory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان لم يأذن لهم الامام [۳۰۴۹ (۷۰) واذا دخل المسلم دار الحرب تاجرا فلا يحل له ان يتعرض لشيء من اموالهم ولا من دمائهم فان غدر بهم فأخذ شيئا ملكه ملكا محظورا
اصول یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ امام کا منشا سمجھ کر کام کیا تو ٹس لیا جائے گا اور وہ کام جائز ہوگا۔
اور اگر امام دستہ کو خود بھیجے تو اس کے مال غنیمت میں خمس ہے۔ اس حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن عبد الله بن عمران رسول الله الله قد كان ينفل بعض من يبعث من السرايا لانفسهم خاصة النفل سوى قسم عامة الجيش والخمس واجب في ذلك كله ( الف ) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی النفل للسرية يخرج من العسكر ، ج ۲، ص ۲۰ نمبر ۲۷۴۶) اس حدیث میں ہے تمام سریے کی نغنیمت میں ٹمس واجب ہوتا تھا۔ ملة : منع سے مشتق ہے روکنے کی طاقت ۔ (۳۰۴۹) (۷۰) اگر مسلمان دار الحرب میں تاجر بن کر داخل ہوا تو ان کے لئے حلال نہیں ہے کہ مال یا جان کو چھیڑے۔ پس اگر ان سے غداری کی اور کچھ لے لیا تو اس کا مالک بن جائے گا ممنوع طریقہ پر اور حکم دیا جائے گا کہ اس کو صدقہ کر دے۔ شر دار الحرب میں تاجر بن کر گیا تو گویا کہ امن لیکر گیا کہ عہد کی خلاف ورزی نہیں کروں گا۔ اس لئے اس کو غدر اور دھوکا نہیں کرنا چاہئے اور نہ حربیوں کی جان اور مال کو نقصان پہنچانا چاہئے۔ اور اگر غدر کر لیا اور ان کے مال کو اٹھا کر دار الاسلام لے آیا تو مالک ہو جائے گا۔ لیکن چونکہ غدر کے ذریعہ سے مالک ہوا ہے اس لئے ملک محظور ہوگا اور حکم دیا جائے گا کہ اس مال کو صدقہ کر دے۔ ندر نہ کرنے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن سلیمان بن بريدة عن ابيه قال كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم اذا امر اميرا على جيش ... قاتلوا من كفر بالله اغزوا ولا تغلوا ولا تغدروا ولا تمثلوا ولا تقتلوا وليدا (ب)(مسلم شریف، باب تامیر الامام الامراء على البحوث و وصیته ایا هم بآداب الغزو وغيرها، ج ۲، ص۸۲، نمبر ۱۷۳۱ را بود او د شریف، باب فی دعاء المشرکین میں ۱۳۶۱، نمبر ۲۶۱۳) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ دارالحرب میں بھی بندر اور دھوکا نہیں کرنا چاہئے۔ اور تربیوں کے مال کو غدر کر کے لیا تو ملک محظور ہو گا اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن المسور بن مخرمة قال خرج رسول الله الله زمن الحديبية في بضع عشرة مائة من اصحابه ... وكان المغيرة صحب قوما في الجاهلية فقتلهم واخذ اموالهم ثم جاء فاسلم فقال النبى الله الله اما الاسلام فقد قبلنا واما المال فانه مال غدر لا حاجة لنا فيه (ج ) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب في صلح العدو، ج ۲، ص ۱۲۴، نمبر ۲۷۶۵ / بخاری شریف ، باب الشروط في الجهاد والمصالحة مع اہل الحرب وكتابة الشروط ، ص ۱۳۷۷، نمبر ۲۷۳۱) اس
حاشیہ : (الف) جس کو خاص طور پر بھیجتے تو عام لشکر کے حصے کے علاوہ اس کو نفل دیتے تا ہم ان تمام میں شمس واجب ہوتا (ب ) آپ جب کسی لشکر پر امیر بناتے تو فرماتے جس نے اللہ کے ساتھ کفر کیا ہے اس سے جنگ کرو ۔ لیکن خیانت نہ کرو، غدر نہ کرو اور مسئلہ نہ کرو، اور بچے کوقتل نہ کرو (ج) حضور صلح حدیبیہ کے سال دس سو سے زیادہ صحابہ کے ساتھ نکلے حضرت مغیرہ زمانہ جاہلیت میں کچھ لوگوں کے ساتھ رہے تھے اور ان کو قتل کر کے مال لیا تھا ، پھر آ کر مسلمان ہوئے تھے تو آپ نے فرمایا بہر حال اسلام تو تمہارا قبول کرتا ہوں، بہر حال مال تو دھو کے کا مال ہے، مجھے اس کی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔

ويؤمر ان يتصدق به
حدیث میں ہے کہ حضرت مغیرہ بن شعبہ نے اپنے کافر ساتھیوں کو دھوکا دے کر قتل کیا اور ان کے مالوں کو ساتھ لیکر حضور کے پاس آئے تو آپ نے فرمایا اسلام تو قبول ہے۔ لیکن مال دھو کے کا ہے اس لئے مجھے اس کی ضرورت نہیں۔ اور آپ نے اس میں سے شمس لینے سے بھی انکار کر دیا۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ اس کی ملکیت محظور ہے۔ پھر آپ نے اس مال کو مالک کے ورثہ کی طرف واپس کرنے کا حکم نہیں دیا۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ مسلمان مالک ہو گیا (۲) پہلے گزر چکا ہے کہ مسلمان حربیوں کے مال کا مالک بن جائے تو وہ مالک ہو جاتا ہے کیونکہ وہ مال غنیمت کے درجے میں ہے۔ جس طرح حربی مسلمان کے مال کا مالک بن جائے تو مالک ہو جاتا ہے (۳) دار الحرب لے جا کر واپس کرنا بھی ایک مشکل کام ہے اس میں جان کا خطرہ ہے اس لئے بھی مسلمان کو مالک قرار دے دیا جائے گا۔ لیکن ملک صحیح نہیں ہے اس لئے مال کو صدقہ کرنے کا حکم دیا جائے گا۔
انت تعرض : عرض سے مشتق ہے چھیڑنا، غدر : دھوکا دینا، محظور : خبیث۔
And if the imam does not permit them [3049 (70)]: And if a Muslim enters Dar al-Harb as a trader, it is not permissible for him to touch any of their property or their blood. Then if he commits treachery against them and takes something, he owns it as a prohibited ownership. [Urdu explanation:] This issue is based on the principle that if one acts understanding the imam's intention, it is accepted and the action is permissible. And if the imam himself sends a detachment, there is khums in its spoils. This hadith proves it: from Abdullah ibn Umar that the Messenger of Allah used to give nafal to some of those he sent from the expeditions for themselves specifically, apart from the general division of the army, and khums is obligatory in all that. (Abu Dawud, chapter on nafal for the detachment going out from the army). In this hadith, khums was obligatory in the spoils of the entire expedition. 'Milla' is derived from 'man' meaning strength to prevent. (3049) (70) If a Muslim enters Dar al-Harb as a trader, it is not halal for him to touch property or life. Then if he commits treachery and takes something, he becomes the owner in a prohibited manner, and he will be ordered to give it in charity. Explanation: Going as a trader into Dar al-Harb means he went with aman (safety guarantee) that he will not violate the covenant. Therefore he should not commit treachery or deception, nor harm the lives or property of the harbis. And if he does treachery and brings their property to Dar al-Islam, he becomes the owner. But since he became owner through treachery, it is a prohibited ownership, and he will be ordered to give that property in charity. The proof for not doing so is this hadith: from Sulayman ibn Burayda from his father: When the Messenger of Allah appointed an amir over an army, he would say: 'Fight those who disbelieve in Allah. Wage war, but do not embezzle (taghullu), do not commit treachery (taghdaru), do not mutilate (tumaththilu), and do not kill children.' (Muslim, chapter on appointing amirs over armies and his advice on etiquettes of warfare, etc.; Abu Dawud, chapter on calling the polytheists). From this hadith it is understood that even in Dar al-Harb, one should not commit treachery or deception. And if one takes the property of harbis by treachery, the ownership is prohibited. Its proof is this hadith: from al-Miswar ibn Makhrama: The Messenger of Allah went out at the time of Hudaybiyya with thirteen hundred of his companions... And al-Mughira had accompanied some people in Jahiliyya, killed them and took their property, then came and accepted Islam. The Prophet said: 'As for Islam, we accept it; as for the property, it is the property of treachery, we have no need for it.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on peace treaties with the enemy; Bukhari, chapter on conditions in jihad and reconciliation with the people of war). This hadith shows that the property is prohibited ownership. Then he did not order returning the property to the heirs of the owner, which shows the Muslim became the owner. (2) It has passed before that if a Muslim becomes owner of the property of harbis, he becomes owner, because that property is in the status of ghanima. Just as if a harbi becomes owner of a Muslim's property, he becomes owner. (3) Taking it back to Dar al-Harb is also a difficult task involving danger to life, therefore the Muslim is deemed owner. But since the ownership is not valid (sahih), he is ordered to give the property in charity. 'Anta ta'rid' is from 'arad' meaning to touch; 'ghadr' means to deceive; 'mahzur' means impure/khabith.
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning a Muslim who enters Dar al-Harb as a trader and then commits treachery (ghadr) by taking enemy property. The author states the basic ruling: the Muslim becomes the owner, but it is a prohibited ownership (milk mahzur), and he is ordered to give it in charity (sadaqah). The commentary explains the underlying principle: entering as a trader implies a covenant of aman (safety), so treachery breaks that covenant. The proof is provided from two hadiths: first, the Prophet's general prohibition of ghadr in warfare (from Sulayman ibn Burayda), and second, the specific incident of al-Mughira who killed his companions in Jahiliyya and took their property; after embracing Islam, the Prophet accepted his Islam but rejected the property, calling it 'mal ghadr' (property of treachery). The author explains that this indicates the Muslim becomes owner (since the Prophet did not order return to the heirs) but the property is not pure and must be given in charity. The Hanafi position is that such ownership is valid in the sense of possession but not lawful for personal use; it must be disposed of by charity. This aligns with the broader Hanafi principle that property taken by treachery becomes the taker's property but is prohibited consumption, analogous to ghanima but without the khums. The passage also notes that returning property to Dar al-Harb is dangerous, justifying the ruling of ownership.

Key Terms
غدر (ghadr): To break a covenant or promise; specifically, to betray or deceive after having given assurance of safety (aman).
ملك محظور (milk mahzur): Ownership that is legally valid (the person takes possession and becomes owner) but the property is prohibited for consumption or use; it must be given in charity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on a Muslim who enters Dar al-Harb as a trader and then treacherously takes property from harbis?
A) The property is halal ghanima and he may keep it.
B) He becomes the owner but must give it in charity.
C) He must return the property to its original owners in Dar al-Harb.
D) He is not considered the owner and the property goes to the state treasury.

Key Takeaway
A Muslim who treacherously takes property while under aman becomes the owner but must give it in charity, because the ownership is milk mahzur.

Ruling on a Harbi Musta'min Staying a Year and Becoming Dhimmi
Ruling with proof for a harbi musta'min staying a full year in Dar al-Islam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a harbi musta'min completes one year in Dar al-Islam and identify the Quranic proof for this ruling.

Core Idea
A musta'min's aman is limited to one year; a full year triggers dhimmi status and jizya.

A harbi (enemy combatant) may enter Dar al-Islam temporarily with aman (safe conduct). But what happens if he stays for a full year? The Hanafi school rules that he automatically becomes a dhimmi and must pay jizya. This lesson examines the ruling and its evidence from the Quran and Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a harbi musta'min residing in Dar al-Islam for one complete year. The ruling is that he becomes a dhimmi and jizya becomes wajib upon him.
The imam must warn him beforehand.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The author cites Quran 9:28 which declares polytheists as najis (impure) and prohibits them from approaching the Sacred Mosque after that year.
This is extended to all of Dar al-Islam by analogy.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The verse's implication (mafhum) is that mushrikun should not be allowed to reside permanently in Muslim territory; a one-year stay is considered permanent in legal effect.
The commentary uses this to justify the one-year limit.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools may allow longer stays or have different conditions for dhimmi status. The Hanafi position is that the year is a decisive limit.
Cross-madhhab reference: other schools might not automatically impose dhimmi status.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is well-established in fiqh and is the mufta bihi. The ruling balances security concerns with the need for trade.
The prohibition of permanent residence is supported by the hadith to expel polytheists from Arabia.

The polytheist is impure, so do not let them approach the Sacred Mosque after this year. (b): He ordered the companions with three things, one of which is to expel the polytheists from the Arabian Peninsula.

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling concerning a harbi (enemy combatant) who enters Dar al-Islam as a musta'min (one seeking temporary safety/aman). The core ruling: such a person cannot be allowed to stay for a complete year. The imam must warn him that if he completes a year, jizya will be imposed upon him, and he will become a dhimmi (protected non-Muslim subject). Once he becomes a dhimmi, he is not permitted to return to Dar al-Harb. The commentary explains the rationale: prolonged stay could enable espionage and harm to Dar al-Islam; however, some flexibility is needed for trade, so short stays are allowed but not a full year. The proof is drawn from the Quranic verse declaring polytheists as najis (impure) and the hadith ordering their expulsion from the Arabian Peninsula. The reference to 'Umar's practice of allowing a three-day stay for traders further supports the restriction on long-term residence. The initial part of the text (before the second (71)) appears to be a repetition or misplacement of the previous lesson's commentary; the actual lesson material for this ruling is the section after the second (71) heading. The Hanafi position is that a musta'min cannot stay beyond one year; if he does, he becomes a dhimmi with the obligation of jizya and cannot leave.

Key Terms
مستأمن (musta'min): A non-Muslim (harbi) who enters Dar al-Islam with a temporary safe conduct (aman) for a specific purpose such as trade.
جزیہ (jizyah): A tax imposed on non-Muslims (dhimmis) in exchange for protection and exemption from military service.
ذمی (dhimmi): A non-Muslim subject living under the protection of the Islamic state, obligated to pay jizyah and subject to Islamic laws.

Ruling on Property Taken from a Harbi by Killing
Explains ruling with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on property taken from a harbi by killing and explain why the Muslim must give it in charity.

Core Idea
Acquisition by treachery invalidates ownership — the property must be given in charity.

This passage clarifies a nuanced ruling in the law of jihad: when a Muslim kills a harbi (enemy combatant) through deception or treachery and takes his property, the Muslim does become the legal owner, but the ownership is defective. The Prophet ﷺ's rejection of such property in the hadith of Mughirah ibn Shu'bah establishes that the property is not halal for personal use. However, practical difficulties prevent return, so charity is commanded.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a Muslim killing a harbi and taking his property. The ruling is that the Muslim becomes owner but must give it in charity (makruh tahrimi).
The ownership is considered sahih in terms of transfer but not halal for consumption.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith of Mughirah ibn Shu'bah, where the Prophet ﷺ refused to accept property taken by treachery.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but sufficient for establishing the ruling.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's refusal indicates the property is not permissible (mahzur). His failure to order return to the original owners implies ownership transfers to the Muslim, but the prohibition remains.
The key point: ownership transfers but is flawed due to the means of acquisition.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some scholars hold the property is lawful as spoils of war (ghanimah), but the Hanafi school distinguishes because of the element of treachery (khida').
The Hanafi position relies on the specific prohibition in the hadith.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The mufta bihi position is that the Muslim must give it in charity. This balances the prohibition with practical impossibility of return.
The ruling reconciles the hadith's implication with the principle that the Muslim gains ownership through conquest.

And he is ordered to give it in charity. [13050(7)] And if a harbi enters our land as a musta'min, it is not possible for him to stay in our land for a year. The imam says to him: 'If you stay a full year, I will impose jizyah on you.' If he stays a year... Hadith: Mughirah ibn Shu'bah deceived and killed his polytheist companions and brought their wealth to the Prophet. Commentary
This passage deals with the ruling on a Muslim who kills a harbi (enemy combatant) and takes his property. The author cites the hadith of Mughirah ibn Shu'bah to show that such property is not halal for the Muslim; the Prophet refused it. However, since returning it to the harbi's heirs is impractical and dangerous, the Muslim is considered owner but is ordered to give it in charity. This is because the property is considered like ghanimah (spoils) in some respects, but the mode of acquisition (treachery) makes it objectionable. The ruling balances between prohibiting unlawful acquisition and practical difficulty.

Key Terms
محظور (mahẓūr): Forbidden or impure; used to describe ownership that is not legitimate.
مستأمن (musta’min): A harbi who enters Dar al-Islam with a temporary safe conduct (aman).
حربي (ḥarbī): An enemy combatant from Dar al-Harb.

Harbi Entering with Aman and Staying One Year
Ruling with proof on harbi musta'min after one year

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a harbi musta'min who stays one year in Dar al-Islam and identify the proofs for the imposition of jizyah.

Core Idea
One year's stay transforms a musta'min into a dhimmi with jizyah obligation.

A harbi (enemy non-Muslim) who enters Dar al-Islam with temporary safe conduct (aman) does not automatically become a permanent resident. However, if he remains for a full year, his status changes: he becomes a dhimmi (protected subject) and incurs the obligation of jizyah. This lesson examines that ruling, its practical conditions, and the evidence from the practice of Umar and the hadith of Mu'adh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a harbi musta'min staying in Dar al-Islam for one year. The ruling: he becomes a dhimmi and jizyah is wajib on him.
The one-year period is counted from the day of entry without leaving.
2
Locate the first proof: athar of Umar
Umar wrote to Ziyad ibn Hudayr: if a harbi stays six months, take a tenth (usher); if a year, take a twentieth (half a tenth). The difference in rate reveals the status change.
Six months = harbi (tenth), one year = dhimmi (twentieth).
3
Locate the second proof: hadith of Mu'adh
The Prophet commanded Mu'adh in Yemen to take one dinar (or its equivalent) from every adult. This establishes jizyah on dhimmis universally.
The hadith is ahad but accepted in practice.
4
Apply the ruling to the musta'min's situation
The imam warns the musta'min before the year ends. If he stays a full year, he becomes a dhimmi and cannot return to Dar al-Harb. Jizyah is one dinar per year, and on trade goods he pays 1/20 (kharaj), while a Muslim pays 1/40 (zakat).
The dhimmi's obligation is permanent; he must reside in Dar al-Islam.

And if a harbi enters our land as a musta'min, it is not possible for him to stay in our land for a year. The imam says to him: 'If you stay a full year, I will impose jizyah on you.' If he stays a year, jizyah is taken from him, and he becomes a dhimmi, and he is not allowed to return to Dar al-Harb... and their needs, and none of them may stay more than three nights (al-Bayhaqi). This athar states that Christians and Magians should not stay more than three days. And if he stays a year, he will be made a dhimmi. The proof is this athar: Ziyad ibn Hudayr said: I wrote to Umar about some people from the people of war who enter our land, the land of Islam, and stay. He wrote back: If they stay six months, take a tenth from them; if they stay a year, take a twentieth. (al-Bayhaqi). This athar indicates that if a harbi stays a year, half a tenth (i.e., one-twentieth) is imposed on him. And one-twentieth is taken from a dhimmi, while one-tenth is taken from a harbi. So staying a year makes him a dhimmi. The dhimmi must remain in Dar al-Islam permanently; he is not allowed to return to Dar al-Harb. Jizyah is obligatory on the head of the dhimmi, which is one dinar per year, and on his trade goods, one-twentieth kharaj is due, while Muslims pay one-fortieth zakah. The proof for jizyah is the hadith of Mu'adh: The Prophet sent him to Yemen and ordered him to take from every adult (mukhtalim) a dinar or its equivalent in Ma'afiri garments. (Abu Dawud, Bukhari).
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage deals with the legal status of a harbi (enemy non-Muslim) who enters Dar al-Islam with a temporary safe-conduct (aman). The imam warns him that if he stays a full year, jizyah will be imposed and he will become a dhimmi (protected non-Muslim subject). The ruling is based on practical considerations: prolonged stay allows espionage and harm, but trade requires some flexibility. The proofs include the athar of Umar differentiating between six months (harbi) and one year (dhimmi), and the hadith of Mu'adh establishing jizyah on dhimmis. The dhimmi status is permanent; he cannot return to Dar al-Harb. On his trade, he pays one-twentieth (half a tenth), whereas a harbi pays one-tenth, and a Muslim pays one-fortieth as zakah.

Key Terms
مستأمن (musta’min): A harbi who enters Dar al-Islam with temporary safe conduct (aman).
جزية (jizyah): Annual poll tax imposed on dhimmis in exchange for protection and exemption from military service.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He must leave immediately
B) He becomes a dhimmi and pays jizyah
C) He pays a one-time tax and stays as musta'min
D) He is expelled by force

Key Takeaway
A harbi musta'min who stays one continuous year in Dar al-Islam becomes a dhimmi wajib al-jizyah and permanently bound to Dar al-Islam.

Harbi Returning to Dar al-Harb After Becoming Dhimmi: Loss of Protection
Ruling on dhimmi returning to Dar al-Harb: blood mubah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that a dhimmi who returns to Dar al-Harb without permission loses protection and his blood becomes mubah, and identify the condition that triggers this ruling.

Core Idea
A dhimmi who returns to Dar al-Harb without permission breaches the covenant; his blood becomes permissible to kill.

This lesson addresses a critical boundary of the dhimmi contract: residence in Dar al-Islam is a condition of protection. The Hanafi school holds that if a dhimmi voluntarily returns to Dar al-Harb, he repudiates the covenant, making his blood and property mubah (permissible). This ruling underscores the binding nature of the dhimma and the consequences of its breach.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and ruling
The passage states: a dhimmi who returns to Dar al-Harb and leaves an amanah or debt with a Muslim or dhimmi — his blood becomes mubah (permissible to kill).
The ruling applies only if the return is voluntary and without permission from the Muslim ruler.
2
Understand the legal basis
The dhimma (covenant of protection) is conditional on residence in Dar al-Islam. By returning to Dar al-Harb, the dhimmi effectively abandons the covenant, nullifying his protected status.
This is based on the principle that the dhimmi must remain in Dar al-Islam to enjoy security.
3
Note the effect on property
In addition to his blood becoming mubah, any property he left as a trust or debt with Muslims also becomes mubah (not subject to return).
This prevents claims from the departed dhimmi or his heirs.
4
Compare with other positions
Some scholars (e.g., Shafi'i) hold that the dhimmi remains protected unless he takes up arms against Muslims. The Hanafi view is stricter, based on the condition of residence.
The practical difference: under Hanafi, mere return to Dar al-Harb forfeits protection; under Shafi'i, only active combat does.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Commentary
This passage, though partly overlapping with the previous lesson, focuses on the consequence for a dhimmi who returns to Dar al-Harb. The key point is that by returning, he breaches the covenant of protection (dhimma). His blood becomes mubah, meaning Muslims may kill him without legal consequence. Additionally, any property he left as a trust or debt with Muslims becomes mubah (not subject to return). This underscores the binding nature of the dhimmi contract: leaving Dar al-Islam without permission nullifies the protection.

Key Terms
مباح (mubāḥ): Permissible; here applied to blood, meaning killing is allowed without liability.

Key Takeaway
A dhimmi who returns to Dar al-Harb without permission forfeits protection; his blood and left property become mubah.

Ruling on Sawad Land as Kharaj Land and Its Sale
Explaining that all of Sawad is kharaj land owned by its people

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the ownership of Sawad (kharaj) land and explain the evidence from the practice of the Companions.

Core Idea
Sawad land is owned by its original inhabitants and may be sold; the kharaj tax does not change ownership.

This passage from Kitab al-Siyar clarifies a foundational Hanafi ruling about conquered lands. It establishes that the fertile Sawad region of Iraq remains in the hands of its original owners with a kharaj tax, contrary to the view that all conquered land becomes state property. The author provides historical evidence from the actions of Caliph Umar and the advice of Ali to support this position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The matn states: 'All of Sawad is kharaj land... The land of Sawad is owned by its people; their sale of it and their disposal of it are permissible.' Note the ruling: land is owned by inhabitants, sale is permissible.
The ruling is specific to Sawad, but the principle applies to similar conquered lands treated as kharaj.
2
Analyse the first proof: Ibn Sirin's statement
Ibn Sirin distinguishes between sulh (peace) and anwatan (force) conquests. For treaty land, the property remains with the owners. The matn does not specify the proportion, but the implication is that even forcible conquest did not remove ownership in Sawad due to Umar's policy.
Consider how this proof supports ownership: by categorizing parts as sulh, those parts are clearly owned. For anwatan parts, the proof is supplemented by Umar's practice.
3
Analyse the second proof: Umar's consultation and Ali's advice
Umar wanted to divide the people of Sawad as war booty, but Ali advised leaving them as a material resource (maddah) for Muslims. Umar accepted and imposed kharaj instead. This shows the land remained with its original inhabitants.
The key here is the Companions' consensus (or near-consensus) on this policy.
4
Understand the distinction between sulh and anwatan
The passage clarifies that Sawad included both types of conquest. The Hanafi position holds that even land conquered by force may, by the Imam's decision, be left with its people subject to kharaj, as Umar did.
This differentiates from the Shafi'i view that forcible conquest automatically makes land state property (fay').
5
Recognise the practical difference (thamarah)
The practical effect is that owners can sell, inherit, and dispose of the land freely. The kharaj continues as a tax on the land itself, not on the owner's religion.
This is the mufta bihi position for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والسواد كلها ارض خراج وهى ما بين العذيب الى عقبة حلوان ومن الثعلبة ويقال ومن العلث الى عبادان وارض السواد مملوكة لاهلها يجوز بيعهم لها وتصرفهم فيها. عن ابن سيرين قال السواد منه صلح ومنه عنوة، فما كان منه عنوة فهو للمسلمين وما كان منه صلح فلهم اموالهم. عن عمر انه اراد ان يقسم اهل السواد بين المسلمين وامر بهم ان يحصوا فوجدوا الرجل المسلم يصيبه ثلاثة من الفلاحين يعنى العلوج فشاور اصحاب النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في ذلك فقال علي دعهم يكونون مادة للمسلمين فبعث عثمان بن حنيف فوضع عليهم ثمانية واربعين واربعة وعشرين واثنى عشر
All of Sawad is kharaj land, and it is what is between al-Udhaib and Uqbat Hulwan, and from al-Tha'labah, and it is said from al-'Alth to 'Abbadan. The land of Sawad is owned by its people; their sale of it and their disposal of it are permissible. From Ibn Sirin: 'Sawad includes that conquered by peace and that conquered by force. Whatever was conquered by force is for the Muslims, and whatever was conquered by peace, their property is theirs.' From Umar: He wanted to divide the people of Sawad among the Muslims and ordered them to be counted. They found that a Muslim man would receive three peasants, meaning the 'ilj (uncultured), so he consulted the Companions of the Prophet (peace be upon him) about that. Ali said: 'Leave them; they will be a source of material for the Muslims.' So he sent Uthman ibn Hunayf and he imposed upon them forty-eight, twenty-four, and twelve [dirhams].
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Siyar clarifies the status of Sawad land (cultivated land in Iraq). The matn states that all of Sawad is kharaj land, defined by specific boundaries. It is owned by its original inhabitants, and they are permitted to sell it and dispose of it. The commentary then provides two proofs: (1) The athar of Ibn Sirin, which explains that Sawad was conquered partly by peace treaty (sulh) and partly by force (anwatan). The forcibly conquered part became spoils for the Muslims, while the peace treaty part remained in the owners' hands. (2) The story of Umar al-Khattab, who initially considered dividing the conquered inhabitants as slaves among the Muslims, but accepted Ali's advice to leave them as a productive workforce (maddah), imposing a fixed kharaj tax of varying amounts. This establishes that the land remains owned by its people, with tax upon it, and they may sell it.

Key Terms
سواد (Sawad): The cultivated black land of Iraq, specifically the region between al-Udhaib, Uqbat Hulwan, al-Tha'labah, and 'Abbadan.
خراج (kharaj): A land tax imposed on non-Muslim inhabitants of conquered lands, paid annually on the land itself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Sawad land is owned by its original inhabitants and may be sold; the kharaj tax is a levy on the land, not on the owner's person or faith.

When Land Becomes 'Ushr Land: Scenarios and Proofs
Stating the two scenarios for 'ushr land and providing proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two scenarios under which land becomes 'ushr land according to the Hanafi school and explain the proofs from the hadith of al-Ala' ibn al-Hadrami and the athar of Abdullah ibn Umar.

Core Idea
Land becomes 'ushr when its people accept Islam or when conquered by force and distributed; Islam removes kharaj.

This ruling addresses when agricultural land is subject to 'ushr (the tithe) instead of kharaj (land tax). The Hanafi school identifies two clear scenarios: the inhabitants' conversion to Islam while owning the land, or the land being conquered by force and then divided among the fighters. The passage provides three proofs—a prophetic hadith, a caliphal decree, and a companion's statement—to establish that a Muslim cannot be burdened with kharaj, which implies humiliation.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling and its two scenarios
Read the matn: every land whose people accept Islam, or which is conquered by force and divided, is 'ushr land. Identify these as the only two paths to becoming 'ushri land.
These are mutually exclusive: either conversion or conquest+division.
2
Analyze the hadith of al-Ala' ibn al-Hadrami
The Prophet sent al-Ala' to Bahrain. In a shared garden, he took 'ushr from the Muslim partner and kharaj from the polytheist. This shows that the same plot of land can have different obligations based on the owner's faith, and that conversion removes kharaj.
The hadith is ahad (zanni thubut) but accepted in practice.
3
Examine the athar of Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz
The caliph wrote that there is no kharaj on a person who accepts Islam from among the people of the land. This confirms that conversion extinguishes the kharaj obligation.
This is a ruling from a caliph, though not from the Prophet.
4
Understand the athar of Abdullah ibn Umar
Ibn Umar said a Muslim should not voluntarily assume kharaj (by buying or renting kharaj land) because it involves humiliation (dhull wa saghar). This indicates that while the purchase is valid, it is disliked (makruh tahrimi).
The kharaj remains on the land, but the Muslim is discouraged from entering such a transaction.
5
Derive the practical implications
A Muslim cannot be forced to pay kharaj; if he inherits or buys kharaj land, he must pay kharaj but it is makruh. The land itself keeps its 'kharaji' status unless the inhabitants convert or it is conquered and divided.
This distinguishes between the tax status of the land and the personal obligation of the owner.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و کل ارض اسلم اهلها عليها او فتحت عنوةً وقسمت بين الغانمين فهى ارض عشر. عن العلاء بن الحضرمي قال بعثني رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم الى البحرين او الى هجر فكنت آتي الحائط يكون بين الاخوة يسلم احدهم فآخذ من المسلم العشر ومن المشرك الخراج. كتب عمر بن عبد العزيز الى عبد الحميد بن عبد الرحمن فذكره فقال فيه ولا خراج على من اسلم من اهل الارض. عن نافع ان عبد الله بن عمر كان اذا سئل عن الرجل من اهل الاسلام يأخذ الارض من اهل الذمة بما عليها من الخراج يقول لا يحل لمسلم او لا ينبغى لمسلم ان يكتب على نفسه الذل والصغار
Every land whose people accept Islam upon it, or which is conquered by force and divided among the spoils-takers, is 'ushr land. From al-'Ala' ibn al-Hadrami: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) sent me to Bahrain or to Hajar, and I used to come to a garden that was between two brothers; one of them becomes Muslim, so I would take the tithe from the Muslim and the kharaj from the polytheist. Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz wrote to Abd al-Hamid ibn Abd al-Rahman, mentioning it, and said: 'There is no kharaj upon whoever accepts Islam among the people of the land.' From Nafi': Abdullah ibn Umar, when asked about a Muslim man taking land from the people of the dhimma with the kharaj upon it, said: 'It is not permissible for a Muslim, or it is not befitting for a Muslim, to write upon himself humiliation and lowliness.'
Source pages p. 304

Commentary
This passage from the same chapter establishes the rule for when land becomes tithable ('ushr) rather than kharaj land. The matn states that there are two cases: (1) The inhabitants become Muslim while still living on the land; (2) The land is conquered by force and then divided among the fighters (ghazis) as part of the spoils. In both cases, the land is 'ushr land, meaning only the Islamic tithe (one-tenth or half-tenth) is levied on its produce, not kharaj. The commentary provides three proofs: First, the hadith of al-'Ala' ibn al-Hadrami, who was sent by the Prophet to Bahrain. He would take 'ushr from a Muslim partner and kharaj from a non-Muslim partner in the same garden. This shows that Islam removes kharaj. Second, the letter of Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz explicitly stating that no kharaj is due from a Muslim who converts from among the land's people. Third, the statement of Ibn Umar that a Muslim should not voluntarily assume kharaj (by renting or buying kharaj land from dhimmis) because it involves humiliation (dhull wa saghar). Thus, a Muslim cannot be forced to pay kharaj; if he acquires kharaj land, he continues to pay kharaj but it is considered disliked (makruh) because of the humiliation factor.

Key Terms
عشر ('ushr): A tithe of one-tenth or one-twentieth of the produce of agricultural land, levied on Muslims as a religious obligation.
عنوةً (anwatan): By force of arms, i.e., conquest without a peace treaty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following correctly describes the ruling on a Muslim purchasing kharaj land?
A) The purchase is invalid because a Muslim cannot own kharaj land.
B) The land becomes 'ushr land immediately upon purchase.
C) The land remains kharaj land and the Muslim must pay kharaj; the purchase is valid but makruh tahrimi.
D) The kharaj is halved for Muslim owners.

Key Takeaway
Land becomes 'ushr only through the inhabitants' Islam or conquest with division; a Muslim should not voluntarily assume kharaj.

Conditions for Land Becoming 'Ushri
Ruling with proof from hadith and athar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions under which land becomes 'ushri according to the Hanafi school and identify the proofs from hadith and athar.

Core Idea
Muslim ownership or conversion removes kharaj and imposes 'ushr on land.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on when land is classified as 'ushri (liable to tithe) rather than kharaji (liable to land tax). The source passage provides two scenarios and supports them with a hadith and an athar. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying the rules of agricultural taxation in Islamic jurisprudence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The text states two ways land becomes 'ushri: (a) the inhabitants embrace Islam, or (b) the land is conquered by force (ʿanwatan) and divided among the mujahideen.
2
State the ruling
In both cases, the land is classified as 'ushri, meaning one-tenth of its produce is due as tax ('ushr).
3
Locate the proof from hadith
The hadith of al-ʿAlaʾ ibn al-Ḥaḍrami shows the Prophet instructed: take 'ushr from Muslims and kharaj from polytheists.
This indicates that Muslim-owned land is subject to 'ushr, not kharaj.
4
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith differentiates based on the religion of the owner, establishing a direct link between Muslim ownership and 'ushr.
5
Consider the athar of ʿUmar ibn ʿAbd al-ʿAzīz
The caliph's letter states no kharaj on a Muslim from the people of the land, reinforcing that conversion cancels kharaj and imposes 'ushr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و كل ارض اسلم اهلها عليها او فتحت عنوةً وقسمت بين الغانمين فهى ارض عشر. عن العلاء بن الحضرمي قال بعثني رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إلى البحرين أو إلى هجر فكنت آتي الحائط يكون بين الأخوة يسلم أحدهم فآخذ من المسلم العشر ومن المشرك الخراج. وكتب عمر بن عبد العزيز إلى عبد الحميد بن عبد الرحمن فقال فيه لا خراج على من أسلم من أهل الأرض.
And every land whose inhabitants embrace Islam, or is conquered by force and divided among the gainers, it is 'ushri land. From al-'Ala' ibn al-Hadrami: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) sent me to Bahrain or to Hajar, so I used to come to a garden that is between brothers; one of them becomes Muslim, so I take from the Muslim the 'ushr and from the polytheist the kharaj. And 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz wrote to 'Abd al-Hamid ibn 'Abd al-Rahman saying in it: There is no kharaj on whoever among the people of the land becomes Muslim.
Source pages p. 304

Commentary
This passage states a ruling regarding the classification of land as 'ushri (subject to tithe) in the Hanafi school. The ruling covers two scenarios: (a) the inhabitants of a land voluntarily embrace Islam, or (b) the land is conquered by force (ʿanwatan) and then distributed among the mujahideen. In both cases, the land becomes 'ushri. The author then provides evidence: first, a hadith from al-ʿAlaʾ ibn al-Haḍrami where the Prophet instructed him to take ʿushr from Muslims and kharaj from polytheists, indicating a distinction based on religion. Second, an athar from Caliph ʿUmar ibn ʿAbd al-ʿAziz stating that no kharaj is due from a Muslim who is among the people of the land. This supports the principle that Muslim ownership or conversion removes kharaj and imposes ʿushr. The Hanafi position is that initially, a Muslim's land is not subject to kharaj because kharaj is a form of humiliation (dhull) inappropriate for a Muslim. Further commentary notes that if a land's inhabitants convert before kharaj is fixed, it becomes ʿushri; if after, the existing kharaj may remain on the land even if sold to a Muslim, but initially no kharaj is imposed on a Muslim.

Key Terms
عشر (ʿushr): A tithe of one-tenth of agricultural produce, levied on lands classified as 'ushri.
خراج (kharāj): A land tax levied on kharaji lands, usually a fixed amount per unit area.
عنوة (ʿanwatan): Conquest by force, as opposed to sulhan (peaceful surrender).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what are two ways a land becomes 'ushri?
A) Inhabitants embrace Islam, or land is conquered by force and divided among mujahideen.
B) Land is conquered peacefully, or it is inherited by a Muslim.
C) Inhabitants pay jizyah, or land is purchased by a Muslim.
D) Land is conquered by force and left to inhabitants, or it is revived from dead land.

Key Takeaway
Land becomes 'ushri when its inhabitants embrace Islam or when conquered by force and divided among the mujahideen.

Kharaji Land: Ruling and Proof from 'Umar's Practice
Ruling with implicit proof from practice of 'Umar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on force-conquered land left to its inhabitants and identify the evidence from 'Umar and the hadith.

Core Idea
Force-conquered land left to non-Muslim inhabitants is kharaji, not 'ushri.

This lesson examines the second major classification of conquered land in Hanafi law. When a land is conquered by force ('anwatan) and its original inhabitants are allowed to remain, it becomes kharaji land, meaning the kharaj tax is imposed on it. The ruling is supported by the actions of Caliph 'Umar, who imposed kharaj on the Sawad of Iraq, and by a hadith of the Prophet instructing the collection of kharaj from polytheists.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
State the classification: land conquered by force and left to its inhabitants is kharaji land. Understand that 'kharaji' means subject to the kharaj tax, not 'ushr.
Contrast with 'ushri land, which is distributed among Muslims.
2
Locate the Evidence
The passage cites two proofs: the action of 'Umar (radi Allahu 'anhu) on the Sawad of Iraq, and the hadith of al-'Ala' ibn al-Hadrami. Recognize that both are used as dalil.
The hadith is shared across schools but interpreted differently.
3
Analyze the Hadith
In the hadith, the Prophet says: 'I take from the Muslim the 'ushr and from the polytheist the kharaj.' The word 'kharaj' here is taken as a command to impose kharaj on non-Muslims for land they hold, implying that such land is kharaji.
The Hanafi understanding emphasizes the distinction between Muslim and non-Muslim taxpayers.
4
Consider the Cross-Madhhab Difference
Some schools, notably the Shafi'i school, may classify such land as fay' (spoils) and subject it to 'ushr instead of kharaj. Recognize that this is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on differing usul.
The Hanafi position relies on 'Umar's practice as a precedent (qawl al-sahabi).
5
Apply to a New Scenario
Given a scenario where a land is conquered by force and its inhabitants remain, apply the Hanafi ruling: it is kharaji, so kharaj is wajib. Contrast with land distributed among mujahideen, which is 'ushri.
Practical fatwa: the ruling affects landowners and tax collectors.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكل ارض فتحت عنوة فأقراهلها عليها فهي ارض خراج. ويدل عليه فعل عمر رضي الله عنه حيث أقر الخراج على سواد العراق. وأيضا حديث العلاء بن الحضرمي السابق: فآخذ من المسلم العشر ومن المشرك الخراج.
And every land conquered by force and its inhabitants are left upon it, it is kharaji land. Evidence for this is the action of 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) when he imposed kharaj on the Sawad of Iraq. Also the previous hadith of al-'Ala' ibn al-Hadrami: I take from the Muslim the 'ushr and from the polytheist the kharaj.
Source pages p. 304

Commentary
This passage states the second major classification: land that is conquered by force ('anwatan) but its inhabitants are allowed to remain on it (i.e., not expelled or enslaved) is kharaji land, meaning it is subject to the kharaj tax. The proof offered is the historical practice of Caliph 'Umar (radi Allahu 'anhu), who imposed kharaj on the Sawad (agricultural region) of Iraq after its conquest, while leaving the non-Muslim inhabitants in place. Additionally, the hadith from al-'Ala' ibn al-Hadrami is referenced: the Prophet distinguished between taking 'ushr from Muslims and kharaj from polytheists. Since the inhabitants here are non-Muslim (dhimmi), kharaj is taken from them. The Hanafi ruling is that kharaj is a form of land tax that compensates for the protection and use of the land, and it is not appropriate to impose it on Muslims initially. The text mentions that 'ushr is an act of worship (ibadah) and non-Muslims are not qualified for it, so they must pay kharaj instead.

Key Terms
خراج (kharāj): Land tax levied on non-Muslims for land they cultivate, often fixed annually.
عشر (ushr): A tithe or tenth payable on agricultural produce, typically by Muslims.
عنوة (anwatan): By force or conquest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this lesson, what makes a conquered land kharaji?
A) Its inhabitants are all Muslims.
B) It is conquered by force and left to its original inhabitants.
C) It is divided among the mujahideen.
D) Its inhabitants pay zakat.

Key Takeaway
Land conquered by force and left to its original non-Muslim inhabitants is classified as kharaji, obligating kharaj tax rather than 'ushr.

Revived Dead Land: Classification by Surrounding Area (Abu Yusuf)
Intra-Hanafi ruling on revived dead land classification by surrounding area (hayyiz)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Abu Yusuf's position on the classification of revived dead land and distinguish it from the views of other Hanafi authorities.

Core Idea
The revived land takes the tax status of its surrounding area, not the reviver's status.

This passage deals with the Hanafi ruling on the classification of revived dead land (mawat). Imam Abu Yusuf held a specific view that the classification depends on the surrounding land (hayyiz): if it lies within a kharaji area, it becomes kharaji; if within an 'ushri area, it becomes 'ushri. He explicitly considered Basra as 'ushri land. This lesson unpacks his reasoning and the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and legal issue
The act is reviving dead land (ihya al-mawat). The legal issue is determining its tax classification (kharaji vs 'ushri) after revival.
Dead land is ownerless, uncultivated land. Revival grants ownership but the tax status is contested.
2
State Abu Yusuf's ruling
According to Abu Yusuf, the classification is based on the surrounding area (hayyiz): if the land is within a kharaji zone, it is kharaji; if within an 'ushri zone, it is 'ushri.
The text uses the term 'hayyiz' which refers to the contiguous region.
3
Recognize the intra-Hanafi difference
Other Hanafi authorities (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani) may consider other factors, such as the water source or the method of irrigation, rather than solely the surrounding area.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.
4
Apply the rule to the example of Basra
Abu Yusuf explicitly states that Basra is 'ushri land. This implies that Basra's surrounding area is predominantly 'ushri, likely due to the consensus of the Companions or historical land classification.
Basra was founded on dead land by Muslims and never had kharaj imposed.
5
Note the authority level and practical application
This opinion is attributed specifically to Abu Yusuf and is considered from the nawadir (rare transmissions). Later Hanafi fatwa often follows Abu Yusuf's view in this matter.
The mufta bihi is not explicitly stated in the text, but Abu Yusuf's view is widely applied.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن احيا ارضا مواتا فهى عند ابي يوسف معتبرة بحيّزها فان كانت من حيز ارض الخراج فهى خراجيّة وان كانت من حيّز ارض العشر فهى عُشرية والبصرة عنده عشرية.
And whoever revives dead land, then according to Abu Yusuf it is considered by its surrounding area: if it is from the area of kharaji land, then it is kharaji; and if it is from the area of 'ushri land, then it is 'ushri. And Basra according to him is 'ushri.
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage presents the position of Imam Abu Yusuf (one of the major Hanafi authorities) regarding the classification of dead land (mawat) that is revived (ihya'). The general rule is that reviving dead land makes it owned by the reviver. However, its tax classification (whether 'ushri or kharaji) is determined by the surrounding area (hayyiz) where the land is located. If the land lies within a region that is predominantly kharaji, the revived plot becomes kharaji; if within an 'ushri region, it becomes 'ushri. The example given is the city of Basra: according to Abu Yusuf, Basra is 'ushri land due to the consensus of the Companions (ijma' al-sahaba) because it was founded on dead land by the Muslims and never had kharaj imposed. This ruling reflects Abu Yusuf's methodology of considering the legal status of the surrounding geography rather than, for example, the water source. The next part of the commentary (not in the Arabic) mentions that this is based on the principle that the dead land has no prior record, so its classification follows the adjacent lands.

Key Terms
الموات (al-mawāt): Dead land: uncultivated, ownerless land that has no known owner and is not under cultivation.
الحيز (al-ḥayyiz): The surrounding area or contiguous region that determines the legal classification of land.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Yusuf, how is revived dead land classified?
A) By the water source used for irrigation.
B) By the religion of the reviver.
C) By the surrounding area (hayyiz): kharaji if in kharaji zone, 'ushri if in 'ushri zone.
D) Always 'ushri because it is owned by a Muslim.

Key Takeaway
Abu Yusuf's ruling: the revived land's tax status is determined by its surrounding area (hayyiz), not the reviver's identity.
