Land Conquered by Force: Kharaj Land and Its Proof
Rule with proof for land conquered by force

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on land conquered by force (anwah) and identify its proof from the hadith of Ibn Majah and the practice of Umar.

Core Idea
Land conquered by force and left with its people is kharaj, not ushr — and kharaj drops if the owner converts to Islam.

This lesson examines a key ruling in the Hanafi law of conquest: the status of land taken by force (anwah) when the inhabitants are allowed to remain. The passage establishes that such land becomes kharaj land, subject to the land tax, and provides both textual proof and the precedent of Umar ibn al-Khattab. Understanding this ruling clarifies the Hanafi position on the distribution of conquered territory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the subject (land conquered by force) and the legal classification (kharaj land). Note that the ruling is declaratory (hukm wad'i), not a command.
The text states: 'Every land conquered by force and its inhabitants left on it is kharaj land.'
2
Locate the primary dalil
Find the cited hadith from Ibn Majah: 'Take ushr from the Muslim and kharaj from the polytheist.'
The hadith is narrated by Ala' ibn al-Hadrami and is ahad (zanni al-thubut).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the hadith implies kharaj on the land of non-Muslims. The distinction between ushr (for Muslims) and kharaj (for polytheists) indicates that kharaj is the tax for non-Muslim land.
The Hanafi usul principle: the explicit differentiation (takhsis) in the text is a valid indicator.
4
Note the companion practice
Examine the practice of Umar ibn al-Khattab in Iraq, where he left the conquered land with its people and imposed kharaj. This serves as corroborating evidence (amal al-sahabah).
The passage references Sunan al-Bayhaqi for this precedent.
5
Note the exception
Identify the footnote: if the landowner embraces Islam, the kharaj drops. This is based on the letter of Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz.
The ruling is not permanent; it is conditional on the inhabitants remaining non-Muslim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب السير
[۳۰۵۹ (۸۰) وكل ارض فتحت عنوة فأقراهلها عليها فهي ارض خراج [۳۰۶۰] (۸۱) ومن احيا ارضا مواتا فهى عند ابي يوسف معتبرة بحيّزها فان كانت من حيز ارض الخراج فهى خراجيّة وان كانت من حيّز ارض العشر فهى عُشرية والبصرة عنده عشرية
الـرحـمـن فـذكـره فقال فيه ولا خراج على من اسلم من اهل الارض (الف) سن لم يقی ، باب من اسلم من اهل الصلح سقط الخراج علی ارضه، ج تاسع، ص ۲۳۸، نمبر ۱۸۴۰۹) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ کوئی ملک والا مسلمان ہو جائے تو اس پر خراج نہیں ہے۔
(۱۳۰۵۹ (۸۰) جس زمین کو بزور طاقت فتح کیا ہو اور اس کے باشندے کو وہیں رکھا ہو تو وہ خراجی زمین ہے۔
کسی زمین کو طاقت سے فتح کیا یا رعب سے فتح کیا لیکن اس زمین کو مجاہدین کے درمیان تقسیم نہیں کی بلکہ اس پر کفار ہی کا قبضہ بحال رہنے دیا تو اس زمین پر خراج لازم ہوگا۔ عشر ایک قسم کی عبادت ہے اور کفار عبادت کا اہل نہیں ہے اس لئے ان پر خراج لازم ہوگا (۲) او پرابن ماجہ شریف کی حدیث گزری۔ عن العلاء بن الحضرمي ... فاخذ من المسلم العشر ومن المشرك الخراج (ب) (ابن ماجہ شریف ، باب العشر والخراج ص ۲۶۲ نمبر ۱۸۳) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مشرک کی زمین پر خراج ہے (۳) عراق کے لوگ مشرک تھے اور ان کو اس کی زمین پر بحال رکھا گیا تھا تو اس کی زمین پر حضرت عمرؓ نے خراج مقرر کیا۔ (سفن للبیہقی ، باب قدر الخراج الذي وضع على السواد، ج تاسع ، ص ۲۳۰، نمبر ۱۸۳۸۲)
حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت عمر بن عبد العزیز نے عبد الحمید بن عبد الرحمن کو لکھا اور اس میں یہ تذکرہ کیا کہ زمین والوں میں سے جو مسلمان ہو جائے اس پر خراج نہیں ہے (ب) علاء بن حضر می فرماتے ہیں۔ مسلمان سے عشر لیتا اور مشرک سے خراج۔
The Book of Siyar. [3059 (80)] Every land conquered by force and its inhabitants left on it is kharaj land. [3060] (81) Whoever revives dead land, according to Abu Yusuf, it is considered by its surrounding: if it is from the area of kharaj land, it is kharaji; if from the area of ushr land, it is ushri. And Basra according to him is ushri. al-Rahman mentioned him and said in it: There is no kharaj on whoever becomes Muslim from the people of the land. (a) [Urdu:] From this effect it is known that if a landowner becomes Muslim, there is no kharaj on him. (13059 (80)) A land conquered by force and its inhabitants kept there, that is kharaj land. A land conquered by force or by terror, but not divided among the mujahideen, and the disbelievers' possession is left, then kharaj is obligatory on that land. Ushr is a type of worship, and disbelievers are not eligible for worship, so kharaj is obligatory on them. (2) And the hadith of Ibn Majah passed: 'Ala' ibn al-Hadrami said: He took ushr from the Muslim and kharaj from the polytheist. (Ibn Majah, Bab al-Ushr wa al-Kharaj, p. 262 no. 183). From this hadith it is known that on the land of a polytheist there is kharaj. (3) The people of Iraq were polytheists and they were left on their land, so Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) fixed kharaj on their land. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab Qadr al-Kharaj, vol. 9 p. 230 no. 18382). Footnote: (a) Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz wrote to Abd al-Hamid ibn Abd al-Rahman, mentioning that whoever among the people of the land becomes Muslim, there is no kharaj on him. (b) Ala' ibn Hadrami said: He takes ushr from the Muslim and kharaj from the polytheist.
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the status of land conquered by force (anwah). The core ruling: any land taken by military force and left with its original inhabitants becomes kharaj land, subject to the land tax (kharaj). The commentary explains the reasoning: ushr is an act of worship, and disbelievers are not qualified for it, so instead kharaj is imposed. Proofs include the hadith of Ala' ibn Hadrami (narrated by Ibn Majah) that the Prophet took ushr from Muslims and kharaj from polytheists, and the practice of Umar ibn al-Khattab in Iraq. A footnote from Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz confirms that if the landowner converts to Islam, kharaj is dropped.

Key Terms
عنوة (anwah): By force; conquest through military power.
خراج (kharaj): Land tax levied on non-Muslim inhabitants of conquered lands left in their possession.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What proof does the text provide for imposing kharaj on land conquered by force?
A) The hadith: 'Take ushr from the Muslim and kharaj from the polytheist'
B) Consensus of the Companions
C) Analogy to ushr
D) The practice of the Umayyads

Key Takeaway
Land conquered by force is kharaj land unless the owner converts to Islam, in which case kharaj drops.

Reviving Dead Land: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Classification
Intra-Hanafi dispute on classifying revived dead land

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding the classification of revived dead land as ushri or kharaji, and identify the practical consequences (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
When reviving dead land, its tax status depends on either the surrounding land (Abu Yusuf) or the water source (Muhammad).

This passage presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute between two of the school's greatest imams: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Both agree that reviving dead land (ihya al-mawat) grants ownership, but they differ on how to classify the revived land for taxation purposes. Their disagreement turns on whether to consider the surrounding land's status or the water source used for irrigation.

Guided Path
1
State the two Hanafi positions
Identify the rulings of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on how to classify revived dead land.
Abu Yusuf looks at surrounding land; Muhammad looks at water source.
2
Examine Abu Yusuf's evidence
What proof does Abu Yusuf rely on? Consider the athar of Umar and the consensus of Companions on Basra.
He uses the athar: 'If it is not jizya land nor land to which jizya water flows...'
3
Examine Muhammad's evidence
What proof does Muhammad rely on? Consider the same athar but focusing on the water condition.
He emphasizes the 'jizya water' part of the athar.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Work out the practical difference. For example, in Basra, Abu Yusuf would classify most revived land as ushri, while Muhammad would classify based on water source.
This affects the owner's tax obligation: ushr vs kharaj.
5
Evaluate the tarjih and mufta bihi
Check which position is preferred in the school. The text does not give a final tarjih, but later Hanafi works often give more weight to Abu Yusuf's view.
This is an example of legitimate ikhtilaf within the madhhab.

حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت عمر بن عبد العزیز نے عبد الحمید بن عبد الرحمن کو لکھا اور اس میں یہ تذکرہ کیا کہ زمین والوں میں سے جو مسلمان ہو جائے اس پر خراج نہیں ہے (ب) علاء بن حضر می فرماتے ہیں۔ مسلمان سے عشر لیتا اور مشرک سے خراج۔

كتاب السير
باجماع الصحابة رضى الله عنهم [۳۰۶۱ (۸۲) وقال محمد رحمه الله تعالى ان احياها ببئر حفرها او بعين استخرجها او بماء دجلة او الفرات او الانهار العظام التي لا يملكها اصول مردہ زمین کی اصلیت کا اندازہ برابر کی زمین کس کی ملکیت ہے اس سے لگایا جائے گا۔ بصرہ ان کے یہاں عشری زمین ہے۔ اس کا اشارہ اس اثر سے ملتا ہے۔ عن محمد بن عبید الله الثقفي ، قال خرج رجل من اهل البصرة من ثقيف يقال له نافع ابو عبد الله، وكان اول من افتلا الفلا ، فقال لعمر بن الخطاب ان قبلنا ارضا بالبصرة ليست من ارض الخراج ولا تضر باحد من المسلمين فان رأيت ان تقطعنيها اتخذ فيها قضبا لخيلى فافعل، قال فكتب عمر الى ابى موسى الاشعرى ... فان لم تكن ارض جزية ولا ارضا يجرى اليها ماء جزية فاعطها اياه (الف) ( رواه عبید فی الاموال، ص ۲۷۷، اعلاء السنن، باب من احياء ارضنا مواتا بماء الخراج فخراجية والافعشریة ، ج الثانی عشر، ص ۲۲۵، نمبر ۴۰۹) اس اثر میں ہے کہ جزیہ کی زمین نہ ہو اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ بصرہ خراجی زمین نہیں تھی۔ اور یہ بھی معلوم ہوا کہ مردہ زمین میں خراجی پانی جائے تو وہ زمین بھی خراجی ہو جائے گی۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ اگلے مسئلے میں امام محمد کی رائے کہ جس پانی سے سیراب کیا جائے زمین وہی شمار کی جائینگی۔ اخت چیز : اردگرد، برابر کی زمین ۔
[۳۰۶۱ (۸۲) امام محمد نے فرمایا اگر زمین کو زندہ کیا کنواں کھود کر یا چشمہ نکال کر یا دجلہ یا فرات یا ان بڑی نہروں کے پانی سے جن کا کوئی مالک نہیں ہے تو وہ عشری ہے۔ اور اگر زندہ کیا ان نہروں کے پانی سے جن کو عجمیوں نے کھودا ہے جیسے نہر ملک اور نہریز دجر د تو وہ خراجی ہے۔ امام محمد کا قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ پانی کس قسم کا استعمال کرتا ہے اس کے اعتبار سے مردہ زمین خراجی یا عشری ہوگی۔ پس اگر خراجی پانی ڈال کر مردہ زمین کو زندہ کیا تو وہ زمین خراجی ہوگی چاہے وہ عشری زمین کے درمیان : و۔ اور اگر عشری پانی ڈال کر زندہ کیا تو وہ عشری ہوگی۔ آگے تفصیل ہے کہ کون سا پانی عشری ہے اور کون ساخراجی ہے۔
کسی نے خود کنواں کھودایا چشمہ نکالا تو ان دونوں کا پانی عشری ہے۔ اس سے مردہ زمین زندہ کیا تو زمین عشری ہوگی۔ یا نہر دجلہ، نہر فرات یا وہ نہر جن کا کوئی مالک نہیں اس کا پانی عشری ہے اس لئے اس پانی سے جو مردہ زمین زندہ کرے گا وہ عشری ہوگی۔
ے دو۔
اور وہ نہر جس کو عجمیوں نے کھودا ہو جیسے نہر ملک اور نہریز و جر دان کا پانی خراجی ہے۔ اس پانی سے مردہ زمین زندہ کرے گا تو وہ خراجی ہوگی۔ اوپر حضرت عمر کا اثر گزرا۔ فان لم تكن ارض جزية ولا ارضا يجرى اليها ماء جزية فاعطها اياه (ب)(رواه عبيد فى الاموال، ص ۷ ۲۷، اعلاء السفن، نمبر ۴۰۹ ) اس اثر میں ہے کہ بصرہ کی اس زمین میں جزیہ یعنی خراجی پانی نہ جاتا ہو تو نافع ابوعبید اللہ کو ۔ حاشیہ : (الف) محمد بن عبید اللہ فرماتے ہیں کہ بصرہ کا ایک آدمی ثقیف سے نکلا جس کا نام نافع ابو عبد اللہ تھا۔ یہ پہلا آدمی ہے جس نے جنگل میں میدان بنایا ۔ پس عمر بن خطاب سے کہا مجھ سے پہلے بصرہ میں خراجی زمین نہیں ہے اور مسلمانوں کو نقصان دیتی ہے۔ پس اگر مجھے زمین کچھ ٹکڑا دیں جس میں گھوڑے کے دوڑنے کی جگہ بناؤں تو کرلوں نے پس حضرت عمر نے حضرت ابو موسی اشعری کو لکھا. اگر جزیہ کی زمین نہ ہو اور نہ ایسی زمین ہو جس میں جزیہ کا پانی جاری ہوتا ہو تو اس کو عطا کر دو۔ (ب) اگر جزیہ کی زمین نہ ہو اور نہ اس میں جزیہ کا پانی جاری ہوتا ہو تو اس کو عطا کر دو۔
[3060 (81)] Whoever revives dead land: according to Imam Abu Yusuf, it is considered by its surrounding: if it is from the area of kharaj land, it is kharaji; if from the area of ushr land, it is ushri. And Basra according to him is ushri due to the consensus of the Companions. Then [Urdu:] When dead land is revived and cultivated, should it be declared ushri or kharaji? Imam Abu Yusuf's opinion is that it is not based on what water irrigates it, but on the type of land nearby. If near dead land there is kharaj land, this too is kharaji; if it is amidst ushr land, it is ushri. Since this land has no previous record, the type of country or area is considered. If nearby land is owned by mujahideen or Muslims, it means this dead land was also owned by mujahideen, so ushr is obligatory. If it remained in the possession of disbelievers due to which kharaj was obligatory, then this dead land is also to some extent owned by disbelievers, so kharaj should be obligatory. Footnote: (a) Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz ... (b) Ala' ibn Hadrami ... [PAGE_306] ... [3061 (82)] And Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) said: If he revives it by digging a well or extracting a spring or by water of Tigris, Euphrates, or the great rivers that no one owns, it is ushri. And if he revives it by water of rivers dug by non-Arabs like Nahr Malak and Nahr al-Dujayr, it is kharaji. [Urdu:] Imam Muhammad's principle is that depending on the type of water used, the revived land becomes kharaji or ushri. If kharaj water is used, it is kharaji even if amidst ushr land; if ushr water is used, it is ushri. Details follow on which water is ushri and which kharaji. He dug a well or spring: that water is ushri. Tigris, Euphrates, or ownerless rivers: their water is ushri. Rivers dug by non-Arabs like Nahr Malak and Nahr al-Dujayr: their water is kharaji. The athar of Umar passed: 'If it is not jizya land nor land to which jizya water flows, give it to him.'
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on how to classify revived dead land (ihya al-mawat) as either ushri (tithed) or kharaji (taxed). Imam Abu Yusuf holds that the classification depends on the surrounding land: if the dead land is near kharaj land, it becomes kharaji; if near ushr land, it becomes ushri. He cites the example of Basra, which he considers ushri due to consensus of the Companions. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, on the other hand, considers the water source as the determining factor: if the land is irrigated with water from a well, spring, or ownerless river (like Tigris, Euphrates), it is ushri; if irrigated with water from rivers dug by non-Arabs (which are considered kharaj water), it is kharaji. The commentary supports Abu Yusuf's view with an athar from Umar regarding a piece of land in Basra, indicating that the surrounding land's status and the type of water were considered. The footnote explains the athar in detail, narrating that Umar instructed Abu Musa al-Ash'ari to grant the land to the petitioner if it was not jizya land and not irrigated by jizya water.

Key Terms
مردہ زمین (mawat ardh): Dead land; uncultivated, ownerless land that is not in use.
عشری (ushri): Land subject to ushr (1/10 tithe) on agricultural produce, typically Muslim-owned land.
خراجی (kharaji): Land subject to kharaj (land tax), originally owned by non-Muslims or conquered by force.
اجماع صحابہ (ijma al-sahaba): Consensus of the Companions of the Prophet, considered a strong source of law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Yusuf, what determines whether revived dead land is ushri or kharaji?
A) The type of water used for irrigation
B) The surrounding land's status
C) The consent of the Imam
D) The religion of the reviver

Key Takeaway
The classification of revived dead land in the Hanafi school involves an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf between Abu Yusuf (surrounding land) and Muhammad (water source), with practical implications for taxation.

Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules

8 min
Ruling on Jizyah: Who Pays and Who Does Not
States the categories subject to jizyah with proofs and the view of Imam Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on which groups are subject to jizyah and which are exempt, and explain the proof for each category.

Core Idea
Jizyah is taken from People of the Book, Majus, and non-Arab polytheists—not from Arab polytheists or apostates.

The Hanafi school outlines clear categories for jizyah, supported by Quranic verses and prophetic practice. This lesson walks through the ruled groups, the evidence behind each, and a key disagreement with Imam al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories that must pay jizyah
List the three groups from whom jizyah is wajib according to the Hanafi school: People of the Book (Jews and Christians), Majus (Zoroastrians), and non-Arab idol worshippers.
These are the only groups from whom jizyah is accepted.
2
Locate the dalil for each category
For Ahl al-Kitab, the proof is Quran 9:29. For Majus, the proof is the hadith that the Prophet took jizyah from the Majus of Hajar. For non-Arab polytheists, the proof is the general command in the hadith to fight polytheists until they pay jizyah.
Each proof is specific and not interchangeable.
3
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how each proof directly yields the ruling. For example, Quran 9:29 uses the imperative 'قاتلوا' indicating obligation to fight until jizyah is given, implying its permissibility.
The generality of the verse is key.
4
Identify the exceptions and their proofs
Arab idol worshippers are exempt based on Quran 9:5 and the hadith 'Nothing is accepted from Arab polytheists except Islam or the sword.' Apostates are exempt because they must either repent or be executed.
These exceptions override any analogy.
5
Evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument and the Hanafi response
Imam al-Shafi'i allows jizyah from Arab polytheists by qiyas on Arab Ahl al-Kitab. The Hanafi school rejects this due to the specific prohibitory texts.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is whether Arab polytheists can remain as dhimmis.

ہے اس لئے عرب کے اہل کتاب پر بھی جزیہ مقرر کیا جا سکتا ہے۔ مجوسی سے جزیہ لینے کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ سمعت عمرا قال .... فاتانا كتاب عمر بن الخطاب قبل موته بسنة فرقوا بين كل ذي محرم من المجوس ولم يكن عمر جزیہ لیا جا سکتا ہے۔ حاشیہ : (الف) حضور نے جب حضرت معاذ کو یمن کی طرف متوجہ فرمایا تو ان کو حکم دیا کہ ہر بالغ سے ایک دینار لے۔ یا اس کے برابر معافری کپڑا جو یمن میں ہوتا ہے (ب) ان لوگوں سے جنگ کرے جو اللہ اور آخرت کے دن پر ایمان نہیں رکھتے۔ اور جس کو اللہ اور رسول نے حرام قرار دیا ہے اس کو حرام نہیں کرتے۔ اور اہل کتاب میں سے جو دین حق کو اختیار نہیں کرتے ان سے اس وقت تک جنگ کریں کہ ہاتھ سے ذلیل ہو کر جزیہ دینے لگیں ( ج ) ہمارے پاس عمر بن خطاب کا خط موت سے ایک سال پہلے آیا کہ مجوس کے ذی رقم محرم کی شادی ذی رحم محرم سے ہو گئی ہو تو اس کو جدا جدا کر دیں۔ اور حضرت عمر نے مجوس سے اس وقت تک جزیہ نہیں لیا جب تک کہ حضرت عبد الرحمن بن عوف نے گواہی نہیں دی کہ حضور نے ہجر کے مجوس سے جزیہ وصول فرمایا تھا ( د ) آپ نے اہل نجران سے دو ہزار صلے پر صلح فرمائی ، آدھا صفر میں اور آدھا رجب میں اس کو مسلمانوں کو ادا کریں گے۔

الشرح الثميرى الجزء الرابع ۳۰۹ كتاب السير على اهل الكتاب والمجوس وعبدة الأوثان من العجم ۳۲ (۹۳) ولا توضع على عجم کے مشرکوں سے جزیہ لیا جائے اس کی دلیل لمبی حدیث کا یہ کڑا ہے۔ قال بعث عمر الناس في افناء الامصار يقاتلون المشركين ... فامرنا نبينا رسول ربنا صلى الله عليه وسلم ان نقاتلكم حتى تعبدوا الله وحده او تؤدو الجزية (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب الجزية واموادعة مع اہل الذمة والحرب، ص ۴۴۶، نمبر ۳۱۵۹) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ عجم کے مشرکوں سے جزیہ لیا جا سکتا ہے۔ کیونکہ افتاء الامصار سے معلوم ہوا کہ عجم کے بت پرستوں سے جہاد کرنے گئے تھے۔ عبد الاوثان : وشن کی جمع ہے، بت کے بندے یعنی بت پرست، المجوس : جو قوم آگ کی پوجا کرتی ہے۔ [۱۳۰۷۲] (۹۳) اور جزیہ مقرر نہیں کیا جائے گا عرب کے بت پرستوں پر اور نہ مرتد پر۔ آیت سے اشارہ ملتا ہے کہ عرب کے مشرکین یا تو اسلام قبول کریں یا قتل کے لئے تیار رہیں۔ ذمی بن کر جزیہ دینا اس کے لئے قابل قبول نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے ان سے جزیہ نہیں لیا جائے گا۔ آیت میں ہے۔ فاذا انسلخ الاشهر الحرم فاقتلوا المشركين حيث وجدتموهم وخذوهم واحصروهم واقعدوا لهم كل مرصد فان تابوا واقاموا الصلوة وآتوا الزكوة فخلوا سبيلهم (ب) ( آیت ۵ ، سورۃ التوبۃ ۹ ) اس آیت میں ہے کہ نماز قائم کرنے یعنی اسلام لانے تک قتال کرتے رہو اور یہ مشرکین عرب کے بارے میں ہے۔ اس لئے مشرکین عرب کو جزیہ دے کر جزیرۂ عرب میں رہنے کا حق نہیں ہے (۲) دوسری آیت میں بھی اس کی تائید ہے۔ وقاتلوهم حتى لا تكون فتنة ويكون الدين كله لله (ج) ( آیت ۳۹، سورۃ الانفال (۸) اس آیت میں کفار عرب کے بارے میں اشارہ ہے کہ ان سے اتنا قتال کرو کہ پورا دین صرف اللہ کا ہو جائے ۔ اس لئے بھی ان سے جزیہ نہیں لیا جائے گا (۳) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابن عباس انه عليه السلام قال لا يقبل من مشركي العرب الا الاسلام او السيف (د) ( فتح القدير، ج خامس ،ص ۲۹۳ را علاء السنن، نمبر ۴۱۷۳) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مشرکین عرب سے قتل یا اسلام دونوں میں سے ایک ہے اس لئے جزیہ نہیں لیا جائے گا۔ فائدہ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ اہل عرب کے مشرکین سے بھی جزیہ لیا جا سکتا ہے۔ وہ فرماتے ہیں کہ عرب کے اہل کتاب سے جزیہ لیا جا سکتا ہے اس پر قیاس کر کے اہل عرب کے مشرکین سے بھی جزیہ لیا جاسکتا ہے۔ مرتد پر جزیہ اس لئے نہیں ہے کہ اگر مرد ہے تو یا دوبارہ اسلام قبول کرے یا اس کو تین دن کے بعد قتل کر دیا جائے گا۔ اور جزیہ کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ کفر کی حالت میں جزیہ دے کر زندہ رہے اور زندہ رہنے کا حق نہیں ہے اس لئے اس سے جزیہ بھی نہیں لیا جائے گا۔ چاہے عرب کا مرتد ہو چاہے عجم کا مرتد ہو۔ حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت عمر نے کچھ لوگوں کو شہر کی مضافات میں جنگ کے لئے روانہ فرمایا ہم کو حضور نے حکم دیا کہ اس وقت تک جنگ کرتے رہیں کہ ایک اللہ کی عبادت کرنے لگ جائیں یا جزیہ ادا کریں (ب) جب اشہر حرم ختم ہو جا ئیں تو جہاں کہیں پائیں مشرکین سے قتال کریں اور ان کو پکڑیں اور ان کو قید کریں اور ان کے لئے ہر گھات کی جگہ میں بیٹھیں ۔ پس اگر توبہ کر لیں اور نماز قائم کرنے لگیں اور زکوۃ دینے لگیں تو ان کا راستہ چھوڑ دیں ( ج ) اور ان سے لڑیں یہاں تک کہ فتنہ نہ رہے اور دین پورا کا پورا اللہ کے لئے ہو جائے (د) آپ نے فرمایا عرب کے مشرکین سے صرف اسلام قبول کیا جائے گا یا تلوار کے لئے تیار ہیں۔
The Sharh al-Thamiri, Part 4, page 308, Book of Siyar. The poor laborer (earns) twelve dirhams, two dirhams each month (92) and jizyah is placed. There is a hadith: From Mu'adh that the Prophet (peace be upon him), when he sent him to Yemen, ordered him to take from every adult (meaning one who has reached puberty) a dinar or its equivalent of Ma'afiri garments which are in Yemen. (Abu Dawud, Chapter on Taking Jizyah, p. 74, no. 3038). From this hadith it is understood that every man (is obligated) annually one dinar, whether rich or poor. 'I'tamala: derived from 'amal, meaning worker. [13071] (92) Jizyah will be imposed on the People of the Book, and on the Majus, and on the idol worshippers of the non-Arabs. Jews, Christians, and Majus, whether they live among Arabs or among non-Arabs. If they wish to live as dhimmis, then jizyah will be imposed on them. Similarly, if the idol worshippers of non-Arabs wish to live as dhimmis, then jizyah will be imposed on their heads. However, jizyah is not (imposed) on Arab idol worshippers; either they accept Islam or be prepared for killing; they cannot be kept in Arabia as dhimmis. For the People of the Book, there is this verse regarding jizyah: 'Fight those who do not believe in Allah nor in the Last Day, nor forbid what Allah and His Messenger have forbidden, nor adopt the religion of truth from among those who were given the Scripture, until they give the jizyah willingly while they are subdued.' (Verse 29, Surah al-Tawbah 9). In this verse it is that the People of the Book, i.e., Jews and Christians, are to be fought until they give jizyah. And this is general (including both Arabs and non-Arabs), so jizyah can also be imposed on the People of the Book of the Arabs. For taking jizyah from the Majus, there is this hadith: 'I heard Amr say.... Then the letter of Umar ibn al-Khattab came to us a year before his death: Separate every Mahram from the Majus. And Umar had not taken jizyah from the Majus until Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf testified that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) took it from the Majus of Hajar.' (Bukhari, Chapter on Jizyah and Truce with the People of Dhimma, p. 446, nos. 3157-3156; and Abu Dawud, Chapter on Taking Jizyah from the Majus, p. 75, no. 3043). From this hadith it is understood that the Prophet took jizyah from the Majus of Hajar, from which it is understood that jizyah can be taken from Arab Majus. (3) From Ibn Abbas: He said, 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) made peace with the people of Najran for two thousand garments, half in Safar and half in Rajab, which they would pay to the Muslims.' (Abu Dawud, Chapter on Taking Jizyah, p. no. 3041). The people of Najran were Arab Christians; jizyah was taken from them, from which it is understood that jizyah can be taken from the People of the Book of the Arabs. Footnote: (a) When the Prophet sent Mu'adh towards Yemen, he ordered him to take from every adult one dinar, or its equivalent of Ma'afiri cloth which is in Yemen. (b) Fight those who do not believe in Allah and the Last Day, and do not forbid what Allah and His Messenger have forbidden, and do not adopt the religion of truth from among the People of the Book, until they give jizyah with their hand while they are subdued. (c) The letter of Umar ibn al-Khattab came to us a year before his death: Separate the Mahram women from the Majus, and Umar did not take jizyah from the Majus until Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf testified that the Prophet had received jizyah from the Majus of Hajar. (d) The Prophet made peace with the people of Najran for two thousand garments, half in Safar and half in Rajab, which they would pay to the Muslims.
[PAGE_316] The Sharh al-Thamiri, Part 4, page 309, Book of Siyar. Upon the People of the Book, and the Majus, and the idol worshippers of the non-Arabs. 32 (93) And it (jizyah) is not placed on... From the non-Arab polytheists jizyah may be taken; its proof is this link from a long hadith: He said, 'Umar sent people to the outskirts of the cities to fight the polytheists... Then our Prophet, the Messenger of our Lord (peace be upon him) ordered us to fight you until you worship Allah alone or pay jizyah.' (Bukhari, Chapter on Jizyah and Truce with the People of Dhimma and War, p. 446, no. 3159). From this hadith it is understood that jizyah can be taken from non-Arab polytheists, because 'afna' al-amsar' indicates that they went to fight the idol worshippers of the non-Arabs. 'Abd al-awthan: plural of wathan, meaning idol worshippers, i.e., polytheists. al-Majus: the people who worship fire. [13072] (93) And jizyah will not be imposed on the Arab idol worshippers, nor on the apostate. The verse indicates that Arab polytheists must either accept Islam or be prepared for killing. To give jizyah as a dhimmi is not acceptable for them. Therefore jizyah will not be taken from them. In the verse: 'And when the sacred months have passed, then kill the polytheists wherever you find them and capture them and besiege them and sit in wait for them at every place. But if they repent, establish prayer, and give zakah, then leave their way free.' (Verse 5, Surah al-Tawbah 9). In this verse it is that fighting continues until they establish prayer, i.e., accept Islam, and this is about the Arab polytheists. Therefore Arab polytheists do not have the right to live in the Arabian Peninsula by giving jizyah. (2) Another verse also supports this: 'And fight them until there is no fitnah and religion is all for Allah.' (Verse 39, Surah al-Anfal 8). This verse indicates about the Arab disbelievers that you should fight them until the whole religion becomes for Allah alone. Therefore jizyah will also not be taken from them. (3) In a hadith: From Ibn Abbas that he (peace be upon him) said: 'Nothing is accepted from the Arab polytheists except Islam or the sword.' (Fath al-Qadir, vol. 5, p. 293; and I'la' al-Sunan, no. 4173). From this hadith it is understood that for Arab polytheists, there is either killing or Islam, so jizyah will not be taken. Benefit: Imam Shafi'i says that jizyah may also be taken from the Arab polytheists. He says that jizyah is taken from the Arab People of the Book, and by analogy upon that, jizyah may also be taken from the Arab polytheists. Jizyah is not imposed on the apostate because if he is a man, he must either re-embrace Islam or be killed after three days. And the meaning of jizyah is that one remains alive while in a state of disbelief by paying jizyah, but he has no right to remain alive, therefore jizyah will not be taken from him. Whether the apostate is an Arab or a non-Arab. Footnote: (a) Umar sent some people to the outskirts of cities to fight, and we were ordered by the Prophet to continue fighting until they worship Allah alone or pay jizyah. (b) When the sacred months expire, then kill the polytheists wherever you find them, seize them, besiege them, and lie in wait for them at every place. But if they repent, establish prayer, and give zakah, then leave them alone. (c) And fight them until fitnah is no more and religion is entirely for Allah. (d) The Prophet said: From the Arab polytheists, only Islam or the sword is accepted.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school on the jizyah tax. It opens by stating the core ruling: jizyah is imposed on three categories—People of the Book (Jews and Christians), Majus (Zoroastrians), and idol worshippers from non-Arabs. The author immediately provides proofs. For the People of the Book, the primary proof is Qur'an 9:29, which commands fighting them until they pay jizyah. This verse is general, covering both Arab and non-Arab People of the Book. The author supports this with the historical precedent of the Prophet taking jizyah from the Christians of Najran (who were Arabs). For the Majus, the proof is the hadith in which Umar initially did not take jizyah from them until Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf testified that the Prophet had taken it from the Majus of Hajar (an Arab tribe). Thus Arab Majus are also subject to jizyah. For non-Arab idol worshippers, the proof is the hadith where the Prophet instructed fighting all polytheists until they pay jizyah, and the context shows this applies to non-Arab polytheists.

The passage then turns to categories exempt from jizyah: Arab idol worshippers and apostates. The author explains that Arab idol worshippers are given only two options: Islam or the sword. The proof is Qur'an 9:5 (the 'sword verse') and 8:39, which indicate that idolatry is not to be tolerated in the Arabian Peninsula. Additionally, the hadith 'Nothing is accepted from the Arab polytheists except Islam or the sword' explicitly excludes jizyah. The passage also refutes a potential analogy: although jizyah is taken from Arab People of the Book, it is not extended to Arab idol worshippers because the texts specifically differentiate them.

A significant benefit mentioned is the view of Imam al-Shafi'i, who allows jizyah from Arab idol worshippers by analogy (qiyas) on Arab People of the Book. The Hanafi response, implied by the author's presentation, is that the texts for Arab idol worshippers are specific and override the analogy. Finally, apostates are not subject to jizyah because they are given the choice of repentance or execution; jizyah implies living in disbelief, which is not permitted for an apostate.

Key Terms
جزية (jizyah): A tax imposed on non-Muslims (dhimmis) in exchange for protection and exemption from military service.
مجوس (Majus): Zoroastrians, a religious community originally from Persia, considered by the Hanafis as subject to jizyah.
مرتد (murtadd): An apostate from Islam; a person who renounces Islam after having accepted it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, from which of the following groups is jizyah NOT taken?
A) People of the Book (Ahl al-Kitab)
B) Majus (Zoroastrians)
C) Non-Arab idol worshippers
D) Arab idol worshippers

Key Takeaway
Jizyah is wajib on People of the Book, Majus, and non-Arab idol worshippers, but not on Arab idol worshippers or apostates, based on specific textual proofs.

Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules
intermediate
10 min
Jizyah on Arab Polytheists and Apostates
Ruling on jizyah for Arab polytheists and apostates with proofs and Shafi'i dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on jizyah for Arab polytheists and apostates, explain the textual proofs, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using qiyas.

Core Idea
Arab polytheists and apostates cannot pay jizyah; they face Islam or death.

Jizyah is a protected tax for certain non-Muslims in Islamic governance. But the Hanafi school draws a sharp line: not all polytheists qualify. This lesson unpacks who can pay jizyah, who cannot, and why — with clear Quranic and Prophetic evidence against the Shafi'i view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling on jizyah for Arab polytheists
State that jizyah is not taken from Arab polytheists; they must choose between Islam and the sword. Also note that apostates are similarly excluded.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Locate the primary proofs for the Hanafi position
Find the Quranic verses (9:5, 8:39) and the hadith of Ibn Abbas that explicitly require Islam or death for Arab polytheists.
These proofs are nass (explicit text).
3
Present the Shafi'i counter-argument
State that Imam al-Shafi'i allows jizyah from Arab polytheists by analogy to Arab People of the Book.
The basis is qiyas.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Explain that the Hanafi school rejects this analogy because the explicit texts (nass) override qiyas; the rulings are mutually exclusive.
Qiyas is not applied when a text specifies a contrary rule.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: according to Hanafis, Arab polytheists can never become dhimmis; according to Shafi'is, they can.
This affects the treatment of conquered Arab tribes.

(۲) دوسری آیت میں بھی اس کی تائید ہے۔ وقاتلوهم حتى لا تكون فتنة ويكون الدين كله لله (ج) ( آیت ۳۹، سورۃ الانفال (۸) اس آیت میں کفار عرب کے بارے میں اشارہ ہے کہ ان سے اتنا قتال کرو کہ پورا دین صرف اللہ کا ہو جائے ۔ اس لئے بھی ان سے جزیہ نہیں لیا جائے گا (۳) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابن عباس انه عليه السلام قال لا يقبل من مشركي العرب الا الاسلام او السيف (د) ( فتح القدير، ج خامس ،ص ۲۹۳ را علاء السنن، نمبر ۴۱۷۳) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مشرکین عرب سے قتل یا اسلام دونوں میں سے ایک ہے اس لئے جزیہ نہیں لیا جائے گا۔ فائدہ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ اہل عرب کے مشرکین سے بھی جزیہ لیا جا سکتا ہے۔ وہ فرماتے ہیں کہ عرب کے اہل کتاب سے جزیہ لیا جا سکتا ہے اس پر قیاس کر کے اہل عرب کے مشرکین سے بھی جزیہ لیا جاسکتا ہے۔ مرتد پر جزیہ اس لئے نہیں ہے کہ اگر مرد ہے تو یا دوبارہ اسلام قبول کرے یا اس کو تین دن کے بعد قتل کر دیا جائے گا۔ اور جزیہ کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ کفر کی حالت میں جزیہ دے کر زندہ رہے اور زندہ رہنے کا حق نہیں ہے اس لئے اس سے جزیہ بھی نہیں لیا جائے گا۔ چاہے عرب کا مرتد ہو چاہے عجم کا مرتد ہو۔ حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت عمر نے کچھ لوگوں کو شہر کی مضافات میں جنگ کے لئے روانہ فرمایا ہم کو حضور نے حکم دیا کہ اس وقت تک جنگ کرتے رہیں کہ ایک اللہ کی عبادت کرنے لگ جائیں یا جزیہ ادا کریں (ب) جب اشہر حرم ختم ہو جا ئیں تو جہاں کہیں پائیں مشرکین سے قتال کریں اور ان کو پکڑیں اور ان کو قید کریں اور ان کے لئے ہر گھات کی جگہ میں بیٹھیں ۔ پس اگر تو بہ کر لیں اور نماز قائم کرنے لگیں اور زکوۃ دینے لگیں تو ان کا راستہ چھوڑ دیں ( ج ) اور ان سے لڑیں یہاں تک کہ فتنہ نہ رہے اور دین پورا کا پورا اللہ کے لئے ہو جائے (د) آپ نے فرمایا عرب کے مشرکین سے صرف اسلام قبول کیا جائے گا یا تلوار کے لئے تیار ہیں۔
The Sharh al-Thamiri, Part Four, 309, Book of Siyar. On the People of the Book, the Zoroastrians, and the idol worshippers of the non-Arabs. (93) And jizyah is not placed on non-Arab polytheists? Jizyah is taken from them. The proof for this is this piece of a long hadith: He said: Umar sent people to the outskirts of the cities to fight the polytheists... So our Prophet, the Messenger of our Lord, peace be upon him, commanded us to fight you until you worship Allah alone or pay jizyah (a) (Sahih al-Bukhari, Book of Jizyah and Truce with People of Dhimmah and War, p. 446, no. 3159). From this hadith it is understood that jizyah can be taken from non-Arab polytheists, because 'the outskirts of the cities' indicates that they went to fight non-Arab idol worshippers. 'Abd al-Awthan' is the plural of 'wathan', meaning servants of idols, i.e., idol worshippers. 'Al-Majus' is the people who worship fire. (13072 (93)) And jizyah will not be imposed on Arab idol worshippers nor on apostates. The verse indicates that Arab polytheists must either accept Islam or be prepared for death. Becoming a dhimmi and paying jizyah is not acceptable for them. Therefore, jizyah will not be taken from them. The verse says: 'Then when the sacred months have passed, slay the polytheists wherever you find them, and take them, and confine them, and lie in wait for them at every place of ambush. But if they repent and establish prayer and give zakat, then leave their way free.' (b) (Surah al-Tawbah 9:5) This verse says to keep fighting until they establish prayer, i.e., accept Islam, and it pertains to Arab polytheists. Therefore, Arab polytheists do not have the right to pay jizyah and remain in the Arabian Peninsula. (2) Another verse supports this: 'And fight them until there is no fitnah and the religion is entirely for Allah.' (c) (Surah al-Anfal 8:39) This verse indicates regarding Arab disbelievers that you should fight them until the entire religion is for Allah alone. Therefore, jizyah will not be taken from them. (3) The hadith says: From Ibn Abbas that he, peace be upon him, said: 'Nothing is accepted from the polytheists of the Arabs except Islam or the sword.' (d) (Fath al-Qadir, vol. 5, p. 293, and 'Ala' al-Sunan, no. 4173) From this hadith it is understood that for Arab polytheists, it is either death or Islam, so jizyah will not be taken. Benefit: Imam al-Shafi'i says that jizyah can be taken from Arab polytheists as well. He says that jizyah can be taken from the People of the Book of the Arabs, and by analogy (qiyas), jizyah can be taken from Arab polytheists. Jizyah is not taken from an apostate because if he is a man, he must either revert to Islam or be killed after three days. The meaning of jizyah is to remain alive in a state of disbelief by paying jizyah, but he has no right to remain alive, so jizyah is not taken from him, whether he is an Arab apostate or a non-Arab apostate. Footnote: (a) Umar sent some people to the outskirts of the cities for war; the Prophet commanded us to fight until they worship Allah alone or pay jizyah. (b) When the sacred months have passed, fight the polytheists wherever you find them, capture them, besiege them, and lie in wait for them in every ambush. Then if they repent and establish prayer and give zakat, leave their way free. (c) And fight them until there is no fitnah and the religion is entirely for Allah. (d) The Prophet said: From Arab polytheists, only Islam is accepted or they are ready for the sword.
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Siyar presents two rulings on jizyah. First, jizyah is taken from non-Arab polytheists, including Zoroastrians and idol worshippers, as proven by the hadith of Umar's expedition to the outskirts of cities. Second, jizyah is not imposed on Arab polytheists or apostates. The author provides multiple proofs for the second ruling: Quran 9:5 commands fighting Arab polytheists until they repent and pray, not until they pay jizyah; Quran 8:39 reinforces this; and the hadith from Ibn Abbas explicitly states only Islam or the sword is accepted from Arab polytheists. The Shafi'i objection is then addressed: Imam al-Shafi'i analogizes from Arab People of the Book to Arab polytheists, but the Hanafi response is that the texts specifically exclude Arab polytheists from jizyah. Apostates are also excluded because they must return to Islam or be killed; jizyah is meant for those who remain in disbelief peacefully.

Key Terms
جزیة (jizyah): A tax imposed on non-Muslims in an Islamic state in exchange for protection and exemption from military service.
مشرك عرب (mushrik 'arab): An Arab polytheist who is not a follower of a revealed scripture.
مرتد (murtadd): A Muslim who renounces Islam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the basis for not taking jizyah from Arab polytheists?
A) They are too poor to pay
B) Quran and hadith explicitly limit them to Islam or the sword
C) They are not conquered
D) They are not polytheists

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school unequivocally excludes Arab polytheists and apostates from jizyah, based on nass (Quran and hadith) that overrides analogy.

Exemptions from Jizyah: Women, Children, and Others
Ruling on categories exempt from jizyah with proofs from hadith and athar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the categories exempt from jizyah in the Hanafi school and identify the textual proofs (dalil) for each exemption.

Core Idea
Jizyah is only on able-bodied adult males; women, children, and the disabled are exempt.

Jizyah is a tax imposed on non-Muslims under Muslim rule, but not all are liable. The Hanafi school specifies clear exemptions based on the inability to fight or work. In this lesson, we examine the passage listing exempt categories and the evidence from the Sunnah and practice of the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the exempt categories
Read the passage and list all categories that are not required to pay jizyah. Note any conditions attached to the exemptions (e.g., monks who do not mix with people).
The passage lists: women, minors, the elderly, the blind, the poor who cannot work, and secluded monks.
2
Analyze the rationale
Determine why each category is exempt. The common thread is inability to fight or earn. Jizyah is in exchange for protection and exemption from military service.
The elderly, blind, and poor cannot participate in fighting or productive work.
3
Examine the proofs
For each exemption, locate the specific dalil mentioned: the hadith of Mu'adh (restriction to adult males), the athar of Umar (exclusion of women/children), and the incident of Umar and the old man.
The hadith uses 'halim' (adult); the athar explicitly excludes women and children; the old man's story shows exemption for the elderly.
4
Note the ruling on apostates
The passage also mentions that apostates cannot pay jizyah. Understand why: a male apostate must be killed or return to Islam; a female apostate is imprisoned and cannot pay jizyah.
The hadith 'Whoever changes his religion, kill him' is cited.
5
Synthesize the legal principle
Formulate the rule: Jizyah is obligatory only on free, adult, able-bodied male non-Muslims. All others are exempt. This is a well-established Hanafi position.
This is based on the principle that jizyah is a substitute for military service.

پر اور نہ اندھے پر اور نہ ایسے فقیر پر جو کام نہ کرتا ہو اور نہ ایسے راہب پر جو لوگوں سے نہ ملتا ہو۔ ر ان لوگوں پر جزیہ نہیں ہے۔ صلى الله عليه يه لوگ غریب ہیں اور کام کرنے کے لائق نہیں ہیں۔ اس لئے ان لوگوں پر جزیہ مقرر نہیں کیا جائے گا (۲) حدیث میں ہے ۔ عن معاذ ان النبي [صلى الله عليه وسلم] لما وجهه الى اليمن امره ان يأخذ من كل حالم يعني محتلما دينارا (ب) (ابو داؤد شریف، باب فی اخذ الجزیۃ ، ص ۷۴ ، نمبر ۳۰۳۸) اس حدیث میں مختلما کی قید سے معلوم ہوا کہ جو بالغ نہ ہو یعنی بچہ ہو اس پر جزیہ نہیں ہے۔ اور عورت پر جزیہ نہ ہونے کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے۔ ان عمر بن الخطاب كتب الـى عـمـاله ان لا يضربوا الجزية على النساء والصبيان ولا يضربوها الا على من جرت عليه المواسی (ج) ( سنن للبیہقی ، باب الزيادة على الدينار بالصلح ، ج تاسع ص ۳۲۹، نمبر ۱۸۶۸۳ مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ، اما قالوافی وضع الجزية والقتال عليها ، ج سادس، ص ۴۳۱، نمبر ۳۲۶۲۶) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ عورتوں اور بچوں پر جزیہ نہیں ہے۔ بوڑھے پر جزیہ نہیں ہے اس کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے۔ قال ابصر عمر شيخا كبيرا من اهل الذمة يسأل فقال له مالك؟ قال ليس لى مال وان الجزية فرمایا اگر میں ہوتا تو ان کو نہیں جلاتا کیونکہ حضور نے منع فرمایا ہے کہ اللہ کے عذاب کی طرح تم آگ سے عذاب نہ دو۔ اور میں ان کو زندیقوں کو قتل کرتا حضور کے فرمان کی وجہ سے کہ جس نے اپنے دین اسلام کو بدل دیا اس کو قتل کر دو (ب) حضور نے جب حضرت معاذ کو یمن کی طرف متوجہ کیا تو حکم دیا کہ ہر بالغ آدمی سے ایک دینار جزیہ لے (ج) حضرت عمر نے اپنے عمال کو لکھا کہ عورتوں اور بچوں پر جزیہ مقرر نہ کرے۔ اور صرف اسی پر جزیہ مقرر کرے جسکے نیچے کے بال نکل آئے ہوں۔
Idol worshippers of the Arabs and nor on apostates. (13073 (94)) And no jizyah on a woman, nor on a child, nor on an old person, nor on a blind person, nor on a poor person who does not work, nor on monks who do not mix with people. After understanding Islam, apostasy is even worse than disbelief, so he will be killed preferentially or he accepts Islam. (2) The proof for killing is this hadith: From Ikrimah who said: Ali was brought some zindiqs (heretics) and he burned them. That reached Ibn Abbas who said: If I had been, I would not have burned them because the Messenger of Allah forbade punishing with Allah's punishment, but I would have killed them due to the saying of the Messenger of Allah: 'Whoever changes his religion, kill him.' (a) (Sahih al-Bukhari, Book of Judgement on Apostates and Apostates, p. 1022, no. 6922). From this hadith it is understood that the apostate will be killed after three days. If the apostate is a woman, she will be imprisoned until she repents. And she will not be left in a state of disbelief. Therefore, jizyah is not taken from her either. Another hadith in Bukhari follows: Then Mu'adh ibn Jabal followed him... he said: I will not sit until the judgment of Allah and His Messenger is carried out three times (Sahih al-Bukhari, no. 6923) meaning I will not sit until the apostate is killed. (13073 (94)) And jizyah is not on a woman, nor on a child, nor on an old person, nor on a blind person, nor on a poor person who does not work, nor on a monk who does not mix with people. These people are poor and not capable of work. Therefore, jizyah will not be imposed on them. (2) A hadith: From Mu'adh that the Prophet, when he sent him to Yemen, commanded him to take from every 'halim', meaning adult, a dinar (b) (Sunan Abi Dawud, Book of Taking Jizyah, p. 74, no. 3038). From this hadith, the condition of 'mukhtalim' (adult) indicates that jizyah is not on those who are not adult, i.e., children. And the proof for no jizyah on women is this athar: Umar ibn al-Khattab wrote to his governors that they should not impose jizyah on women and children, and they should only impose it on those whose pubic hair has grown. (c) (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Book of Increase over the Dinar by Treaty, vol. 9, p. 329, no. 18683; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, Regarding Placing Jizyah and Fighting for It, vol. 6, p. 431, no. 32626). From this athar it is understood that there is no jizyah on women and children. There is no jizyah on an old person; the proof is this athar: Umar saw a very old man from the People of Dhimmah begging. He asked him: What is the matter with you? He said: I have no wealth and jizyah is taken from me. Umar said: We have not been fair to you; we consumed your youth and then take jizyah from you. Then he wrote to his governors. Footnote: (a) Some zindiqs were brought to Ali and he burned them. This news reached Ibn Abbas who said: If I had been, I would not have burned them because the Prophet forbade punishing with Allah's punishment, but I would kill them due to the Prophet's saying: Whoever changes his religion, kill him. (b) The Prophet, when he sent Mu'adh to Yemen, commanded him to take one dinar from every adult. (c) Umar wrote to his governors not to impose jizyah on women and children, and only impose it on those whose pubic hair has grown.
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage lists categories exempt from jizyah: women, children, the elderly, the blind, the poor who cannot work, and monks who seclude themselves. The rationale is that jizyah is a tax on able-bodied adult males who can fight. The author provides proofs: the hadith of Mu'adh restricting jizyah to 'halim' (adult males), the athar of Umar explicitly excluding women and children, and the incident of Umar exempting an old man. Additionally, the passage touches on apostates, reiterating that they cannot pay jizyah because they must be killed or return to Islam. The evidence for killing apostates is the hadith 'Whoever changes his religion, kill him.' The footnotes clarify the Arabic text of the proofs.

Key Terms
صبي (sabi): A minor child, not yet adult.
زمن (zamin): An elderly or physically disabled person incapable of work.
أعمى (a'ma): A blind person.
فقير غير معتمل (faqir ghayr mu'tamil): A poor person who does not have the ability to work.
راهب (rahb): A monk who has secluded himself from society and does not mix with people.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Jizyah is only obligatory on free, adult, able-bodied male non-Muslims; all others are exempt based on clear textual evidence.

Exemption from Jizya for Elderly, Disabled, and Monks
Proof from athar that jizya is not taken from the very old, blind, disabled, and reclusive monks

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on jizya exemption for the elderly, blind, disabled, and monks, and explain the proof and analogy used.

Core Idea
Jizya is not taken from those who cannot earn – inability to work is the decisive cause.

This lesson explores who is exempt from paying jizya in Hanafi law. The author cites prophetic precedents (athar) from the companions Umar and Khalid ibn al-Walid, then extends the ruling to the blind and disabled through analogy. Understanding this shows how Hanafi jurists combine textual proof and reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its basis
The ruling is that jizya is not taken from a very old person. The basis is an athar (precedent) attributed to Umar via Zanjawayh.
2
Locate the dalil
Two athar are cited: one from Umar about not taking jizya from the elderly, and the treaty of Khalid ibn al-Walid with al-Hirah which exempts monks who have no hand (cannot earn).
The second athar explicitly mentions 'except those who have no hand'.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'except those who have no hand' indicates that inability to earn (lack of means) is the effective cause of exemption. The elderly are analogized to this.
4
Understand the qiyas
The blind and disabled are analogized to the elderly because they share the same effective cause: inability to earn. The monk who does not mix with people is also analogized because he cannot earn.
Qiyas is applied to extend the ruling from the established case (old person) to new cases.
5
Note the scope
The exemption applies to those who are permanently unable to earn due to old age, disability, blindness, or monastic seclusion. Those who are able to earn but choose not to are not exempt.

ان لا يأخذوا الجزية من شيخ كبير (الف) ( رواة زنجوية في الاموال را اعلاء السنن، باب لا جزیہ علی صبی ولا امرأة الخ ، ج ثانی عشر ص ۵۰۹ نمبر ۴۱۷۵) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ بہت بوڑھے سے جزیہ نہیں لیا جائے گا۔ اور اسی پر اپاہج اور اندھے کو قیاس کیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ یہ دونوں بھی کما نہیں سکتے ہیں۔ جو راہب لوگوں سے اختلاط نہ کرتا ہو وہ بھی کما نہیں سکتا ہے اس لئے اس سے بھی جزیہ نہیں لیا جائے گا (۲) اثر میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن خالد بن وليد انه صالح اهل الحيرة على تسعين ومائة الف درهم تقبل كل سنة جزاء عن ايديهم في الدنيا رهبانهم وقسيسهم الا من كان غير ذى يد حبيسا عن الدنيا تاركا لها وسائحا تاركا للدنيا (ب) ( مختصر رواه الطبری فی تاریخہ ، ج رابع ص ۱۴ را اعلاء السنن، باب لا توضح الدنيا على الرهبان لا يخالطون الناس، ج ثانی عشر ، ص ۵۱۳، نمبر ۴۱۷۹ ) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ جو راہب لوگوں سے اختلاط نہ کرتا ہو اس پر جزیہ نہیں ہے۔ انت زن : اپانچ ، الربان : راہب کی جمع ہے، یخالطون : خلط سے ہے ملنا جلنا۔
That they should not take jizya from a very old person (a) (narrated by Zanjawayh in al-Amwal, I'la al-Sunan, chapter: No jizya on child or woman, etc., vol. 12, p. 509, no. 4175) From this athar it is known that jizya will not be taken from a very old person. And on him [the old] will be analogized the disabled and the blind, because these two also cannot earn. A monk who does not mix with people also cannot earn, therefore jizya will not be taken from him. (2) There is proof in the athar: From Khalid ibn al-Walid that he made peace with the people of al-Hirah on 190,000 dirhams, accepted every year as compensation for their hands in this world, their monks and priests, except those who have no hand, are detached from this world, leaving it, and are wanderers leaving the world. (b) (Summarized by al-Tabari in his Tarikh, vol. 4, p. 14, and I'la al-Sunan, chapter: No jizya on monks who do not mix with people, vol. 12, p. 513, no. 4179) From this athar it is known that jizya is not on the monk who does not mix with people. Vocabulary: اپانچ = disabled, الربان = plural of راهب (monk), يخالطون = from خلط, meaning to mix.
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on who is exempt from jizya. The author first states that jizya is not taken from the very old, citing an athar (precedent) from the Companion Umar (indirectly). Then he extends the ruling to the blind and disabled by qiyas (analogy) because they share the same effective cause: inability to earn. He also adds that a monk who does not mix with people also cannot earn, so jizya is not taken from him. The second athar from Khalid ibn al-Walid confirms that monks who are detached from worldly life are exempt, while others are required to pay. The passage concludes with a glossary for some Arabic terms. This ruling is based on the principle that jizya is a tax on able-bodied earning men; those incapable are exempt.

Key Terms
جزية (jizya): Poll tax imposed on free, adult, able-bodied non-Muslim men under the Islamic state.
راهب (rahb): A monk who secludes himself from society for worship.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogicial reasoning from an established case (asl) to a new case (far') based on a common effective cause (illa).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) A healthy adult male dhimmi
B) A blind dhimmi who cannot work
C) A wealthy merchant who is a dhimmi
D) A young adult dhimmi who is able-bodied

Key Takeaway
Jizya exemption in Hanafi law is based on inability to earn, as proven by athar and extended by qiyas.

Jizya Drops Upon Conversion: The Hanafi Ruling
Ruling with hadith proof and distinction from kharaj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on jizya when a dhimmi converts to Islam and explain the distinction between jizya and kharaj.

Core Idea
When a dhimmi accepts Islam, the jizya obligation is immediately removed, but kharaj on land remains.

This passage presents a clear ruling on the fate of jizya when a non-Muslim subject (dhimmi) embraces Islam. The author provides a hadith proof and a key distinction between jizya—a personal humiliation tax—and kharaj—a land tax that survives conversion. Understanding this ruling clarifies the nature of jizya as a penalty for disbelief, not a perpetual charge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The act is a dhimmi converting to Islam while jizya is due. The ruling: the jizya obligation drops immediately.
The ruling is absolute—no condition of paying arrears.
2
Locate the Dalil
The proof is a hadith: 'There is no jizya upon a Muslim' (Sunan Abi Dawud, Tirmidhi). This is a general statement covering all Muslims, including converts.
The hadith is ahad, but its meaning is clear (zanni al-dalala).
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
The negation 'laysa' indicates complete denial of obligation. The phrase 'upon a Muslim' (على مسلم) includes any person who becomes Muslim, so upon conversion the obligation ceases.
This interpretation is supported by the companion Sufyan al-Thawri.
4
Distinguish Jizya from Kharaj
Jizya is a personal humiliation (dhull) for disbelief, so it is incompatible with Islam. Kharaj is a land-based tax, not tied to personal status, so it remains even after conversion.
This distinction prevents confusion: land taxes are not waived by conversion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۳۰۷۴) (۹۵) کوئی ایسا آدمی اسلام لائے کہ اس پر جزیہ ہو تو وہ ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ پہلے ذمی تھا جس کی وجہ سے اس کے سر پر جزیہ تھا اب وہ مسلمان ہو گیا تو جزیہ ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ البتہ اگر اس کی زمین پر خراج تھا تو وہ باقی رہے گا۔ یہ کفر کی وجہ سے اس کی ذلت کی چیز ہے اور مسلمان ہونے کے بعد اس ذلت کا اہل نہیں رہا اس لئے ساقط ہو جائے گا (۲) حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال قال رسول الله الله ليس على مسلم جزية سئل سفيان عن تفسير هذا فقال اذا اسلم فلا جزية عليه ( ج ) ( ابو داؤد شریف، باب فی الذمى الذى يسلم في بعض السنتي حل عليه جزية ، ص ۷۷، نمبر ۳۰۵۳ / ترمذی شریف باب ما جاءلیس علی المسلمین جزیہ ، ص ۱۳۸، نمبر ۶۳۳ ، کتاب الزکوۃ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ذمی مسلمان ہو جائے تو اس پر سے جزیہ ساقط ہو جائے گا۔
3074) (95) If a person accepts Islam while he has jizya upon him, then it will fall. Previously he was a dhimmi, due to which jizya was upon his head; now he has become Muslim, so jizya will fall. However, if there was kharaj on his land, that will remain. This is because jizya is a matter of humiliation due to disbelief, and after becoming Muslim he is no longer deserving of that humiliation, so it falls. (2) There is proof in the hadith: From Ibn Abbas, he said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'There is no jizya upon a Muslim.' Sufyan was asked about its interpretation and he said: 'When he becomes Muslim, there is no jizya upon him.' (c) (Abu Dawud, chapter: On the dhimmi who becomes Muslim during some part of the year, p. 77, no. 3053 / Tirmidhi, chapter: On there being no jizya upon Muslims, p. 138, no. 633, Kitab al-Zakat) From this hadith it is known that if a dhimmi becomes Muslim, jizya will drop from him.
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage presents a clear ruling: if a dhimmi converts to Islam, the obligation of jizya is immediately dropped. However, if the land he owned is subject to kharaj (land tax), that remains because it is not a personal humiliation but a tax on land. The author explains that jizya is a mark of humiliation for disbelief, so it is incompatible with the honor of Islam. The proof is a hadith from Ibn Abbas where the Prophet explicitly states that there is no jizya upon a Muslim. The companion Sufyan (likely Sufyan al-Thawri) interpreted it to mean that upon conversion, jizya is nullified. This ruling is consistent across the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
جزیہ (jizya): Poll tax on non-Muslims in Islamic state.
خراج (kharaj): Land tax imposed on agricultural land in conquered territories.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Upon conversion to Islam, a dhimmi's jizya obligation drops immediately, while kharaj on land remains.

Interposition of Two Years' Jizya (Tadakhul)
Ruling that two years' accrued jizya interpose so only one is taken, with intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on tadakhul of jizya and evaluate the opposing arguments from Imam Shafi'i and Imam Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
When jizya accumulates for two years, tadakhul applies — only one year is due.

What happens when a dhimmi fails to pay jizya for two consecutive years? Are both years due, or do the obligations merge into one? The Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani) holds that the two years interpose, so only one jizya is collected. However, Imam Shafi'i and Imam Abu Yusuf within the Hanafi school argue that both years must be taken. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind both positions and identifies the relied-upon (mufta bihi) view.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling that only one year's jizya is due when two years accumulate. Recognise the term 'tadakhul' and its application.
The principle of tadakhul also applies to zakat and ushr.
2
Identify the opposing view
Note that Imam Shafi'i and Imam Abu Yusuf hold that both years' jizya must be collected. Understand their concern for treasury loss and deterrence of evasion.
This creates an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
3
Examine the Hanafi proof
Analyse the Hanafi evidence: analogy (qiyas) to sadaqah and ushr, athar from Tawus and Zuhri, and the principle of ease (taysir) for the dhimmi.
The athar show that early caliphs did not collect ushr twice in one year, analogised to jizya.
4
Analyse the opposing proof
Understand the opposing argument: accumulation implies both years are due; otherwise, the treasury suffers and dhimmis may deliberately delay payment.
Focus on the practical concern about loss of revenue.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
Recognise the practical difference: in the Hanafi mufta bihi, only one year's jizya is collected; in the other view, two years. Understand why Abu Hanifa's view is relied upon (ease and established practice).
Tarjih is based on sahih athar and the spirit of Islamic leniency.

حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت عمر نے ایک بہت بوڑھے ذمی کو دیکھا کہ وہ مانگ رہا ہے۔ تو اس سے پوچھا کیا بات ہے؟ کہا میرے پاس مال نہیں ہے اور مجھ سے جزیہ لیا جاتا ہے۔ تو حضرت عمر نے اس سے کہا۔ ہم نے تمہارے ساتھ انصاف نہیں کیا ۔ تمہاری میں جوانی میں کھایا پھر بھی تم سے جزیہ لیں۔ پھر اپنے عمال کو لکھا کہ بہت بوڑھے سے جزیہ نہ لیں (ب) خالد بن ولید نے حیرہ والوں سے ایک لاکھ نوے ہزار درہم پر صلح کی قبول کیا جائے گا ہر مال میں دنیا میں رہنے کے بدلے کی وجہ سے چاہے ان کے راہب ہو چاہے تقسیس ہو۔ البتہ جن کا ہاتھ خالی ہو دنیا کو چھوڑے ہوا ہو، سفر کرتا رہتا ہو اور دنیا کو چھوڑ رکھا ہو اس سے جزیہ نہیں لیا جائے گا (ج) حضور نے فرمایا مسلمان پر جزیہ نہیں ہے۔ حضرت سفیان سے اس کی تغیر پوچھی تو فرمایا اگر می مسلمان ہو جائے تو اس پر جز یہ نہیں ہے۔

الشرح الثميرى الجزء الرابع ) ۳۱۲ كتاب السير
الحولان تداخلت الجزيتان [ ۹۷۳۰۶) ولايجوز احداث بيعة ولا كنيسة في دار
اثر میں ہے۔ عن طاؤس انه قال اذا تداركت الصدقات فلا توخذ الاولى كالجزية(الف) (مصنف ابن ابي شيبة ،۱۳۲ من قال لاتو خذ الصدقة في السنة الا مرة واحدة ، ج خانی پس ۴۳۱، نمبر ۱۰۷۳۳ (۲) ایک اور اثر میں ہے۔ عن الزهري قال لم يبلغنا من احد من ولاة هذه الامة الذين كانوا بالمدينة ابوبكر وعمر وعثمان انهم كانوا لا يثنون العشور لكن يبعثون عليها كل عام في الخصب والجدب لان اخذها سنة من رسول الله الا الله (ب) (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ، من قال لا تو خذ الصدقة في الستة الا مرة واحدة ، ج ثانی، ص ۴۳۱، نمبر ۱۰۷۳۲) اس اثر سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ ایک سال میں دومرتبہ عشر نہیں لیتے تھے ۔ اور دوسال کا ایک سال میں لیں گے تو دو مرتبہ جزیہ لینا ہوگا۔ اس لئے ایک جزیہ ساقط ہوگا اور ایک جزیہ لازم ہوگا (۳) اس میں ذمی کے لئے سہولت ہے جس میں اسلام میں بڑا خیال رکھا گیا ہے۔

3075] (96) If two years' jizya accumulate upon him, then interposition occurs between them. If he could not pay jizya for two years, then one year's jizya will fall, and only one year's jizya will be obligatory.
Footnote: (a) Umar saw a very old dhimmi begging... (b) Khalid... (c) The Prophet said no jizya on a Muslim...
[Page 319]... The two years interpose the two jizyas. 
There is an athar from Tawus that he said: 'When sadaqat are concurrent, the first is not taken, like jizya.'... Another athar from Zuhri... This athar also shows that they did not take ushr twice in one year. And if they take two years' jizya in one year, then taking jizya twice would be required. Therefore one jizya falls and one jizya is obligatory. In this there is ease for the dhimmi, which Islam greatly takes care of.
They (Imam Shafi'i and Imam Abu Yusuf) say: Since two years have accumulated, two years' jizya will be taken. Otherwise the government would suffer loss, and the dhimmi would deliberately procrastinate to drop it.
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage deals with a situation where a dhimmi fails to pay jizya for two consecutive years. The Hanafi position (attributed to Abu Hanifa) is that only one year's jizya is due because of the principle of tadakhul (interposition): the two obligations merge into one. The commentary supports this with athar: Tawus analogized jizya to sadaqah (zakat), where if two years' zakah are missed, only one is taken. Similarly, the practice of early caliphs showed they did not collect ushr twice in one year. The Hanafi view emphasizes ease for the dhimmi. However, Imam Shafi'i and Imam Abu Yusuf (within the Hanafi school) hold that both years must be collected to prevent loss to the treasury and to avoid deliberate evasion. The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is the view of Abu Hanifa (tadakhul).

Key Terms
تداخل (tadakhul): Interposition: multiple obligations of the same type merge into one.
جزیہ (jizya): Annual poll tax on non-Muslims.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Only one year
C) Neither year
D) One and a half years

Key Takeaway
When jizya accumulates for two years, the Hanafi school applies tadakhul so only one year is due, prioritising ease for the dhimmi.

Prohibition of New Churches in Dar al-Islam
Ruling with proof from hadith and athar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on building new churches in Muslim-founded cities and explain the proofs from hadith and athar.

Core Idea
New churches and synagogues cannot be built in Muslim-founded cities to prevent the spread of other religions.

This passage addresses a key rule in Hanafi siyar: non-Muslim subjects (dhimmis) are not permitted to construct new places of worship in cities established by Muslims. The ruling preserves the Islamic character of the land. We will examine the proof texts and reasoning behind this prohibition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is being ruled upon? The act of building new churches/synagogues in Dar al-Islam. The ruling is haram (prohibited).
Hanafi law distinguishes between Muslim-founded cities and those conquered by treaty; the ruling here applies to the former.
2
Locate the dalil
Two proofs are cited: a hadith from Ibn Abbas ("Two qiblas cannot combine in one land") and an athar from Ibn Abbas explicitly prohibiting churches, naqus, and pork sales in Muslim-founded cities.
The hadith is from Tirmidhi (no. 633), the athar from Bayhaqi and Ibn Abi Shayba.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the prohibition? 'Two qiblas' is interpreted as two dominant religions or public manifestations of religion. Building a church is a public manifestation of another religion, thus prohibited.
The athar provides explicit support for the prohibition in Muslim-founded cities.
4
Note the scope and exceptions
The prohibition is absolute in Muslim-founded cities. In cities conquered by treaty, existing places may be allowed but new ones still cannot be built.
Some Shafi'i scholars allow new churches if stipulated in the treaty, but the Hanafi position is strict.
5
Evaluate the authority
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but is supported by the athar and the general principle of protecting Islamic dominance.
The Hanafi school relies on this as part of zahir al-riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۳۰۷۶] (۹۷) دارالاسلام میں یہودی اور نصرانی کا نیا عبادت خانہ بنانا جائز نہیں ہے۔ تش دارالاسلام کے شہروں میں یہودی کا اور نصرانی کا نیا عبادت خانہ نہ بنانے دیا جائے۔ اس سے اس کی شوکت بڑھے گی اور دوسرے دین کی اشاعت ہوگی ۔ اس لئے ان کا نیا عبادت خانہ بنانے کی اجازت نہیں ہوگی۔ حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال قال رسول الله الا الله لا تصلح قبلتان في ارض واحدة وليس على المسلمين جزية (ج) ترندی شریف، باب ما جاء لیس علی المسلمین جزیہ ، ص ، ۱۳۸، نمبر ۶۳۳، کتاب الزکوۃ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ذمیوں کو بہت زیادہ اس کے دین کی اشاعت کی اجازت نہیں ہوگی ۔ اور نیا کنیسہ یا بچہ بنانا دین کی اشاعت ہے اس لئے اس کی اجازت نہیں ہوگی (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال كل مصر مصره المسلمون لا يبنى فيه بيعة ولا كنيسة ولا يضرب فيه بناقوس ولا يباع فيه لحم خنزیر (و) (سن للبیہقی ، باب بیشتر علیهم ان لا حد ثوافی امصار المسلمین کنیتہ ولا مجمعالصلو انتم ولاصوت ناقوس ولا حمل خزر مرولا ادخال خنزیر، ج تاسع ص ۱۳۳۹، نمبر ۱۸۷۱۴ر مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ۷۰ ما قالوا فی حدم البيع والكنائز وبيوت النار، ج سادس ص ۴۷۱، نمبر ۳۲۹۷۲) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ جس شہر کو مسلمانوں نے بسایا ہے اس میں ذمیوں کا نیا عبادت خانہ نہ بنانے دیا جائے۔
3076] (97) In Dar al-Islam, building a new place of worship for Jews and Christians is not permissible. That is, in cities of Dar al-Islam, a new place of worship for Jews and Christians should not be allowed. This would increase their prestige and spread another religion. Therefore, permission to build new places of worship will not be given. There is a hadith: From Ibn Abbas, he said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Two qiblas cannot be combined in one land, and there is no jizya upon Muslims.' (c) (Tirmidhi, chapter on no jizya on Muslims, p. 138, no. 633, Kitab al-Zakat) From this hadith it is known that dhimmis will not be given much permission to spread their religion. And building a new church or temple is spreading religion, so it will not be permitted. (2) There is an athar: From Ibn Abbas, he said: Any city founded by Muslims, a church or synagogue should not be built in it, nor should the naqus be struck, nor should pork be sold. (w) (Sunan al-Bayhaqi... Musannaf ibn Abi Shayba...) From this athar it is known that in a city founded by Muslims, a new place of worship for dhimmis should not be allowed.
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that new churches and synagogues cannot be built in Muslim-founded cities within Dar al-Islam. The reasoning is that it would enhance the prestige of non-Muslim religions and lead to the spread of other religions. The proof is a hadith: 'Two qiblas cannot combine in one land' (interpreted as Islam and another religion cannot coexist with equal prominence). Also, an athar from Ibn Abbas explicitly prohibits building churches or synagogues in Muslim-founded cities, as well as striking the naqus (a wooden instrument used to call to worship) and selling pork. This ruling is part of the Hanafi law of siyar, governing the relationship between the Islamic state and its non-Muslim subjects.

Key Terms
بيعة (bay'a): Church (place of Christian worship).
كنيسة (kanisa): Synagogue or temple (place of Jewish or other worship).
دار الاسلام (Dar al-Islam): Territory under Islamic rule where Islamic law prevails.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, where can a new church be built?
A) In any city within Dar al-Islam
B) Only in cities that were originally founded by Muslims
C) Only in cities conquered by treaty that have not become Muslim-majority
D) Nowhere within Dar al-Islam

Key Takeaway
Building new churches and synagogues in Muslim-founded cities is prohibited by Hanafi law to prevent the dominance of other religions.

Rebuilding Old Churches and Synagogues of Dhimmis
Ruling on rebuilding non-Muslim places of worship after destruction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on rebuilding old non-Muslim places of worship and identify the proof from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
The dhimma contract protects existing places of worship; rebuilding after collapse is a continuation of that protection.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on the restoration of non-Muslim places of worship. The key question: when an old church or synagogue collapses, may the dhimmi community rebuild it? The source passage states plainly that they may, and supports this with the precedent of the Prophet's treaty with the Christians of Najran.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The act is rebuilding old churches and synagogues after they collapse. The ruling is mubah (permissible).
The text says 'اعادوها' (they may rebuild them).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a hadith from Ibn Abbas about the Prophet's peace treaty with the Christians of Najran. The treaty explicitly prohibits demolition of their churches.
Hadith from Sunan Abi Dawud and Bayhaqi.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The prohibition of demolition implies protection of existing structures. Rebuilding after collapse is an extension of that protection, not a new construction.
The hadith conditions protection as long as dhimmis do not commit offenses or consume usury.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Maliki school generally prohibits rebuilding, considering it a renewal of a prohibited act. The Hanafi school permits it based on the treaty's explicit protection.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi (operative) because it is based on a clear prophetic precedent and the principle of fulfilling the covenant.
The text presents it without internal dispute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا انهدمت البيع والكنائس القديمة اعادوها (۹۸) عن ابن عباس قال صالح رسول الله ﷺ اهل نجران على الفي حلة ... على ان لا تهدم لهم بيعة ولا يخرج لهم قس ولا يفتنوا عن دينهم مالم يحدثوا حدثا أو يأكلوا الربا (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی اخذ الجزية ، ص۷۴، نمبر ۳۰۴ سفن للمتقی ، باب لا تهدم هم کنیسه ولا بیعته ، ج تاسع، ص ۳۳۹، نمبر ۱۸۷۱۵)
And if the old churches and synagogues collapse, they may rebuild them (98). From Ibn Abbas: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ made peace with the people of Najran on (payment of) two thousand garments... on condition that no church of theirs be demolished, nor any priest expelled, nor they be tempted (to leave) their religion, as long as they do not commit an offense or consume usury.
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school concerning the maintenance of non-Muslim places of worship in the Islamic state. The text states that when old churches and synagogues fall into ruin, their dhimmi owners are permitted to rebuild them. The proof adduced is the Prophet's peace treaty with the Christians of Najran, recorded by Ibn Abbas, which explicitly stipulates that their churches shall not be demolished and their priests shall not be expelled. This indicates that the covenant of dhimma includes the right to maintain existing places of worship. The Hanafi position is that such buildings, if they predate the Islamic conquest, may be repaired and rebuilt if they collapse, as long as the dhimmis adhere to the terms of the covenant. This is in contrast to building new ones, which is generally prohibited. The hadith also conditions that this right remains as long as they do not introduce innovations or consume usury, meaning that gross violations of the covenant can forfeit this protection.

Key Terms
بيع (biya'): Places of worship of Jews and Christians
كنائس (kanai's): Churches of Christians

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on rebuilding old churches and synagogues that have collapsed?
A) They cannot be rebuilt at all.
B) They may be rebuilt as long as the dhimmis maintain their covenant.
C) Only the Muslims can rebuild them.
D) Rebuilding requires permission from the caliph only.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits dhimmis to rebuild their old places of worship based on the precedent of the Prophet's treaty with Najran.
